Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
12 min
The Fudhuli's Offer: Half or Complete Contract?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fudhuli's utterance in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the fudhuli's offer in marriage, distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad from Abu Yusuf, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving half contracts.

Core Idea
A fudhuli's single utterance is only half a contract – it becomes void if not accepted in the session.

The Hanafi school holds that a contract requires both offer and acceptance in the same session. But what if a person without authority (fudhuli) makes an offer on behalf of someone? Does that single utterance count as a full contract that can be accepted later? This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side, and Abu Yusuf on the other, and shows how this distinction affects the validity of the marriage.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed-upon rule
Recognize that half a contract (shutr al-ʻaqd) does not depend on absent acceptance. If one party offers and the other does not accept in the session, the offer becomes void – this is by consensus in sale, marriage, and other contracts.
The phrase 'ولا يتوقف شطر العقد على قبول ناكح غائب' establishes this baseline.
2
Identify the point of disagreement
The dispute concerns whether the fudhuli's single utterance (e.g., 'I married you to her') is a full contract or half. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is half; Abu Yusuf says it is a complete contract.
The text says: 'فعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد شطر فيبطل، وعند أبي يوسف عقد تام فيتوقف'.
3
Follow the proof of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
Their proof is an analogy with ordinary contracts: just as an offer in presence is half, so too in absence. Half does not suspend beyond the session. The speech of an authorized agent is transferred to the principals, but a fudhuli's speech remains his own.
They argue that what exists is only half the contract, and half cannot suspend.
4
Follow the proof of Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf analogizes to khul', divorce for compensation, and emancipation for payment – where one side's statement creates a binding obligation that suspends upon fulfillment. He argues that the fudhuli's speech should similarly create a suspended marriage.
Abu Yusuf's view: 'فصار كالخلع والطلاق والإعتاق على مال'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: If a fudhuli says 'I married you to her' and the parties accept later, according to Abu Hanifa/Muhammad the offer is void and no marriage is formed; according to Abu Yusuf, the marriage is suspended and becomes valid upon subsequent acceptance.
This affects whether a later consent can cure the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يتوقف شطر العقد على قبول ناكح غائب أي لا يتوقف الإيجاب على قبول كان غائباً عن المجلس بل يبطل ولا يلحقه ،إجازة وهذا بالاتفاق كما لو أوجب أحد المتعاقدين فلم يقبل الآخر في المجلس فإنه يبطل الإيجاب لا نعلم فيه خلافاً. ولا فرق في بين البيع والنكاح وغيرهما من العقود فقوله ناكح ليس بقيد احترازي. ثم اختلفوا في أن ما يقوم بالفضولي عقد تام فيصح أن يتولى الطرفين أو شطره فلا يتوقف؛ فعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد شطر فيبطل، وعند أبي يوسف عقد تام فيتوقف لأنه لو كان مأموراً من الجانبين ينفذ فإذا كان فضولياً يتوقف فصار كالخلع والطلاق والإعتاق على مال. ولهما أن الموجود شطر العقد لأنه شطر حالة الحضرة فكذا عند الغيبة وشطر العقد لا يتوقف على ما وراء المجلس كما في البيع بخلاف المأمور من الجانبين لأنه ينتقل كلامه إلى العاقدين، وما يجري بين الفضوليين عقد تام فكذا الخلع واختاره لأنه يمين من جانبه حتى يلزم فيتم به فتفرع على هذا الأصل ست صور: ثلاث اتفاقية وهي قول الرجل تزوجت فلانة، أو المرأة تزوجت فلاناً، أو الفضولي زوجت فلاناً من فلانة، وقيل آخر في الثلاث فالعقد متوقف لحصول الشطرين. وثلاثة خلافية هي هذه إذا لم يقبل أحد فلا تقوم عبارة الفضولي مقام عبارتين، سواء تكلم بكلام واحد أو بكلامين حتى لو قال زوجت فلاناً وقبلت عنه لم يتوقف على قولهما وهو الحق خلافاً لما ذكر في الحواشي لاتفاق أهل المذهب في نقل قولهما على أن الفضولي الواحد لا يتولى الطرفين وهو مطلق، ولو عبر به المصنف لكان أولى وحاصل متولي الطرفين بالقسمة العقلية عشرة : واحد منها مستحيل وهو الأصيل من الجانبين وأربعة هي من منطوق المتن على الخلاف : الفضولي من الجانبين والفضولي من جانب الوكيل من جانب، والفضولي من جانب الأصيل من جانب، والفضولي من جانب الولي من جانب، فعندهما لا يتوقف كما قدمناه. والخمسة الباقية مستفادة من مفهوم المتن وهي نافذة بالاتفاق : الوكيل من الجانبين، والولي من الجانبين والأصيل من جانب الولي من جانب والوكيل من جانب الأصيل من
His saying: 'And half of the contract does not depend on the acceptance of an absent marrying party' means that the offer does not depend on an acceptance that was absent from the session, rather it becomes void and no consent can join it. This is by agreement, just as if one of the two contractors made an offer and the other did not accept in the session, then the offer becomes void – we know of no disagreement in this. And there is no difference between sale, marriage, and other contracts, so his word 'marrying party' is not a restrictive qualifier. Then they differed concerning that which issues from the fudhuli: is it a complete contract such that he may undertake both sides, or is it half so that it does not depend? According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is half, so it becomes void. According to Abu Yusuf, it is a complete contract, so it becomes suspended, because if he had been commanded from both sides, it would be effective; when he is a fudhuli, it becomes suspended, analogous to khul', divorce, and emancipation for consideration. And for them (Abu Hanifa/Muhammad), the existing thing is half of the contract because it is half in the state of presence, and likewise in the state of absence. And half of the contract does not depend on what is beyond the session, as in sale, unlike the one commanded from both sides because his speech is transferred to the two contractors. And what takes place between two fudhulis is a complete contract, and likewise khul', and he chose it because it is an oath from his side until it becomes binding, so it is completed by it. Derived from this principle are six cases: three agreed-upon cases: the man's saying 'I have married so-and-so', or the woman's saying 'I have married so-and-so', or the fudhuli's saying 'I have married so-and-so to so-and-so', and another version in these three, then the contract is suspended because both halves have occurred. And three disputed cases are these: if no one accepts, then the statement of the fudhuli does not suffice for two statements, whether he speaks with one statement or two statements – even if he said 'I married so-and-so and I accept on his behalf', it does not depend on his statement, and this is the correct view contrary to what is mentioned in the commentaries, due to the agreement of the scholars of the school in transmitting their statement that a single fudhuli does not undertake both sides, and it is absolute. And if the author had expressed it, it would have been better. The summary of the one who undertakes both sides by rational division is ten: one is impossible: the principal from both sides; four are from the explicit text of the matn, subject to disagreement: a fudhuli from both sides, a fudhuli from one side and an agent from one side, a fudhuli from one side and a principal from one side, a fudhuli from one side and a guardian from one side – according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it does not suspend as we mentioned. The remaining five are derived from the implication of the matn and are effective by agreement: an agent from both sides, a guardian from both sides, a principal from one side and a guardian from one side, an agent from one side and a principal from one side.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This commentary explains the matn line 'ولا يتوقف شطر العقد على قبول ناكح غائب'. The author clarifies that half a contract does not depend on the acceptance of an absent party; the offer becomes void. Then it presents the core dispute: when a fudhuli makes an offer (e.g., 'I married you to so-and-so'), is that considered half a contract (shutr) or a complete contract? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it is half, so it does not suspend and becomes void if not accepted in the session. Abu Yusuf says it is a complete contract, so it suspends and can be later accepted. The passage provides the reasoning: Abu Yusuf compares it to khul' and divorce for compensation, which are complete from one side. The majority rely on the fact that only half the contract is present, and half cannot suspend. The passage then enumerates six cases: three agreed-upon (where the contract does suspend because both halves are present) and three disputed (where the fudhuli alone speaks). It also outlines ten categories of one who undertakes both sides, some of which are effective by agreement and some subject to dispute.

Key Terms
شطر العقد (shutr al-ʻaqd): Half of the contract; i.e., only the offer or only the acceptance, not both.
فصد (fudhuli): A person who acts as a party to a contract without authorization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the status of a fudhuli's statement 'I married you to so-and-so' when no acceptance is made in the session?
A) It is a suspended contract waiting for acceptance.
B) It is half a contract and becomes void.
C) It is valid as an oath.
D) It is considered a full contract.

Key Takeaway
The fudhuli's offer in marriage is only half a contract; it does not suspend and becomes void if not accepted in the same session.

One Person Acting as Both Wali and Groom in Marriage
Ruling that a single utterance suffices when one person acts as both parties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a single utterance sufficing when one person acts as both parties in a marriage contract, and distinguish the majority view from the condition set by Khwahrazadah.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, a single utterance suffices when one person represents both sides in a marriage contract.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key procedural point in the marriage contract. Normally, separate offer and acceptance are required, but when the same person acts as both wali and groom (or wali from both sides), a single comprehensive utterance covers both. However, there is an intra-madhhab difference regarding the capacity in which the person speaks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the situation where the same person acts as both parties in a marriage contract (e.g., a wali marrying himself, or a judge marrying two minors).
2
Understand the default requirement
Know that normally a marriage needs two separate utterances: offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul).
3
Apply the exception
State that in this scenario, one utterance suffices because it implies both sides.
4
Examine the disagreement
Note the condition suggested by Khwahrazadah (that the wording must be in the capacity of a principal) and how the majority rejects it.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that no condition applies; any single comprehensive utterance suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والولي من جانب الوكيل من جانب. ثم إذا تولى الطرفين في هذه المسائل الخمس فقوله زوجت فلانة من نفسي يتضمن الشطرين فلا يحتاج إلى القبول بعده، وكذا ولي الصغيرين القاضي وغيره، والوكيل من الجانبين يقول زوجت فلانة من فلان وقال شيخ الإسلام خواهر زاده : وهذا إذا ذكر لفظاً هو أصيل فيه، أما إذا ذكر لفظاً هو نائب فيه فلا يكفي، فإن قال تزوجت فلانة كفى، وإن قال زوجتها من نفسي لا يكفي لأنه نائب فيه . وعبارة الهداية صريحة في نفي هذا الاشتراط وصرح بنفيه في التجنيس أيضاً في علامة غريب الرواية والفتاوى الصغرى قال : رجل زوج بنت أخيه من ابن أخيه فقال زوجت فلانة . من فلان يكفي ولا يحتاج أن يقول قبلت، وكذا كل من يتولى طرفي العقد إذا أتى بأحد شطري الإيجاب يكفيه ولا يحتاج إلى الشطر الآخر لأن اللفظ الواحد يقع دليلاً من الجانبين. كذا في فتح القيدر.
The guardian is from one side and the agent from the other. Then, if one person undertakes both sides in these five issues, his saying 'I married so-and-so to myself' encompasses both parts, so he does not need acceptance after that. Likewise, the guardian of two minors—the judge and others—and the agent from both sides says, 'I married so-and-so to so-and-so.' And Shaykh al-Islam Khwahrazadah said: This is if he mentions a wording in which he is a principal; but if he mentions a wording in which he is a deputy, it does not suffice. If he says 'I married so-and-so' it suffices; if he says 'I married her to myself' it does not suffice because he is a deputy in it. And the expression of Al-Hidayah is explicit in negating this condition, and he explicitly negated it in Al-Tajnīs as well, in the sign of Ghareeb al-Riwayah and al-Fatawa al-Sughra: A man married his brother's daughter to his brother's son and said, 'I married so-and-so to so-and-so'—it suffices, and he does not need to say 'I accept.' Likewise, anyone who undertakes both sides of a contract, if he brings one of the two parts of the offer, it suffices him and he does not need the other part, because one single word serves as proof from both sides. Thus in Fath al-Qadeer.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of a ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The ruling is about a person who acts as both the guardian (wali) and the groom (or agent on the groom's side) in a marriage contract. Normally, a marriage contract requires two separate utterances: offer (ijab) from the guardian and acceptance (qabul) from the groom. However, if the same person performs both roles, a single utterance suffices because it covers both sides. For example, if a man is the guardian of a woman and also the groom, his saying 'I married so-and-so to myself' constitutes both offer and acceptance. Similarly, if a judge acts as guardian for two minors and marries them to each other, his utterance is sufficient. There is a disagreement from Khwahrazadah who distinguishes based on whether the wording is principal (asil) or deputy (na'ib). According to him, if the person is acting as a deputy (e.g., an agent), saying 'I married her to myself' is insufficient because he is not the principal in that role. However, the text from al-Hidayah and other works rejects this condition, stating that regardless of the capacity, a single comprehensive utterance suffices. The key principle is that the same word functions as proof from both sides. Students should note that this ruling is specific to marriage contracts and not generalizable to other contracts like sale, where conditions differ.

Key Terms
الولي (al-wali): The guardian who has authority to give a woman in marriage; in this context, the person who performs the offer (ijab).
الوكيل (al-wakil): The agent who acts on behalf of the groom, usually to make the acceptance (qabul).
أصيل (asil): Principal; the person who has original authority in the action, as opposed to a deputy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a man acts as both guardian and groom in a marriage contract, what is required for validity?
A) He must say both 'I marry her to myself' and then separately 'I accept'.
B) He must say 'I marry her to myself' only once, which suffices for both offer and acceptance.
C) He must say 'I accept' first, then 'I marry her to myself'.
D) The marriage is invalid because one person cannot act as both parties.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when one person acts as both parties in a marriage contract, a single comprehensive utterance suffices; the condition of being a principal is not required.

Nikah — Marriage

Proxy Marrying Two Women: Mukhalafa and Fuduli Contracts
Ruling on agent's non-conformity in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an agent marries two women instead of one and explain the role of ratification.

Core Idea
An agent who marries two women instead of one creates a suspended contract; only the principal's ratification makes it valid.

When you instruct someone to marry you a woman and he marries you two, he has acted contrary to your mandate. The Hanafi school treats this as a fuduli (unauthorized) contract, suspended upon your approval. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mandate
The principal ordered the agent to marry him one unspecified woman. The agent’s action of marrying two women violates this mandate.
If the mandate is specific (e.g., a named woman), see lesson on specification.
2
Recognize the mukhalafa
The agent’s act is mukhalafa (non-conformity). Because the agent acted without authority, both marriages are not binding immediately.
Mukhalafa triggers the fuduli status.
3
Understand the fuduli status
A fuduli contract is valid only upon ratification by the principal. Neither marriage is effective until the principal approves.
Ratification can be for one or both.
4
Apply the rule of ratification
If the principal ratifies one or both marriages, they become valid retroactively. If not, the contract is void.
The principal may ratify intentionally or by conduct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والمأمور بنكاح امرأة مخالف بامرأتين لأنه لا وجه إلى تنفيذهما للمخالفة ولا إلى التنفيذ في أحدهما غير عين للجهالة ولا إلى التعيين لعدم الأولوية فتعين التفريق عند عدم الإجازة وهو مراد صاحب الهداية بدليل أنه قال في صدر المسألة : لم تلزمه واحدة منهما . فكان كلامه مستقيماً فاندفع به ما ذكره الشارح من عدم استقامته، ولذا عبر المصنف بالمخالفة ليفيد عدم النفاذ وأنه عقد فضولي فإن أجاز نكاحهما أو إحداهما نفذ فيه بالأمر بواحدة لأنه لو أمره يزوجه امرأتين في عقدة فزوجه واحدة جاز إلا أذا قال لا تزوجني إلا امرأتين في عقدة واحدة فحينئذ لا يجوز. كذا في غاية البيان ومثله ما في المحيط : لو أمره أن يزوجه امرأتين في عقدة فزوجهما في عقدتين جاز، ولو قال لا تزوجني امرأتين إلا في عقدتين فزوجهما في عقدة لا يجوز، والفرق أن في الأول أثبت الوكالة حالة الجمع ولم ينف الوكالة حال التفرد نصاً بل سكت عنه والتنصيص على الجمع لا يدل على نفي ما عداه، وفي العقد الثاني نفي الوكالة حالة التفرد والنفي مفيد لأن فائدته في الجمع أكثر لما فيه من تعجيل مقصوده فلا بد من مراعاة النفي فلم يصر وكيلاً حالة الانفراد اهـ. وهذا بخلاف البيع لو أمره أن يشتري ثوبين في صفقة لا يملك التفريق لأن الثياب إذا اشتريت جملة تؤخذ بأرخص مما تشترى على التفاريق فاعتبر قوله فيه فأما ههنا بخلافه كذا في النهاية. وفي الخانية : لو وكله أن يزوجه فلانة أو فلانة فأيتهما زوجه جاز ولا يبطل التوكيل بهذه الجهالة، وإنه زوجهما جميعاً في عقدة واحدة لم يجز واحدة منهما كما لو وكل رجلاً أن يزوجه امرأة فزوجه امرأتين في عقدة واحدة لم يجز اهـ. وقيد بكون المرأة منكرة أخذاً من التنكير لأنه لو عينها فزوجها وأخرى معها تلزمه المعينة. وقيد في الهداية نكاح المرأتين بأن يكون في عقد واحد لأنه لو زوجهما في عقدتين تلزمه الأولى ونكاح الثانية موقوف على الإجازة لأنه فضولي فيه، ولذا قال في المختصر «بامرأتين) ولم يقل بعقدين»، وفرعوا على أن التنصيص على الشيء لا ينفي الحكم عما عداه لو قال زوج ابنتي هذه رجلاً يرجع إلى علم ودين بمشورة فلان فزوجها رجلاً على هذه الصفة من غير مشورة فإنه يجوز كما في الخانية، وأما إذا قال له عبدي هذا بشهود أو بمحضر فلان فباعه بغير شهود أو بغير محضر فلان فإنه يجوز بخلاف ما إذا قال لا تبعه إلا بشهود فباعه بغير شهود فإنه لا يجوز كما في الظهيرية
His saying: (And the one ordered to marry a woman who acts contrary by marrying two women) because there is no way to execute both due to the non-conformity, nor to execute one of them without specification due to ambiguity, nor to specify due to lack of priority. So dissolution is determined in the absence of ratification. This is what is meant by the author of Al-Hidayah, as evidenced by his statement at the beginning of the issue: 'Neither of them is binding upon him.' So his speech is consistent, and thereby is repelled what the commentator mentioned about its inconsistency. Hence the author expressed it as 'contrary' to indicate non-enforcement and that it is a contract of a fuduli (unauthorized agent). If he ratifies both or one of them, it is enforced with the order for one, because if he ordered him to marry two women in one contract and he married one, it is valid, unless he said, 'Do not marry me except two women in one contract,' then it is not valid. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. Similarly, what is in Al-Muhit: If he ordered him to marry two women in one contract and he married them in two contracts, it is valid. If he said, 'Do not marry me two women except in two contracts,' and he married them in one contract, it is not valid. The difference is that in the first, he established agency in the state of combination and did not explicitly negate agency in the state of singularity, but remained silent about it, and specification of combination does not indicate negation of what is other than it. In the second contract, negation of agency in the state of singularity is beneficial because its benefit in combination is greater due to the hastening of his purpose, so the negation must be observed, and he did not become an agent in the state of singularity. This is contrary to sale: if he ordered him to buy two garments in one transaction, he does not have the right to separate them, because if garments are bought in bulk, they are taken cheaper than if bought separately, so his statement is considered in it. But here it is otherwise. Thus in Al-Nihayah. And in Al-Khaniyyah: If he authorized him to marry him so-and-so or so-and-so, whichever he marries is valid, and the authorization is not invalidated by this ambiguity. But if he marries both in one contract, neither is valid, just as if he authorized a man to marry him a woman and he married him two women in one contract, it is not valid. And it is conditioned that the woman is indefinite, taken from the indefinite article, because if he specified her and he married her together with another, the specified one is binding. And in Al-Hidayah it is conditioned that the marriage of two women is in one contract, because if he married them in two contracts, the first is binding and the second marriage is suspended pending ratification, because he is a fuduli in it. Hence the author said in Al-Mukhtasar 'by two women' and did not say 'by two contracts.' And they branched out that specification of a thing does not negate the ruling regarding what is other than it. If he said, 'Marry my daughter to a man who refers to knowledge and religion, with the consultation of so-and-so,' and he married her to a man with this description without consultation, it is valid, as in Al-Khaniyyah. But if he said to him, 'Sell my slave in the presence of witnesses or in the presence of so-and-so,' and he sold him without witnesses or without the presence of so-and-so, it is valid, contrary to if he said, 'Do not sell him except with witnesses,' and he sold him without witnesses, then it is not valid, as in Al-Dhuhayriyyah.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a principal orders his agent to marry him a woman (without specifying which woman), and the agent instead marries him two women in a single contract. The ruling is that this is a case of 'mukhalafa' (non-conformity) meaning the agent violated his mandate. As a result, neither marriage is effective unless the principal ratifies. The reasoning is: both marriages cannot be executed because they violate the mandate; selecting one without specification is impossible due to ambiguity (jahala); and the agent has no priority to choose one. Therefore, the contract is treated as a fuduli contract (unauthorized) pending ratification. If the principal ratifies both or one, it becomes effective as if he had ordered only one. This is the meaning intended by the author of Al-Hidayah. The text then distinguishes between cases where the agent's mandate is explicit: if ordered to marry two women in one contract, marrying one is valid (since combination does not negate singularity unless explicitly negated). If ordered 'do not marry me except two women in one contract,' then marrying one is invalid. Similarly, if told to marry two women in one contract, marrying them separately is valid; but if told 'do not marry me two women except in two contracts,' then marrying them together is invalid. This differs from sale, where if told to buy two garments in one transaction, he cannot buy them separately because bulk purchase is cheaper. The key principle: 'Specification of a thing does not negate the ruling regarding what is other than it' unless the principal explicitly negates the other possibility.

Key Terms
مخالف (mukhalif): An agent who acts contrary to the mandate given by the principal.
فضولي (fuduli): An unauthorized agent; a person who acts without prior authorization. The contract is suspended upon ratification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an agent is ordered to marry a woman (unspecified) and instead marries two women in one contract, what is the status of the marriages?
A) Both marriages are valid and binding immediately.
B) Only one marriage is valid at the agent's choice.
C) Both marriages are invalid unless the principal ratifies one or both.
D) The agent must divorce one woman immediately.

Key Takeaway
An agent who exceeds the mandate creates a suspended contract; ratification by the principal is essential for validity.

Specification Does Not Negate: The Hanafi Principle of Agency
Expansion of the principle that specification does not negate the opposite

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'specification of a thing does not negate the ruling regarding what is other than it' to various agency scenarios.

Core Idea
Specifying a condition does not negate the opposite unless the negation is explicit.

When a principal gives a detailed mandate, does specifying one condition automatically exclude others? The Hanafi school answers no, as long as the principal has not explicitly prohibited the alternative. This lesson explores that principle through examples in marriage and sale.

Guided Path
1
State the principle
The text says: 'Specification of a thing does not negate the ruling regarding what is other than it.' Understand this maxim.
This is a general principle in Hanafi muamalat.
2
Apply to marriage cases
If told to marry two women in one contract, marrying one is valid because the mandate for combination did not explicitly negate singularity.
Likewise, if told to marry two in one contract, marrying in two contracts is valid.
3
Apply to explicit negation
If the principal says 'do not marry me except two women in one contract,' then marrying one is invalid. Explicit negation overrides the principle.
The negation is effective because it prevents the agent from acting in the negated manner.
4
Compare with sale
In sale, if told to buy two garments in one transaction, the agent cannot buy them separately because the economic benefit of bulk purchase is assumed to be intended. This is an exception.
The difference is due to the nature of the transaction (price advantage).
5
Apply to consultation and witness conditions
If told to marry with consultation of X, marrying without consultation is valid unless explicitly prohibited. Similarly for selling with witnesses.
The principle holds unless the principal specifically negates the alternative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والمأمور بنكاح امرأة مخالف بامرأتين لأنه لا وجه إلى تنفيذهما للمخالفة ولا إلى التنفيذ في أحدهما غير عين للجهالة ولا إلى التعيين لعدم الأولوية فتعين التفريق عند عدم الإجازة وهو مراد صاحب الهداية بدليل أنه قال في صدر المسألة : لم تلزمه واحدة منهما . فكان كلامه مستقيماً فاندفع به ما ذكره الشارح من عدم استقامته، ولذا عبر المصنف بالمخالفة ليفيد عدم النفاذ وأنه عقد فضولي فإن أجاز نكاحهما أو إحداهما نفذ فيه بالأمر بواحدة لأنه لو أمره يزوجه امرأتين في عقدة فزوجه واحدة جاز إلا أذا قال لا تزوجني إلا امرأتين في عقدة واحدة فحينئذ لا يجوز. كذا في غاية البيان ومثله ما في المحيط : لو أمره أن يزوجه امرأتين في عقدة فزوجهما في عقدتين جاز، ولو قال لا تزوجني امرأتين إلا في عقدتين فزوجهما في عقدة لا يجوز، والفرق أن في الأول أثبت الوكالة حالة الجمع ولم ينف الوكالة حال التفرد نصاً بل سكت عنه والتنصيص على الجمع لا يدل على نفي ما عداه، وفي العقد الثاني نفي الوكالة حالة التفرد والنفي مفيد لأن فائدته في الجمع أكثر لما فيه من تعجيل مقصوده فلا بد من مراعاة النفي فلم يصر وكيلاً حالة الانفراد اهـ. وهذا بخلاف البيع لو أمره أن يشتري ثوبين في صفقة لا يملك التفريق لأن الثياب إذا اشتريت جملة تؤخذ بأرخص مما تشترى على التفاريق فاعتبر قوله فيه فأما ههنا بخلافه كذا في النهاية. وفي الخانية : لو وكله أن يزوجه فلانة أو فلانة فأيتهما زوجه جاز ولا يبطل التوكيل بهذه الجهالة، وإنه زوجهما جميعاً في عقدة واحدة لم يجز واحدة منهما كما لو وكل رجلاً أن يزوجه امرأة فزوجه امرأتين في عقدة واحدة لم يجز اهـ. وقيد بكون المرأة منكرة أخذاً من التنكير لأنه لو عينها فزوجها وأخرى معها تلزمه المعينة. وقيد في الهداية نكاح المرأتين بأن يكون في عقد واحد لأنه لو زوجهما في عقدتين تلزمه الأولى ونكاح الثانية موقوف على الإجازة لأنه فضولي فيه، ولذا قال في المختصر «بامرأتين) ولم يقل بعقدين»، وفرعوا على أن التنصيص على الشيء لا ينفي الحكم عما عداه لو قال زوج ابنتي هذه رجلاً يرجع إلى علم ودين بمشورة فلان فزوجها رجلاً على هذه الصفة من غير مشورة فإنه يجوز كما في الخانية، وأما إذا قال له عبدي هذا بشهود أو بمحضر فلان فباعه بغير شهود أو بغير محضر فلان فإنه يجوز بخلاف ما إذا قال لا تبعه إلا بشهود فباعه بغير شهود فإنه لا يجوز كما في الظهيرية
His saying: (And the one ordered to marry a woman who acts contrary by marrying two women) because there is no way to execute both due to the non-conformity, nor to execute one of them without specification due to ambiguity, nor to specify due to lack of priority. So dissolution is determined in the absence of ratification. This is what is meant by the author of Al-Hidayah, as evidenced by his statement at the beginning of the issue: 'Neither of them is binding upon him.' So his speech is consistent, and thereby is repelled what the commentator mentioned about its inconsistency. Hence the author expressed it as 'contrary' to indicate non-enforcement and that it is a contract of a fuduli (unauthorized agent). If he ratifies both or one of them, it is enforced with the order for one, because if he ordered him to marry two women in one contract and he married one, it is valid, unless he said, 'Do not marry me except two women in one contract,' then it is not valid. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. Similarly, what is in Al-Muhit: If he ordered him to marry two women in one contract and he married them in two contracts, it is valid. If he said, 'Do not marry me two women except in two contracts,' and he married them in one contract, it is not valid. The difference is that in the first, he established agency in the state of combination and did not explicitly negate agency in the state of singularity, but remained silent about it, and specification of combination does not indicate negation of what is other than it. In the second contract, negation of agency in the state of singularity is beneficial because its benefit in combination is greater due to the hastening of his purpose, so the negation must be observed, and he did not become an agent in the state of singularity. This is contrary to sale: if he ordered him to buy two garments in one transaction, he does not have the right to separate them, because if garments are bought in bulk, they are taken cheaper than if bought separately, so his statement is considered in it. But here it is otherwise. Thus in Al-Nihayah. And in Al-Khaniyyah: If he authorized him to marry him so-and-so or so-and-so, whichever he marries is valid, and the authorization is not invalidated by this ambiguity. But if he marries both in one contract, neither is valid, just as if he authorized a man to marry him a woman and he married him two women in one contract, it is not valid. And it is conditioned that the woman is indefinite, taken from the indefinite article, because if he specified her and he married her together with another, the specified one is binding. And in Al-Hidayah it is conditioned that the marriage of two women is in one contract, because if he married them in two contracts, the first is binding and the second marriage is suspended pending ratification, because he is a fuduli in it. Hence the author said in Al-Mukhtasar 'by two women' and did not say 'by two contracts.' And they branched out that specification of a thing does not negate the ruling regarding what is other than it. If he said, 'Marry my daughter to a man who refers to knowledge and religion, with the consultation of so-and-so,' and he married her to a man with this description without consultation, it is valid, as in Al-Khaniyyah. But if he said to him, 'Sell my slave in the presence of witnesses or in the presence of so-and-so,' and he sold him without witnesses or without the presence of so-and-so, it is valid, contrary to if he said, 'Do not sell him except with witnesses,' and he sold him without witnesses, then it is not valid, as in Al-Dhuhayriyyah.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage deals with a scenario where a principal orders his agent to marry him a woman (without specifying which woman), and the agent instead marries him two women in a single contract. The ruling is that this is a case of 'mukhalafa' (non-conformity) meaning the agent violated his mandate. As a result, neither marriage is effective unless the principal ratifies. The reasoning is: both marriages cannot be executed because they violate the mandate; selecting one without specification is impossible due to ambiguity (jahala); and the agent has no priority to choose one. Therefore, the contract is treated as a fuduli contract (unauthorized) pending ratification. If the principal ratifies both or one, it becomes effective as if he had ordered only one. This is the meaning intended by the author of Al-Hidayah. The text then distinguishes between cases where the agent's mandate is explicit: if ordered to marry two women in one contract, marrying one is valid (since combination does not negate singularity unless explicitly negated). If ordered 'do not marry me except two women in one contract,' then marrying one is invalid. Similarly, if told to marry two women in one contract, marrying them separately is valid; but if told 'do not marry me two women except in two contracts,' then marrying them together is invalid. This differs from sale, where if told to buy two garments in one transaction, he cannot buy them separately because bulk purchase is cheaper. The key principle: 'Specification of a thing does not negate the ruling regarding what is other than it' unless the principal explicitly negates the other possibility.

Key Terms
التنصيص (al-tansis): Specification; the act of explicitly stating a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a principal says to his agent 'Marry my son to a girl from a good family, and consult her father,' but the agent marries the son to a girl from a good family without consulting her father, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is invalid because consultation was required.
B) The marriage is valid because the agent fulfilled the main condition.
C) The marriage is valid only if the father later agrees.
D) The marriage is suspended pending the father's consultation.

Key Takeaway
Unless explicitly negated, specifying a condition does not exclude the alternative; the agent may validly act without that condition.

Proxy Marrying an Enslaved Woman: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on proxy marrying an enslaved woman when ordered to marry a free woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over a proxy marrying an enslaved woman and identify the preferred view for fatwa along with its reasoning.

Core Idea
When a proxy marries an enslaved woman, Abu Hanifa says it's valid; the Sahibayn require a suitable match, and their view is preferred for fatwa.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute from Al-Hidayah about the scope of a proxy's authority. The question: if a principal tells a proxy 'marry me a woman', and the proxy marries an enslaved woman, is that valid? Abu Hanifa and his two disciples differ based on the role of custom (urf) and juristic preference (istihsan). Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to analyze how literal wording, custom, and legal principles interact in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Abu Hanifa holds that the proxy did not act contrary to the mandate; the marriage is valid and binding upon the principal because the wording 'a woman' literally includes both free and enslaved women, and there is no evidence of bad faith.
This is a strict literalist approach: the absolute wording governs.
2
Identify the opponent's view (Sahibayn)
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the proxy acted contrary to the mandate; the marriage is not valid unless the principal ratifies it. They argue that the absolute term 'woman' is customarily understood to mean a free woman, and the proxy must ensure suitability (kuf').
The Sahibayn rely on custom (urf) and the principle of istihsan.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Sahibayn base their view on two points: (1) the absolute term is diverted to the customary meaning (free woman), and (2) considering suitability is istihsan because everyone can marry 'a woman', but the proxy's assistance is needed specifically for a suitable match.
Istihsan here departs from the literal qiyas (analogy) in favor of practical custom.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa's followers respond that the custom is not exclusive (i.e., the term 'woman' is shared between free and enslaved) or that it is merely a practical custom, not a legal restrictor. They also argue that Abu Hanifa's view is not qiyas but following the literal text, so the comparison to istihsan is misplaced.
Fath al-Qadeer argues Abu Hanifa's view is not qiyas because he took the literal wording.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the marriage is immediately binding; under the Sahibayn, it is suspended pending ratification. The text indicates that the Sahibayn's view is preferred for fatwa (al-Asbijabi, Abu al-Layth) because istihsan is generally given precedence over qiyas, and this case is not an exception.
However, Fath al-Qadeer notes that Abu Hanifa's literalist position has merit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا بأمة) أي لا يكون المأمور بنكاح امرأة مخالفاً بنكاح أمة لغيره فينفذ على الموكل عند أبي حنيفة رجوعاً إلى إطلاق اللفظ وعدم التهمة. وقالا : لا يجوز أن يزوجه كفئاً لأن المطلق ينصرف إلى المتعارف وهو التزوج بالإكفاء. قلنا : العرف مشترك أو هو عرف عملي فلا يصح مقيداً، وذكر في الوكالة أن اعتبار الكفاءة في هذا استحسان عندهما لأن كل واحد لا يعجز عن التزوج بمطلق الزوجة فكانت الاستعانة في التزوج بالكفء . كذا في الهداية وظاهره ترجيح قولهما لأن الاستحسان مقدم على القياس إلا في مسائل معدودة ليس هذا منها، ولذا قال الأسبيجابي : قولهما أحسن للفتوى واختاره أبو الليث وفي فتح القدير والحق أن قول أبي حنيفة ليس قياساً لأنه أخذ بنفس اللفظ المنصوص فكان النظر في أي الاستحسان من أولى اهـ.
His saying: (not with an enslaved woman) i.e., the one ordered to marry a woman is not acting contrary by marrying an enslaved woman belonging to someone else, so it is binding upon the principal according to Abu Hanifa, reverting to the absoluteness of the wording and the absence of suspicion. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not permissible for him to marry him a suitable match, because the absolute is diverted to the customary, which is marriage to a suitable match. We replied: The custom is shared (not exclusive) or it is a practical custom, so it is not valid as a restrictor. And it is mentioned in Al-Wakala that considering suitability in this is istihsan according to them, because each person is not incapable of marrying an absolute wife, so the assistance in marriage is with the suitable. Thus in Al-Hidayah, and apparently it is a preference of their view because istihsan is given precedence over qiyas, except in a few issues, and this is not among them. Hence al-Asbijabi said: Their view is better for fatwa, and Abu al-Layth chose it. And in Fath al-Qadeer: The truth is that the statement of Abu Hanifa is not qiyas because he took the literal wording, so the consideration is which istihsan is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a proxy who is ordered to marry a woman (free, unspecified) but instead marries an enslaved woman (ama). Abu Hanifa rules that this is not a case of non-conformity (mukhalafa); the marriage is effective and binding upon the principal. His reasoning is based on the absolute wording of the mandate: the principal said 'a woman' which literally includes both free and enslaved. Since there is no evidence of bad faith, the agent's act is valid. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. They hold that the agent must marry a suitable match (kuf') for the principal, because the absolute term is understood to refer to what is customary, and the custom is to marry free women. According to them, it is istihsan to consider suitability, as everyone is capable of marrying a woman, but the assistance of an agent is sought specifically for a suitable match. The text from Al-Hidayah appears to favor the view of the Sahibayn, stating that istihsan is generally preferred over qiyas (and Abu Hanifa's view is considered qiyas here). However, Fath al-Qadeer argues that Abu Hanifa's view is not qiyas; it follows the literal text. The author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq does not explicitly favor one side, but notes that al-Asbijabi and Abu al-Layth chose the view of the Sahibayn for fatwa. The dispute hinges on whether the absolute wording of the mandate can be restricted by common custom (urf) and whether istihsan should override the literal application. Students should understand that this is a nuanced debate within the Hanafi school about the role of custom and istihsan in agency contracts.

Key Terms
أمة (ama): An enslaved woman; a female slave.
كفء (kuf'): Suitable or compatible match, usually considered in terms of lineage, religion, and status.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of departing from apparent analogy in favor of a more suitable ruling based on custom or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view for fatwa mentioned in this passage, if a proxy ordered to marry 'a woman' marries an enslaved woman, what is the ruling?
A) The marriage is valid and binding immediately.
B) The marriage is invalid unless the principal ratifies it.
C) The proxy must marry a free woman instead.
D) The marriage is valid but the principal can divorce her.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi muamalat, when a proxy acts beyond the customary meaning of the mandate, the school weighs literal wording against custom and istihsan, with the Sahibayn's view often preferred for fatwa.

The Agent's Authority: Absolute Wording vs. Customary Practice in Marriage Agency
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agency and suitability in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on an agent marrying a slave woman under an unqualified command and explain the usul difference between absolute wording and customary restriction.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds the agent's marriage to a slave woman valid; the Sahibayn hold it invalid because custom restricts the absolute command to a free suitable match.

When a principal authorizes an agent to marry him a woman without specifying free or slave, does the agent have the authority to marry a slave woman belonging to another? The Hanafi school is divided. Abu Hanifa adheres to the literal wording, while his two disciples argue that customary practice restricts the absolute command. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind each view and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal's command and the agent's action
The principal says 'marry me a woman' (absolute). The agent marries a slave woman owned by another.
The command is unqualified; the agent deviates from what is usually expected.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Valid because the word 'woman' includes slave women, and there is no suspicion (the woman belongs to another). He relies on the explicit wording (itlaq al-lafz).
Abu Hanifa prioritizes the literal text over presumed custom.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Invalid because the absolute command is understood according to custom (urf), which is to marry a free suitable woman. They invoke istihsan.
For the Sahibayn, the agent's role is to secure a suitable match, so violation invalidates the act.
4
Analyze the dispute in terms of usul
The key is whether custom (urf) can restrict an absolute expression. Abu Hanifa says only verbal custom restricts; practical custom does not. The Sahibayn say the practical custom here indicates the agent's purpose is to find a suitable match, so violating that invalidates the agency.
The dispute reflects a deeper usul principle about the binding force of 'urf amali.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح/ فصل في الكفاءة

وكله أن يزوجه فلانة أو فلانة فأيتهما زوجه جاز ولا يبطل التوكيل بهذه الجهالة، وإنه زوجهما جميعاً في عقدة واحدة لم يجز واحدة منهما كما لو وكل رجلاً أن يزوجه امرأة فزوجه امرأتين في عقدة واحدة لم يجز اهـ. وقيد بكون المرأة منكرة أخذاً من التنكير لأنه لو عينها فزوجها وأخرى معها تلزمه المعينة. وقيد في الهداية نكاح المرأتين بأن يكون في عقد واحد لأنه لو زوجهما في عقدتين تلزمه الأولى ونكاح الثانية موقوف على الإجازة لأنه فضولي فيه، ولذا قال في المختصر «بامرأتين) ولم يقل بعقدين»، وفرعوا على أن التنصيص على الشيء لا ينفي الحكم عما عداه لو قال زوج ابنتي هذه رجلاً يرجع إلى علم ودين بمشورة فلان فزوجها رجلاً على هذه الصفة من غير مشورة فإنه يجوز كما في الخانية، وأما إذا قال له عبدي هذا بشهود أو بمحضر فلان فباعه بغير شهود أو بغير محضر فلان فإنه يجوز بخلاف ما إذا قال لا تبعه إلا بشهود فباعه بغير شهود فإنه لا يجوز كما في الظهيرية قوله : (لا بأمة) أي لا يكون المأمور بنكاح امرأة مخالفاً بنكاح أمة لغيره فينفذ على الموكل عند أبي حنيفة رجوعاً إلى إطلاق اللفظ وعدم التهمة. وقالا : لا يجوز أن يزوجه كفئاً لأن المطلق ينصرف إلى المتعارف وهو التزوج بالإكفاء. قلنا : العرف مشترك أو هو عرف عملي فلا يصح مقيداً، وذكر في الوكالة أن اعتبار الكفاءة في هذا استحسان عندهما لأن كل واحد لا يعجز عن التزوج بمطلق الزوجة فكانت الاستعانة في التزوج بالكفء . كذا في الهداية وظاهره ترجيح قولهما لأن الاستحسان مقدم على القياس إلا في مسائل معدودة ليس هذا منها، ولذا قال الأسبيجابي : قولهما أحسن للفتوى واختاره أبو الليث وفي فتح القدير والحق أن قول أبي حنيفة ليس قياساً لأنه أخذ بنفس اللفظ المنصوص فكان النظر في أي الاستحسان من أولى اهـ.
قيد بكونه أمره بنكاح امرأة ولم يصفها لأنه لو وكله بتزويج - ترة فزوجه أمة أو عكسه لم يجز، ولو زوجه في عسكه مدبرة أو أم ولد أو مكاتبة جاز. وأطلق في الأمر فشمل الأمير وغيره، ووضعها في الهداية في الأمير ليفيد أن غيره بالأولى. وقيد بكون الأمر رجلاً لأنها لو وكلته في تزويجها ولم تعين فزوجها غير كفء كان مخالفاً على قول أبي حنيفة أيضاً على الأصح كما في الخانية لاعتبارها من جهة الرجال، وإن كان كفئاً إلا أنه أعمى أو مقعد أو أو معتوه فهو جائز، وكذا لو كان خصياً أو عنيناً وإن كان لها التفريق بعد ذلك. وأفاد المصنف أن الأمر المطلق يجري على إطلاقه ولا يجوز تقييده إلا بدليل وإن العرف المشترك لا مخصصاً فالوكيل بتزويج امرأة ليس مخالفاً لو زوجه عمياء أو شوهاء لها لعاب سائل
صبي
يصح
قوله (وقالا لا يجوز إلا أن يزوجه كفؤاً الخ) قال الكشاف دلت المسألة على أن الكفاءة تعتبر في النساء للرجال أيضاً عندهما، وكذا ذكره في الأصل كذا في العناية. وذكر قبله تحت قول الهداية ومن أمره أمير الخ قيده بالأمير وحكم غيره كذلك. قال الإمام المحبوبي : وعلى هذا

وعقل زائل وشق مائل أو شلاء أو رتقاء أو صغيرة لا يجامع مثلها أو كتابية أو امرأة حلف بطلاقها أو زوجه امرأة على أكثر من مهر مثلها ولو بغبن فاحش عند الإمام، أو زوجها رجلاً بأقل من مهر مثلها كذلك أو امرأة كان الموكل آلي منها أو في عدة الموكل والأصل أن الوكيل إذا خالف إلى خير أو كان خلافه كلا خلاف نفذ عقده كما لو أمره بعمياء فزوجه بصيرة، وليس منه ما إذا أمره بالفاسد فزوجه صحيحاً بل لا يجوز لعدم الوكالة بالنكاح أصلاً. وأما العدة بعد الدخول فيه وثبوت النسب فليس حكماً له بل للوطء إذ لم يتمحض زنا بخلاف أمره بالبيع الفاسد له البيع صحيحاً وليس منه أيضاً ما إذا وكله بألف فلم ترض المرأة حتى زادها الوكيل ثوباً من مال نفسه فإنه موقوف على إجازة الزوج لكونه ضرراً على تقدير استحقاق الثوب أو هلاكه قبل التسليم فإنها ترجع بقيمته على الزوج لا الوكيل - كما في الذخيرة - وللزوج الخيار. وإذا دخل بها قبل العلم فإن اختار التفريق فكالنكاح الفساد. وليس منه أيضاً ما إذا أمره ببيضاء فزوجه سوداء أو على القلب أو من قبيلة كذا فزوجه من أخرى فإنه غير نافذ، وقيدنا بكون الأمة لغيره لأنه لو زوجه أمة نفسه ولو مكاتبته ـ كما في المحيط - فإنه لا ينفذ للتهمة كما لو زوجه بنته فإن كانت صغيرة لا يجوز اتفاقاً، وكذا موليته كبنت أخيه الصغيرة، وإن كانت كبيرة فكذلك عنده خلافاً لهما. ولو زوجه أخته الكبيرة برضاها جاز اتفاقاً، والوكيل من قبل المرأة إذا زوجها من أبيه أو ابنه لا يجوز في قول أبي حنيفة، وفي كل موضع لا ينفذ فعل الوكيل فالعقد موقوف على إجازة الموكل، وحكم الرسول كحكم الوكيل في جميع ما ذكرنا وضمانهما المهر صحيح. وإنكار المرسل والموكل الرسالة والوكالة بعد الضمان ولا بينة لا يسقط الضمان عنهما فيجب نصف المهر، وتوكيل المرأة المتزوجة بالتزويج إذا طلقت وانقضت عدتها صحيح كتوكيلة أن الخلاف إذا لم يكن أميراً فزوجه الوكيل أمة أو حرة عمياء أو مقطوعة اليدين أو رتقاء أو مفلوجة أو مجنونة، إما اتفاقاً وإما لما قيل قيده بذلك ليظهر الكفاءة فإنها من جانب النساء للرجال مستحسنة الوكالة عندهما .اهـ. فأفاد أنها معتبرة عندهما لا مطلقاً بل هنا فقط. وعن هذا قال في الحواشي السعدية : قوله «دلت المسألة الخ إن أراد دلت على اعتبارها في الوكالة عندهما فمسلم بالنظر إلى دليلها، وإن أراد مطلقاً اه. فمنوع

ويؤيده ما قدمناه في أول الفصل عن البدائع قوله : (أو) عرف عملي الخ) أي عرف من حيث العمل والاستعمال لا من حيث اللفظ وبيانه أن العرف على نوعين لفظي نحو الدابة تقيد لفظاً بالفرس، ونحو المال بين العرب بالإبل، وعملي أي العزف من حيث العمل أي من حيث إن عمل الناس كذا كلبسهم الجديد يوم العيد وأمثاله كذا في العناية وفيه بحث لصاحب السعدية
فراجعه .
Book of Nikah / Chapter on Suitability. He appointed him to marry him to so-and-so or so-and-so; whichever he marries him to is valid, and the agency is not invalidated by this ambiguity. And if he marries him to both in one contract, neither is valid, just as if he appointed a man to marry him a woman and he married him two women in one contract, it is not valid. He restricted it to the woman being indefinite, taking from the tanwin, because if he specified her and married her along with another, the specified one is binding. In Al-Hidayah, he restricted marrying two women to being in one contract, because if he marries them in two contracts, the first is binding and the marriage of the second is suspended on permission because he is an unauthorized agent in it. Therefore he said in Al-Mukhtasar 'with two women' and did not say 'with two contracts'. They derived that specification of a thing does not negate the ruling from what is other than it: if he said 'marry this daughter of mine to a man who is knowledgeable and religious with the counsel of so-and-so' and he married her to a man with these qualities without counsel, it is valid, as in Al-Khaniyyah. And if he said to him 'sell this slave of mine with witnesses or in the presence of so-and-so' and he sold him without witnesses or without the presence of so-and-so, it is valid, contrary to if he said 'do not sell him except with witnesses' and he sold him without witnesses, it is not valid, as in Al-Zahiriyyah. His statement: (not to a slave woman) i.e. the one ordered to marry a woman is not in violation by marrying a slave woman belonging to another, and it is effective on the principal according to Abu Hanifah, returning to the absolute wording and absence of suspicion. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not permissible unless he marries him a suitable person, because the absolute is turned to the customary, which is marriage to suitable people. We said: The custom is shared or it is a practical custom, so it is not valid as a restriction. It is mentioned in Al-Wakalah that consideration of suitability in this is istihsan according to them because each person is not incapable of marrying an absolute wife, so assistance is in marrying a suitable person. Thus in Al-Hidayah, and its apparent meaning is preponderance of their statement because istihsan is given precedence over qiyas except in a few issues, and this is not one of them. Therefore Al-Asbijabi said: Their statement is better for fatwa, and Abu Al-Layth chose it. In Fath Al-Qadir, the truth is that Abu Hanifah's statement is not qiyas because he took the explicit wording, so consideration is which istihsan is more appropriate. He restricted it to his ordering him to marry a woman without describing her, because if he appointed him to marry a free woman and he married a slave woman, or vice versa, it is not valid. If he marries him a mudabbarah, umm walad, or makatabah, it is valid. And his command is absolute, so it includes the amir and others. In Al-Hidayah, he placed it in the amir to indicate that others are even more so. He restricted it to the commander being a man, because if she appointed him to marry her and she did not specify, and he married her to an unsuitable person, he is in violation according to Abu Hanifah as well according to the most correct view, as in Al-Khaniyyah, because she is considered from the side of men. Even if he is suitable but is blind, paralyzed, or insane, it is valid. Similarly, if he is a eunuch or impotent, although she may separate afterwards. The author indicated that the absolute command runs on its absolute, and it is not permissible to restrict it except with evidence, and shared custom is not a specifier. So the agent appointed to marry a woman is not in violation if he marries her to a blind, ugly woman with flowing saliva, a boy? It is valid. His statement (they said it is not permissible unless he marries him a suitable person) Al-Kashshaf said the issue indicates that suitability is considered for women from men as well according to them, and it is mentioned in Al-Asl, thus in Al-Inayah. And he mentioned before it under the statement of Al-Hidayah 'whoever an amir commanded' etc., he restricted it to the amir, and the ruling for others is similar. Imam Al-Mahbubi said: And on this... and removing intellect, leaning face, or paralyzed hand, or a woman with a blockage, or a young girl who is not fit for intercourse, or a kitabiyyah, or a woman he swore divorce on, or he married him a woman for more than her proper mahr even if excessive according to the Imam, or he married her to a man for less than her proper mahr similarly, or a woman from whom the principal had taken an oath of abstinence, or a woman in the principal's waiting period. The principle is that if the agent violates to something better, or his violation is like no violation, his contract is effective, as if he commanded him to marry a blind woman and he married a sighted one. Not from this is if he commanded him to sell in a corrupt way and he sold in a valid way; rather it is not permissible due to absence of agency in marriage at all. As for the waiting period after consummation and establishment of lineage, it is not a ruling for him but for intercourse, because it was not purely zina, unlike if he commanded him to sell corruptly, he has the valid sale. Also not from this is if he appointed him with a thousand and the woman did not agree until the agent added a garment from his own wealth, then it is suspended on the husband's permission because it is harm due to possibility of the garment being claimed or destroyed before delivery, so she claims its value from the husband, not the agent, as in Al-Dhakhirah. The husband has the option. If he consummated before knowledge, if he chooses separation, it is like a defective marriage. Also not from this is if he commanded him to marry a white woman and he married a black woman, or vice versa, or from such a tribe and he married from another, it is not effective. We restricted it to the slave woman belonging to another, because if he marries him his own slave woman, even if she is his makatabah, as in Al-Muhit, it is not effective due to suspicion, like if he marries him his daughter: if she is young, it is not valid by agreement; similarly his ward like his young brother's daughter; if she is an adult, similarly according to him, unlike them. If he marries him his adult sister with her consent, it is valid by agreement. The agent from the woman's side, if he marries her to his father or son, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifah. In every place where the agent's action is not effective, the contract is suspended on the principal's permission. The ruling of the messenger is like the ruling of the agent in all we mentioned, and their guarantee of the mahr is valid. The denial of the sender and principal of the message and agency after the guarantee without evidence does not drop the guarantee from them, so half the mahr is obligatory. The agency of a married woman for marriage if she divorces and her waiting period ends is valid. Like his agency that the disagreement if he was not an amir and the agent married him a slave woman or a free blind woman, or one with hands cut, or with a blockage, or paralyzed, or insane, either by agreement or due to what was said restricting it to show suitability, for it is from the side of women for men, agency is recommended according to them. So it indicates that it is considered according to them not absolutely but only here. And from this he said in Al-Hawashi Al-Sa'diyyah: His statement 'the issue indicates...' if he meant it indicates consideration in agency according to them, it is granted with regard to its evidence; if he meant absolutely, it is denied. It is supported by what we presented at the beginning of the chapter from Al-Bada'i'. His statement: 'or practical custom' i.e. custom in terms of action and usage not in terms of wording. Explanation: custom is of two types: verbal, like 'animal' is restricted verbally to horse, like wealth among Arabs to camels; and practical, i.e. custom in terms of action, i.e. action of people like wearing new clothes on Eid and similar, thus in Al-Inayah, and there is a discussion for the author of Al-Sa'diyyah, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the chapter on suitability (kafa'ah) in marriage. It primarily deals with the scope of an agent's authority when appointed to marry a woman to a man, particularly when the agent deviates from implicit or explicit conditions. The text opens with the ruling that if a principal appoints an agent to marry him to one of two named women, the agent's choice is valid, and the agency is not invalidated by this ambiguity. However, if the agent marries both in a single contract, neither marriage is valid, analogized to an agent appointed to marry one woman marrying two in one contract. The commentator clarifies that this restriction applies only when the woman is unspecified (nakirah); if specified and the agent marries her along with another, the specified marriage is binding. The discussion continues with examples of conditions: if the principal says 'marry my daughter to a knowledgeable, religious man with the counsel of so-and-so,' and the agent does so without counsel, it is valid because the condition is not a strict stipulation. Conversely, if the principal explicitly prohibits sale without witnesses, selling without witnesses invalidates the sale. The central dispute arises when the agent is simply told to marry a woman (without description) and he marries a slave woman belonging to another. Abu Hanifa holds that the agent has not violated his mandate because the wording is absolute; there is no suspicion because the slave woman is owned by another, so the marriage is effective on the principal. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that the absolute command is understood according to customary practice, and custom dictates marrying a free woman (kuf'), so marrying a slave woman is a violation. They base this on istihsan (juristic preference), considering that each person can easily marry a free woman, so the need to rely on an agent arises only for finding a suitable match. The text notes that Al-Hidayah seems to preponderate the Sahibayn's view, and Al-Asbijabi and Abu al-Layth preferred it for fatwa. However, Fath al-Qadir argues that Abu Hanifa's position is not mere qiyas but adheres to the explicit wording, and the 'istihsan' in question is which one is more appropriate. The passage then lists numerous scenarios where the agent's action is considered valid or invalid: if the agent marries a mudabbarah, umm walad, or makatabah, it is valid; if he marries a blind, paralyzed, or insane person, it is valid even if unsuitable in some respects; but if he marries a woman with obvious defects like a flowing salivating mouth, crooked face, or a young girl unfit for intercourse, it is invalid. For women, if a female principal appoints an agent to marry her and he marries her to an unsuitable man, it is a violation according to Abu Hanifa as well, because suitability is considered from the man's side. The text emphasizes the principle that the agent's action is valid if he deviates to something better (e.g., marrying a sighted woman when told to marry a blind one) or if the deviation is inconsequential. However, if he deviates to something that harms the principal or violates explicit instructions, the marriage is invalid or suspended on the principal's permission. The passage concludes with distinctions between verbal and practical custom, noting that practical custom (like wearing new clothes on Eid) does not serve as a specifier for absolute wording.

Key Terms
كفؤ (kuf'): A suitable or equal match in marriage, specifically a free person (ḥurr) vs. slave (ama) in this context
وكيل (wakil): Agent appointed by the principal (muwakkil) to perform a legal act, here marriage
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to depart from strict qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling
عرف عملي (urf amali): Practical custom based on common practice, not conventional usage of language

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the marriage valid when the agent marries a slave woman belonging to another, despite the principal's unqualified command?
A) Because the agent must follow custom, and custom allows slave marriages
B) Because the agent was told to marry a woman, and the term 'woman' includes free and slave, and there is no suspicion
C) Because the agent obtained the slave owner's permission
D) Because the principal implicitly agreed to any type of woman

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an absolute command is not restricted by practical custom; only verbal custom can limit it, which is why Abu Hanifa upheld the marriage to a slave woman.

Nikah — Marriage

Practical Custom ('Urf 'Amali) vs. Verbal Custom in Restricting Absolute Commands
Definition of verbal and practical custom in Hanafi legal theory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between verbal custom (urf lafzi) and practical custom (urf amali) and explain why the Hanafi school does not consider practical custom a restrictor of absolute commands.

Core Idea
Only verbal custom restricts an absolute command; practical custom, based on common action, does not.

In the previous lesson, we saw that Abu Hanifa argued that the custom of marrying free women is a practical custom and thus does not limit the absolute wording. This lesson defines the two types of custom in Hanafi jurisprudence and explains the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types of custom
Verbal custom (urf lafzi): where a word is conventionally used for a specific meaning (e.g., 'animal' for horse). Practical custom (urf amali): common practice (e.g., wearing new clothes on Eid).
The distinction is crucial for legal interpretation.
2
Explain why practical custom does not restrict absolute commands
Because absolute wording is general; practical custom is not a linguistic usage that changes the meaning of the word. The Hanafi usul principle: only verbal custom can restrict an absolute expression.
This is based on the idea that language is defined by convention (urf lafzi), not by actions.
3
Apply to the agency case
The custom of marrying free women is a practical custom; thus the absolute command 'marry a woman' includes slave women. Therefore, the agent is not in violation.
This directly explains Abu Hanifa's position.

كتاب النكاح/ فصل في الكفاءة

وكله أن يزوجه فلانة أو فلانة فأيتهما زوجه جاز ولا يبطل التوكيل بهذه الجهالة، وإنه زوجهما جميعاً في عقدة واحدة لم يجز واحدة منهما كما لو وكل رجلاً أن يزوجه امرأة فزوجه امرأتين في عقدة واحدة لم يجز اهـ. وقيد بكون المرأة منكرة أخذاً من التنكير لأنه لو عينها فزوجها وأخرى معها تلزمه المعينة. وقيد في الهداية نكاح المرأتين بأن يكون في عقد واحد لأنه لو زوجهما في عقدتين تلزمه الأولى ونكاح الثانية موقوف على الإجازة لأنه فضولي فيه، ولذا قال في المختصر «بامرأتين) ولم يقل بعقدين»، وفرعوا على أن التنصيص على الشيء لا ينفي الحكم عما عداه لو قال زوج ابنتي هذه رجلاً يرجع إلى علم ودين بمشورة فلان فزوجها رجلاً على هذه الصفة من غير مشورة فإنه يجوز كما في الخانية، وأما إذا قال له عبدي هذا بشهود أو بمحضر فلان فباعه بغير شهود أو بغير محضر فلان فإنه يجوز بخلاف ما إذا قال لا تبعه إلا بشهود فباعه بغير شهود فإنه لا يجوز كما في الظهيرية قوله : (لا بأمة) أي لا يكون المأمور بنكاح امرأة مخالفاً بنكاح أمة لغيره فينفذ على الموكل عند أبي حنيفة رجوعاً إلى إطلاق اللفظ وعدم التهمة. وقالا : لا يجوز أن يزوجه كفئاً لأن المطلق ينصرف إلى المتعارف وهو التزوج بالإكفاء. قلنا : العرف مشترك أو هو عرف عملي فلا يصح مقيداً، وذكر في الوكالة أن اعتبار الكفاءة في هذا استحسان عندهما لأن كل واحد لا يعجز عن التزوج بمطلق الزوجة فكانت الاستعانة في التزوج بالكفء . كذا في الهداية وظاهره ترجيح قولهما لأن الاستحسان مقدم على القياس إلا في مسائل معدودة ليس هذا منها، ولذا قال الأسبيجابي : قولهما أحسن للفتوى واختاره أبو الليث وفي فتح القدير والحق أن قول أبي حنيفة ليس قياساً لأنه أخذ بنفس اللفظ المنصوص فكان النظر في أي الاستحسان من أولى اهـ.
قيد بكونه أمره بنكاح امرأة ولم يصفها لأنه لو وكله بتزويج - ترة فزوجه أمة أو عكسه لم يجز، ولو زوجه في عسكه مدبرة أو أم ولد أو مكاتبة جاز. وأطلق في الأمر فشمل الأمير وغيره، ووضعها في الهداية في الأمير ليفيد أن غيره بالأولى. وقيد بكون الأمر رجلاً لأنها لو وكلته في تزويجها ولم تعين فزوجها غير كفء كان مخالفاً على قول أبي حنيفة أيضاً على الأصح كما في الخانية لاعتبارها من جهة الرجال، وإن كان كفئاً إلا أنه أعمى أو مقعد أو أو معتوه فهو جائز، وكذا لو كان خصياً أو عنيناً وإن كان لها التفريق بعد ذلك. وأفاد المصنف أن الأمر المطلق يجري على إطلاقه ولا يجوز تقييده إلا بدليل وإن العرف المشترك لا مخصصاً فالوكيل بتزويج امرأة ليس مخالفاً لو زوجه عمياء أو شوهاء لها لعاب سائل
صبي
يصح
قوله (وقالا لا يجوز إلا أن يزوجه كفؤاً الخ) قال الكشاف دلت المسألة على أن الكفاءة تعتبر في النساء للرجال أيضاً عندهما، وكذا ذكره في الأصل كذا في العناية. وذكر قبله تحت قول الهداية ومن أمره أمير الخ قيده بالأمير وحكم غيره كذلك. قال الإمام المحبوبي : وعلى هذا

وعقل زائل وشق مائل أو شلاء أو رتقاء أو صغيرة لا يجامع مثلها أو كتابية أو امرأة حلف بطلاقها أو زوجه امرأة على أكثر من مهر مثلها ولو بغبن فاحش عند الإمام، أو زوجها رجلاً بأقل من مهر مثلها كذلك أو امرأة كان الموكل آلي منها أو في عدة الموكل والأصل أن الوكيل إذا خالف إلى خير أو كان خلافه كلا خلاف نفذ عقده كما لو أمره بعمياء فزوجه بصيرة، وليس منه ما إذا أمره بالفاسد فزوجه صحيحاً بل لا يجوز لعدم الوكالة بالنكاح أصلاً. وأما العدة بعد الدخول فيه وثبوت النسب فليس حكماً له بل للوطء إذ لم يتمحض زنا بخلاف أمره بالبيع الفاسد له البيع صحيحاً وليس منه أيضاً ما إذا وكله بألف فلم ترض المرأة حتى زادها الوكيل ثوباً من مال نفسه فإنه موقوف على إجازة الزوج لكونه ضرراً على تقدير استحقاق الثوب أو هلاكه قبل التسليم فإنها ترجع بقيمته على الزوج لا الوكيل - كما في الذخيرة - وللزوج الخيار. وإذا دخل بها قبل العلم فإن اختار التفريق فكالنكاح الفساد. وليس منه أيضاً ما إذا أمره ببيضاء فزوجه سوداء أو على القلب أو من قبيلة كذا فزوجه من أخرى فإنه غير نافذ، وقيدنا بكون الأمة لغيره لأنه لو زوجه أمة نفسه ولو مكاتبته ـ كما في المحيط - فإنه لا ينفذ للتهمة كما لو زوجه بنته فإن كانت صغيرة لا يجوز اتفاقاً، وكذا موليته كبنت أخيه الصغيرة، وإن كانت كبيرة فكذلك عنده خلافاً لهما. ولو زوجه أخته الكبيرة برضاها جاز اتفاقاً، والوكيل من قبل المرأة إذا زوجها من أبيه أو ابنه لا يجوز في قول أبي حنيفة، وفي كل موضع لا ينفذ فعل الوكيل فالعقد موقوف على إجازة الموكل، وحكم الرسول كحكم الوكيل في جميع ما ذكرنا وضمانهما المهر صحيح. وإنكار المرسل والموكل الرسالة والوكالة بعد الضمان ولا بينة لا يسقط الضمان عنهما فيجب نصف المهر، وتوكيل المرأة المتزوجة بالتزويج إذا طلقت وانقضت عدتها صحيح كتوكيلة أن الخلاف إذا لم يكن أميراً فزوجه الوكيل أمة أو حرة عمياء أو مقطوعة اليدين أو رتقاء أو مفلوجة أو مجنونة، إما اتفاقاً وإما لما قيل قيده بذلك ليظهر الكفاءة فإنها من جانب النساء للرجال مستحسنة الوكالة عندهما .اهـ. فأفاد أنها معتبرة عندهما لا مطلقاً بل هنا فقط. وعن هذا قال في الحواشي السعدية : قوله «دلت المسألة الخ إن أراد دلت على اعتبارها في الوكالة عندهما فمسلم بالنظر إلى دليلها، وإن أراد مطلقاً اه. فمنوع

ويؤيده ما قدمناه في أول الفصل عن البدائع قوله : (أو) عرف عملي الخ) أي عرف من حيث العمل والاستعمال لا من حيث اللفظ وبيانه أن العرف على نوعين لفظي نحو الدابة تقيد لفظاً بالفرس، ونحو المال بين العرب بالإبل، وعملي أي العزف من حيث العمل أي من حيث إن عمل الناس كذا كلبسهم الجديد يوم العيد وأمثاله كذا في العناية وفيه بحث لصاحب السعدية
