Book of Nikah / Chapter on Suitability. He appointed him to marry him to so-and-so or so-and-so; whichever he marries him to is valid, and the agency is not invalidated by this ambiguity. And if he marries him to both in one contract, neither is valid, just as if he appointed a man to marry him a woman and he married him two women in one contract, it is not valid. He restricted it to the woman being indefinite, taking from the tanwin, because if he specified her and married her along with another, the specified one is binding. In Al-Hidayah, he restricted marrying two women to being in one contract, because if he marries them in two contracts, the first is binding and the marriage of the second is suspended on permission because he is an unauthorized agent in it. Therefore he said in Al-Mukhtasar 'with two women' and did not say 'with two contracts'. They derived that specification of a thing does not negate the ruling from what is other than it: if he said 'marry this daughter of mine to a man who is knowledgeable and religious with the counsel of so-and-so' and he married her to a man with these qualities without counsel, it is valid, as in Al-Khaniyyah. And if he said to him 'sell this slave of mine with witnesses or in the presence of so-and-so' and he sold him without witnesses or without the presence of so-and-so, it is valid, contrary to if he said 'do not sell him except with witnesses' and he sold him without witnesses, it is not valid, as in Al-Zahiriyyah. His statement: (not to a slave woman) i.e. the one ordered to marry a woman is not in violation by marrying a slave woman belonging to another, and it is effective on the principal according to Abu Hanifah, returning to the absolute wording and absence of suspicion. They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not permissible unless he marries him a suitable person, because the absolute is turned to the customary, which is marriage to suitable people. We said: The custom is shared or it is a practical custom, so it is not valid as a restriction. It is mentioned in Al-Wakalah that consideration of suitability in this is istihsan according to them because each person is not incapable of marrying an absolute wife, so assistance is in marrying a suitable person. Thus in Al-Hidayah, and its apparent meaning is preponderance of their statement because istihsan is given precedence over qiyas except in a few issues, and this is not one of them. Therefore Al-Asbijabi said: Their statement is better for fatwa, and Abu Al-Layth chose it. In Fath Al-Qadir, the truth is that Abu Hanifah's statement is not qiyas because he took the explicit wording, so consideration is which istihsan is more appropriate. He restricted it to his ordering him to marry a woman without describing her, because if he appointed him to marry a free woman and he married a slave woman, or vice versa, it is not valid. If he marries him a mudabbarah, umm walad, or makatabah, it is valid. And his command is absolute, so it includes the amir and others. In Al-Hidayah, he placed it in the amir to indicate that others are even more so. He restricted it to the commander being a man, because if she appointed him to marry her and she did not specify, and he married her to an unsuitable person, he is in violation according to Abu Hanifah as well according to the most correct view, as in Al-Khaniyyah, because she is considered from the side of men. Even if he is suitable but is blind, paralyzed, or insane, it is valid. Similarly, if he is a eunuch or impotent, although she may separate afterwards. The author indicated that the absolute command runs on its absolute, and it is not permissible to restrict it except with evidence, and shared custom is not a specifier. So the agent appointed to marry a woman is not in violation if he marries her to a blind, ugly woman with flowing saliva, a boy? It is valid. His statement (they said it is not permissible unless he marries him a suitable person) Al-Kashshaf said the issue indicates that suitability is considered for women from men as well according to them, and it is mentioned in Al-Asl, thus in Al-Inayah. And he mentioned before it under the statement of Al-Hidayah 'whoever an amir commanded' etc., he restricted it to the amir, and the ruling for others is similar. Imam Al-Mahbubi said: And on this... and removing intellect, leaning face, or paralyzed hand, or a woman with a blockage, or a young girl who is not fit for intercourse, or a kitabiyyah, or a woman he swore divorce on, or he married him a woman for more than her proper mahr even if excessive according to the Imam, or he married her to a man for less than her proper mahr similarly, or a woman from whom the principal had taken an oath of abstinence, or a woman in the principal's waiting period. The principle is that if the agent violates to something better, or his violation is like no violation, his contract is effective, as if he commanded him to marry a blind woman and he married a sighted one. Not from this is if he commanded him to sell in a corrupt way and he sold in a valid way; rather it is not permissible due to absence of agency in marriage at all. As for the waiting period after consummation and establishment of lineage, it is not a ruling for him but for intercourse, because it was not purely zina, unlike if he commanded him to sell corruptly, he has the valid sale. Also not from this is if he appointed him with a thousand and the woman did not agree until the agent added a garment from his own wealth, then it is suspended on the husband's permission because it is harm due to possibility of the garment being claimed or destroyed before delivery, so she claims its value from the husband, not the agent, as in Al-Dhakhirah. The husband has the option. If he consummated before knowledge, if he chooses separation, it is like a defective marriage. Also not from this is if he commanded him to marry a white woman and he married a black woman, or vice versa, or from such a tribe and he married from another, it is not effective. We restricted it to the slave woman belonging to another, because if he marries him his own slave woman, even if she is his makatabah, as in Al-Muhit, it is not effective due to suspicion, like if he marries him his daughter: if she is young, it is not valid by agreement; similarly his ward like his young brother's daughter; if she is an adult, similarly according to him, unlike them. If he marries him his adult sister with her consent, it is valid by agreement. The agent from the woman's side, if he marries her to his father or son, it is not valid according to Abu Hanifah. In every place where the agent's action is not effective, the contract is suspended on the principal's permission. The ruling of the messenger is like the ruling of the agent in all we mentioned, and their guarantee of the mahr is valid. The denial of the sender and principal of the message and agency after the guarantee without evidence does not drop the guarantee from them, so half the mahr is obligatory. The agency of a married woman for marriage if she divorces and her waiting period ends is valid. Like his agency that the disagreement if he was not an amir and the agent married him a slave woman or a free blind woman, or one with hands cut, or with a blockage, or paralyzed, or insane, either by agreement or due to what was said restricting it to show suitability, for it is from the side of women for men, agency is recommended according to them. So it indicates that it is considered according to them not absolutely but only here. And from this he said in Al-Hawashi Al-Sa'diyyah: His statement 'the issue indicates...' if he meant it indicates consideration in agency according to them, it is granted with regard to its evidence; if he meant absolutely, it is denied. It is supported by what we presented at the beginning of the chapter from Al-Bada'i'. His statement: 'or practical custom' i.e. custom in terms of action and usage not in terms of wording. Explanation: custom is of two types: verbal, like 'animal' is restricted verbally to horse, like wealth among Arabs to camels; and practical, i.e. custom in terms of action, i.e. action of people like wearing new clothes on Eid and similar, thus in Al-Inayah, and there is a discussion for the author of Al-Sa'diyyah, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the chapter on suitability (kafa'ah) in marriage. It primarily deals with the scope of an agent's authority when appointed to marry a woman to a man, particularly when the agent deviates from implicit or explicit conditions. The text opens with the ruling that if a principal appoints an agent to marry him to one of two named women, the agent's choice is valid, and the agency is not invalidated by this ambiguity. However, if the agent marries both in a single contract, neither marriage is valid, analogized to an agent appointed to marry one woman marrying two in one contract. The commentator clarifies that this restriction applies only when the woman is unspecified (nakirah); if specified and the agent marries her along with another, the specified marriage is binding. The discussion continues with examples of conditions: if the principal says 'marry my daughter to a knowledgeable, religious man with the counsel of so-and-so,' and the agent does so without counsel, it is valid because the condition is not a strict stipulation. Conversely, if the principal explicitly prohibits sale without witnesses, selling without witnesses invalidates the sale. The central dispute arises when the agent is simply told to marry a woman (without description) and he marries a slave woman belonging to another. Abu Hanifa holds that the agent has not violated his mandate because the wording is absolute; there is no suspicion because the slave woman is owned by another, so the marriage is effective on the principal. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that the absolute command is understood according to customary practice, and custom dictates marrying a free woman (kuf'), so marrying a slave woman is a violation. They base this on istihsan (juristic preference), considering that each person can easily marry a free woman, so the need to rely on an agent arises only for finding a suitable match. The text notes that Al-Hidayah seems to preponderate the Sahibayn's view, and Al-Asbijabi and Abu al-Layth preferred it for fatwa. However, Fath al-Qadir argues that Abu Hanifa's position is not mere qiyas but adheres to the explicit wording, and the 'istihsan' in question is which one is more appropriate. The passage then lists numerous scenarios where the agent's action is considered valid or invalid: if the agent marries a mudabbarah, umm walad, or makatabah, it is valid; if he marries a blind, paralyzed, or insane person, it is valid even if unsuitable in some respects; but if he marries a woman with obvious defects like a flowing salivating mouth, crooked face, or a young girl unfit for intercourse, it is invalid. For women, if a female principal appoints an agent to marry her and he marries her to an unsuitable man, it is a violation according to Abu Hanifa as well, because suitability is considered from the man's side. The text emphasizes the principle that the agent's action is valid if he deviates to something better (e.g., marrying a sighted woman when told to marry a blind one) or if the deviation is inconsequential. However, if he deviates to something that harms the principal or violates explicit instructions, the marriage is invalid or suspended on the principal's permission. The passage concludes with distinctions between verbal and practical custom, noting that practical custom (like wearing new clothes on Eid) does not serve as a specifier for absolute wording.

Key Terms
عرف عملي (urf amali): Practical custom based on common practice, not conventional usage of language
عرف لفظي (urf lafzi): Verbal custom: when a word is conventionally used for a specific meaning
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference used to depart from strict qiyas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of custom can restrict an absolute command in legal texts?
A) Both verbal and practical
B) Only verbal
C) Only practical
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Practical custom does not change the linguistic meaning of a command, so it cannot restrict an absolute wording in Hanafi law.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Principle of the Agent's Deviation: Valid or Invalid?
Continues the discussion of the agent's actions and defines 'urf 'amali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that an agent's deviation to a better option results in a valid contract, and distinguish it from cases where the deviation invalidates the contract.

Core Idea
If the agent acts to the principal's benefit or the deviation is not truly contrary, the marriage is valid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the fundamental rule governing a marriage agent's actions when he departs from his instructions. The key is whether the departure is to the better or harmless; if so, the contract is effective. We will explore the initial list of prohibited deviations and the crucial example of ordering a blind woman but marrying a sighted one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm of the agent's deviation
Determine whether the deviation results in a valid, invalid, or suspended marriage. The text lists several scenarios (e.g., witless, crooked, etc.) that are prima facie invalid unless the deviation is to a better option.
These defects are assumed to be harmful unless overridden by explicit benefit.
2
Locate the principle
Find the statement: 'الوكيل إذا خالف إلى خير أو كان خلافه كلا خلاف نفذ عقده' (if the agent acts to a better option or his contrary is not a true contrary, his contract is executed). This is the governing rule.
The principle is based on the agent's duty to act in the principal's interest.
3
Apply to the example of blind vs. sighted
If the principal ordered marrying a blind woman but the agent married a sighted one, the contract is valid because it is a better option. Test this against the principle.
This contrasts with deviations that are clearly worse, such as marrying a woman with defects.
4
Contrast with the case of ordering a fasid marriage
If the principal ordered a corrupt (fasid) marriage and the agent performed a valid one, the contract is invalid because the agent had no authority to perform a marriage at all when the principal's order was based on a corrupt basis.
This highlights that agency for marriage is a specific authorization; if the principal's order is itself invalid, the agent cannot override it.
5
Note the distinction between marriage and sale
The text contrasts with sale: if ordered a fasid sale, the agent can make a valid sale because the agency for sale is broader. In marriage, the agent's authority is narrower.
This distinction is rooted in the different natures of the contracts.

وعقل زائل وشق مائل أو شلاء أو رتقاء أو صغيرة لا يجامع مثلها أو كتابية أو امرأة حلف بطلاقها أو زوجه امرأة على أكثر من مهر مثلها ولو بغبن فاحش عند الإمام، أو زوجها رجلاً بأقل من مهر مثلها كذلك أو امرأة كان الموكل آلي منها أو في عدة الموكل والأصل أن الوكيل إذا خالف إلى خير أو كان خلافه كلا خلاف نفذ عقده كما لو أمره بعمياء فزوجه بصيرة، وليس منه ما إذا أمره بالفاسد فزوجه صحيحاً بل لا يجوز لعدم الوكالة بالنكاح أصلاً. وأما العدة بعد الدخول فيه وثبوت النسب فليس حكماً له بل للوطء إذ لم يتمحض زنا بخلاف أمره بالبيع الفاسد له البيع صحيحاً وليس منه أيضاً ما إذا وكله بألف فلم ترض المرأة حتى زادها الوكيل ثوباً من مال نفسه فإنه موقوف على إجازة الزوج لكونه ضرراً على تقدير استحقاق الثوب أو هلاكه قبل التسليم فإنها ترجع بقيمته على الزوج لا الوكيل - كما في الذخيرة - وللزوج الخيار. وإذا دخل بها قبل العلم فإن اختار التفريق فكالنكاح الفساد. وليس منه أيضاً ما إذا أمره ببيضاء فزوجه سوداء أو على القلب أو من قبيلة كذا فزوجه من أخرى فإنه غير نافذ، وقيدنا بكون الأمة لغيره لأنه لو زوجه أمة نفسه ولو مكاتبته ـ كما في المحيط - فإنه لا ينفذ للتهمة كما لو زوجه بنته فإن كانت صغيرة لا يجوز اتفاقاً، وكذا موليته كبنت أخيه الصغيرة، وإن كانت كبيرة فكذلك عنده خلافاً لهما. ولو زوجه أخته الكبيرة برضاها جاز اتفاقاً، والوكيل من قبل المرأة إذا زوجها من أبيه أو ابنه لا يجوز في قول أبي حنيفة، وفي كل موضع لا ينفذ فعل الوكيل فالعقد موقوف على إجازة الموكل، وحكم الرسول كحكم الوكيل في جميع ما ذكرنا وضمانهما المهر صحيح. وإنكار المرسل والموكل الرسالة والوكالة بعد الضمان ولا بينة لا يسقط الضمان عنهما فيجب نصف المهر، وتوكيل المرأة المتزوجة بالتزويج إذا طلقت وانقضت عدتها صحيح كتوكيلة أن الخلاف إذا لم يكن أميراً فزوجه الوكيل أمة أو حرة عمياء أو مقطوعة اليدين أو رتقاء أو مفلوجة أو مجنونة، إما اتفاقاً وإما لما قيل قيده بذلك ليظهر الكفاءة فإنها من جانب النساء للرجال مستحسنة الوكالة عندهما .اهـ. فأفاد أنها معتبرة عندهما لا مطلقاً بل هنا فقط. وعن هذا قال في الحواشي السعدية : قوله «دلت المسألة الخ إن أراد دلت على اعتبارها في الوكالة عندهما فمسلم بالنظر إلى دليلها، وإن أراد مطلقاً اه. فمنوع ويؤيده ما قدمناه في أول الفصل عن البدائع قوله : (أو) عرف عملي الخ) أي عرف من حيث العمل والاستعمال لا من حيث اللفظ وبيانه أن العرف على نوعين لفظي نحو الدابة تقيد لفظاً بالفرس، ونحو المال بين العرب بالإبل، وعملي أي العزف من حيث العمل أي من حيث إن عمل الناس كذا كلبسهم الجديد يوم العيد وأمثاله كذا في العناية وفيه بحث لصاحب السعدية فراجعه .
And a witless woman, a woman with a crooked stature, a crippled woman, a woman with vaginal obstruction, a young girl who is not yet fit for intercourse, a kitabiyya, a woman whom he has sworn divorce against, or if he married him to a woman for more than her proper mahr, even with excessive disparity according to Imam Abu Hanifa, or married him to a man for less than her proper mahr likewise, or a woman from whom the principal had taken an oath of ila' or who was in the 'idda of the principal. The principle is that if the agent acts to a better option or his contrary action is not a real contrary, his contract is executed, as when he was ordered to marry a blind woman and he married a sighted one. Not included is if he was ordered to perform a corrupt marriage and he performed a valid one; rather it is not permissible due to the complete lack of agency for marriage. As for the 'idda after consummation and the establishment of lineage, it is not a ruling from him but from intercourse since it is not outright zina, contrary to his order for a corrupt sale; he may make a valid sale. Also not included is if he was authorized with a thousand, but the woman did not agree until the agent added a garment from his own wealth; then it is suspended on the husband's approval because it is harmful given the possibility that the garment is due or is lost before delivery, then she will claim its value from the husband, not the agent - as in al-Dhakhira - and the husband has the option. If he consummated before knowledge, and he chooses separation, it is like a defective marriage. Also not included is if he ordered a white woman and he married a black one, or vice versa, or from such a tribe and he married from another; then it is not effective. We restricted to the slave belonging to another because if he married him his own slave, even his mukataba - as in al-Muhit - then it is not effective due to accusation, as if he married him his daughter; if she is young, it is invalid by agreement, similarly his ward like his brother's young daughter. If she is adult, then likewise according to him (Abu Hanifa) contrary to the two. And if he married him his adult sister with her consent, it is valid by agreement. The agent from the woman's side, if he married her to his father or son, is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. In every place where the agent's action is not effective, the contract is suspended on the principal's ratification. The ruling of the messenger is like the ruling of the agent in all that we mentioned, and their guarantee of the mahr is valid. The denial of the principal and the agent of the message and agency after guarantee without evidence does not drop the guarantee from them, so half the mahr is due. The authorization of a married woman for marriage, if she divorces and her 'idda expires, is valid like his authorization. The disagreement when he is not an amir, then the agent married him a slave or free woman, blind, handless, with vaginal obstruction, paralyzed, or insane - either by agreement or because it was said he restricted it to manifest suitability, for it from the women's side for men, agency is considered commendable according to them. End. So it indicates that it is considered according to them not absolutely but only here. And about this, al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya said: 'His saying "the issue indicates" etc. If he meant it indicates its consideration in agency according to them, it is accepted with respect to its evidence, and if he meant absolutely, it is rejected.' And it is supported by what we presented earlier in the chapter from al-Bada'i': his saying '(or) 'urf 'amali' meaning custom from the perspective of practice and usage, not from the perspective of wording. Its explanation is that custom is of two types: verbal, like 'dabba' is verbally restricted to horse, and like wealth among Arabs to camels; and practical, meaning custom from the perspective of practice, i.e., people's practice like wearing new clothes on Eid and the like. This is from al-'Inaya, and there is a discussion by the author of al-Sa'diyya, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of rulings on the actions of a marriage agent (wakil) when he deviates from the principal's instructions. The text lists numerous scenarios: when the deviation is to a better option (e.g., marrying a sighted woman instead of a blind one), the contract is valid; but if the deviation is to a clearly inferior option (e.g., opposite tribe), it is not effective. It distinguishes between cases where the principal's order was for a fasid (corrupt) contract versus a valid one, and discusses the effect of the agent adding his own wealth. The passage also covers the status of the messenger (rasul) versus wakil, the guarantee of mahr, and the validity of a woman's agency after divorce. At the end, it defines 'urf 'amali (practical custom) as a type of custom based on habitual practice, as opposed to verbal custom. Throughout, the Hanafi school's reliance on istihsan and custom is evident, with disagreements between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn noted (e.g., on marrying the ward if adult). The relied-upon principle is that if the agent's action is to the benefit or not a real detriment, it is valid; otherwise, it is suspended on the principal's ratification.

Key Terms
الوكيل (al-wakil): The agent appointed by the principal (muwakkil) to conduct a marriage contract on his behalf.
خير (khayr): Better option; a deviation that benefits the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle, if a wakil is instructed to marry a blind woman but instead marries a sighted woman, the marriage is:
A) invalid
B) valid
C) suspended
D) void

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle: an agent's contract is valid if the deviation is to the better or not a true contrary; otherwise it is ineffective.

Nikah — Marriage
advanced
12 min
Specific Deviations: Own Wealth, Change of Attributes, and the Ward Dispute
Continues the discussion of the agent's actions and defines 'urf 'amali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the effect of the agent's deviation when adding his own wealth, changing ethnicity/tribe, marrying his own slave or relative, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on marrying an adult ward.

Core Idea
Adding personal wealth or changing key attributes renders the contract suspended; marrying one's own relative is generally invalid due to self-interest.

This passage extends the discussion to more nuanced scenarios where the agent deviates in ways that are potentially harmful or suspect. The text covers the agent adding a garment from his own wealth, changing the bride's color or tribe, marrying his own slave or daughter, and the disputed case of marrying an adult ward. Understanding these cases is key to mastering agency rules in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the scenario of agent adding own wealth
If the agent adds a garment from his own money to secure the woman's consent, the marriage is suspended on the husband's approval because it may cause harm (loss of garment).
The garment's value becomes a liability on the husband, not the agent.
2
Apply the rule to changes of color or tribe
If the agent was ordered to marry a white woman but marries a black one, or from a specific tribe but marries from another, the contract is not effective because these are material attributes that affect suitability.
Such changes are considered detrimental unless proven otherwise.
3
Understand the rulings on marrying one's own slave or relative
If the agent marries the principal to his own slave (even mukataba) or his daughter, the contract is invalid due to accusation of self-interest (tuhma). For a young ward (e.g., minor brother's daughter), it is invalid by agreement; for an adult ward, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa says invalid, Sahibayn say valid.
The dispute hinges on whether the agent's self-interest is presumed or rebuttable.
4
Examine the ruling on the woman's agent marrying her to his father/son
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this is not valid because of partiality. The opinion of the Sahibayn is not stated here, but later fatwa often follows them (valid).
In all cases where the agent's action is ineffective, the contract is suspended on the principal's ratification.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf for the ward dispute
If the agent marries the adult ward without her consent (according to Abu Hanifa) it is suspended; according to Sahibayn it is valid immediately unless she rejects. The practical difference is whether the marriage needs ratification.
The mufta bihi position often follows the Sahibayn for ease.

And a witless woman, a woman with a crooked stature, a crippled woman, a woman with vaginal obstruction, a young girl who is not yet fit for intercourse, a kitabiyya, a woman whom he has sworn divorce against, or if he married him to a woman for more than her proper mahr, even with excessive disparity according to Imam Abu Hanifa, or married him to a man for less than her proper mahr likewise, or a woman from whom the principal had taken an oath of ila' or who was in the 'idda of the principal. Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of rulings on the actions of a marriage agent (wakil) when he deviates from the principal's instructions. The text lists numerous scenarios: when the deviation is to a better option (e.g., marrying a sighted woman instead of a blind one), the contract is valid; but if the deviation is to a clearly inferior option (e.g., opposite tribe), it is not effective. It distinguishes between cases where the principal's order was for a fasid (corrupt) contract versus a valid one, and discusses the effect of the agent adding his own wealth. The passage also covers the status of the messenger (rasul) versus wakil, the guarantee of mahr, and the validity of a woman's agency after divorce. At the end, it defines 'urf 'amali (practical custom) as a type of custom based on habitual practice, as opposed to verbal custom. Throughout, the Hanafi school's reliance on istihsan and custom is evident, with disagreements between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn noted (e.g., on marrying the ward if adult). The relied-upon principle is that if the agent's action is to the benefit or not a real detriment, it is valid; otherwise, it is suspended on the principal's ratification.

Key Terms
التهمة (al-tuhma): Accusation or suspicion of self-interest that invalidates the agent's action.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a contract that is not effective until ratified by the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a woman's agent marries her to his own father, the marriage according to Imam Abu Hanifa is:
A) Valid and effective immediately
B) Invalid and void
C) Suspended on the woman's ratification
D) Valid if she consents

Key Takeaway
The agent's deviation involving self-interest, material changes, or added personal liability renders the contract suspended or ineffective until the principal ratifies.

Messenger's Ruling, Guarantee, and Practical Custom ('Urf 'Amali)
Continues the discussion of the agent's actions and defines 'urf 'amali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling that the messenger is like the agent, the guarantee of mahr, and define 'urf 'amali as a source of law in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The messenger binds the principal just as the agent does; practical custom ('urf 'amali) is a valid basis for legal rulings when no text exists.

This final portion of the passage ties together the rulings on the messenger (who merely conveys) vs. the agent, discusses the guarantee of mahr even if agency is denied, and concludes with a definition of practical custom ('urf 'amali). Understanding these concepts is essential for grasping the full scope of agency and the role of custom in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the rule that the messenger is like the agent
The text says 'وحكم الرسول كحكم الوكيل' meaning the messenger (who is sent to convey an offer) has the same ruling as the agent: his actions bind the principal.
This includes responsibility for the mahr.
2
Analyze the guarantee of mahr
If the messenger or agent denies his role after the marriage is consummated, but there is no evidence, they are still liable for half the mahr. This is because the principal can deny the agency, but the marriage itself is valid and mahr is due.
The guarantee is not dropped by mere denial.
3
Examine the case of a divorced woman's authorization
If a married woman authorizes someone to marry her after divorce and completion of 'idda, it is valid, similar to the principal's authorization.
This confirms that agency can be given by a woman who is eligible to marry.
4
Define 'urf 'amali
The text defines 'urf 'amali as custom based on practice (e.g., wearing new clothes on Eid), as opposed to verbal custom (e.g., restricting the word 'dabba' to horse).
This distinction is important for understanding how custom is used as a legal source.
5
Note the discussion in the commentaries
The author references al-'Inaya and al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya, stating that the consideration of 'urf in agency is not absolute but only in this context.
This shows the nuanced application of 'urf in Hanafi law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعقل زائل وشق مائل أو شلاء أو رتقاء أو صغيرة لا يجامع مثلها أو كتابية أو امرأة حلف بطلاقها أو زوجه امرأة على أكثر من مهر مثلها ولو بغبن فاحش عند الإمام، أو زوجها رجلاً بأقل من مهر مثلها كذلك أو امرأة كان الموكل آلي منها أو في عدة الموكل والأصل أن الوكيل إذا خالف إلى خير أو كان خلافه كلا خلاف نفذ عقده كما لو أمره بعمياء فزوجه بصيرة، وليس منه ما إذا أمره بالفاسد فزوجه صحيحاً بل لا يجوز لعدم الوكالة بالنكاح أصلاً. وأما العدة بعد الدخول فيه وثبوت النسب فليس حكماً له بل للوطء إذ لم يتمحض زنا بخلاف أمره بالبيع الفاسد له البيع صحيحاً وليس منه أيضاً ما إذا وكله بألف فلم ترض المرأة حتى زادها الوكيل ثوباً من مال نفسه فإنه موقوف على إجازة الزوج لكونه ضرراً على تقدير استحقاق الثوب أو هلاكه قبل التسليم فإنها ترجع بقيمته على الزوج لا الوكيل - كما في الذخيرة - وللزوج الخيار. وإذا دخل بها قبل العلم فإن اختار التفريق فكالنكاح الفساد. وليس منه أيضاً ما إذا أمره ببيضاء فزوجه سوداء أو على القلب أو من قبيلة كذا فزوجه من أخرى فإنه غير نافذ، وقيدنا بكون الأمة لغيره لأنه لو زوجه أمة نفسه ولو مكاتبته ـ كما في المحيط - فإنه لا ينفذ للتهمة كما لو زوجه بنته فإن كانت صغيرة لا يجوز اتفاقاً، وكذا موليته كبنت أخيه الصغيرة، وإن كانت كبيرة فكذلك عنده خلافاً لهما. ولو زوجه أخته الكبيرة برضاها جاز اتفاقاً، والوكيل من قبل المرأة إذا زوجها من أبيه أو ابنه لا يجوز في قول أبي حنيفة، وفي كل موضع لا ينفذ فعل الوكيل فالعقد موقوف على إجازة الموكل، وحكم الرسول كحكم الوكيل في جميع ما ذكرنا وضمانهما المهر صحيح. وإنكار المرسل والموكل الرسالة والوكالة بعد الضمان ولا بينة لا يسقط الضمان عنهما فيجب نصف المهر، وتوكيل المرأة المتزوجة بالتزويج إذا طلقت وانقضت عدتها صحيح كتوكيلة أن الخلاف إذا لم يكن أميراً فزوجه الوكيل أمة أو حرة عمياء أو مقطوعة اليدين أو رتقاء أو مفلوجة أو مجنونة، إما اتفاقاً وإما لما قيل قيده بذلك ليظهر الكفاءة فإنها من جانب النساء للرجال مستحسنة الوكالة عندهما .اهـ. فأفاد أنها معتبرة عندهما لا مطلقاً بل هنا فقط. وعن هذا قال في الحواشي السعدية : قوله «دلت المسألة الخ إن أراد دلت على اعتبارها في الوكالة عندهما فمسلم بالنظر إلى دليلها، وإن أراد مطلقاً اه. فمنوع ويؤيده ما قدمناه في أول الفصل عن البدائع قوله : (أو) عرف عملي الخ) أي عرف من حيث العمل والاستعمال لا من حيث اللفظ وبيانه أن العرف على نوعين لفظي نحو الدابة تقيد لفظاً بالفرس، ونحو المال بين العرب بالإبل، وعملي أي العزف من حيث العمل أي من حيث إن عمل الناس كذا كلبسهم الجديد يوم العيد وأمثاله كذا في العناية وفيه بحث لصاحب السعدية فراجعه .
And a witless woman, a woman with a crooked stature, a crippled woman, a woman with vaginal obstruction, a young girl who is not yet fit for intercourse, a kitabiyya, a woman whom he has sworn divorce against, or if he married him to a woman for more than her proper mahr, even with excessive disparity according to Imam Abu Hanifa, or married him to a man for less than her proper mahr likewise, or a woman from whom the principal had taken an oath of ila' or who was in the 'idda of the principal. The principle is that if the agent acts to a better option or his contrary action is not a real contrary, his contract is executed, as when he was ordered to marry a blind woman and he married a sighted one. Not included is if he was ordered to perform a corrupt marriage and he performed a valid one; rather it is not permissible due to the complete lack of agency for marriage. As for the 'idda after consummation and the establishment of lineage, it is not a ruling from him but from intercourse since it is not outright zina, contrary to his order for a corrupt sale; he may make a valid sale. Also not included is if he was authorized with a thousand, but the woman did not agree until the agent added a garment from his own wealth; then it is suspended on the husband's approval because it is harmful given the possibility that the garment is due or is lost before delivery, then she will claim its value from the husband, not the agent - as in al-Dhakhira - and the husband has the option. If he consummated before knowledge, and he chooses separation, it is like a defective marriage. Also not included is if he ordered a white woman and he married a black one, or vice versa, or from such a tribe and he married from another; then it is not effective. We restricted to the slave belonging to another because if he married him his own slave, even his mukataba - as in al-Muhit - then it is not effective due to accusation, as if he married him his daughter; if she is young, it is invalid by agreement, similarly his ward like his brother's young daughter. If she is adult, then likewise according to him (Abu Hanifa) contrary to the two. And if he married him his adult sister with her consent, it is valid by agreement. The agent from the woman's side, if he married her to his father or son, is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. In every place where the agent's action is not effective, the contract is suspended on the principal's ratification. The ruling of the messenger is like the ruling of the agent in all that we mentioned, and their guarantee of the mahr is valid. The denial of the principal and the agent of the message and agency after guarantee without evidence does not drop the guarantee from them, so half the mahr is due. The authorization of a married woman for marriage, if she divorces and her 'idda expires, is valid like his authorization. The disagreement when he is not an amir, then the agent married him a slave or free woman, blind, handless, with vaginal obstruction, paralyzed, or insane - either by agreement or because it was said he restricted it to manifest suitability, for it from the women's side for men, agency is considered commendable according to them. End. So it indicates that it is considered according to them not absolutely but only here. And about this, al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya said: 'His saying "the issue indicates" etc. If he meant it indicates its consideration in agency according to them, it is accepted with respect to its evidence, and if he meant absolutely, it is rejected.' And it is supported by what we presented earlier in the chapter from al-Bada'i': his saying '(or) 'urf 'amali' meaning custom from the perspective of practice and usage, not from the perspective of wording. Its explanation is that custom is of two types: verbal, like 'dabba' is verbally restricted to horse, and like wealth among Arabs to camels; and practical, meaning custom from the perspective of practice, i.e., people's practice like wearing new clothes on Eid and the like. This is from al-'Inaya, and there is a discussion by the author of al-Sa'diyya, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of rulings on the actions of a marriage agent (wakil) when he deviates from the principal's instructions. The text lists numerous scenarios: when the deviation is to a better option (e.g., marrying a sighted woman instead of a blind one), the contract is valid; but if the deviation is to a clearly inferior option (e.g., opposite tribe), it is not effective. It distinguishes between cases where the principal's order was for a fasid (corrupt) contract versus a valid one, and discusses the effect of the agent adding his own wealth. The passage also covers the status of the messenger (rasul) versus wakil, the guarantee of mahr, and the validity of a woman's agency after divorce. At the end, it defines 'urf 'amali (practical custom) as a type of custom based on habitual practice, as opposed to verbal custom. Throughout, the Hanafi school's reliance on istihsan and custom is evident, with disagreements between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn noted (e.g., on marrying the ward if adult). The relied-upon principle is that if the agent's action is to the benefit or not a real detriment, it is valid; otherwise, it is suspended on the principal's ratification.

Key Terms
الرسول (al-rasul): The messenger who conveys the offer but has no discretion; his ruling is like the agent.
العرف العملي (al-'urf al-'amali): Practical custom based on habitual actions of people, as opposed to verbal custom based on linguistic usage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, if a messenger denies his agency after the marriage is consummated and there is no evidence, the half mahr is:
A) Dropped because agency is disputed
B) Due from the messenger
C) Due from the principal (husband)
D) Waived because of doubt

Key Takeaway
The messenger's contract binds the principal; the mahr guarantee is not dropped by denial; and 'urf 'amali is a contextual source of law.

Marriage Valid Without Mahr; Minimum Mahr Ten Dirhams
Commentary proving validity and minimum mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that marriage is valid without specifying mahr and derive the minimum mahr of ten dirhams from the hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Marriage is valid without mentioning mahr; mahr is wajib and its minimum is ten dirhams.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains two key rulings: first, marriage is valid even if no mahr is specified; second, the minimum mahr is ten dirhams. The commentator uses the Quranic verse allowing divorce without specification to prove validity, and a hadith (strengthened by multiple chains) plus qiyas on the nisab of theft to fix the minimum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
State the two separate rulings: (1) marriage is valid without specifying mahr, (2) the minimum mahr is ten dirhams.
Note: These are distinct; the first deals with validity, the second with the amount if specified.
2
Locate the dalil for validity
Find the Quranic proof: verse 2:226 allows divorce without having specified a mahr, implying the marriage itself is valid.
Divorce presupposes a valid marriage.
3
Locate the dalil for minimum mahr
Find the hadith 'La mahr aqalla min ashara dirham' and note its weakness but strengthening through multiple chains; also the qiyas on nisab al-sariqa.
The hadith becomes hasan due to multiple chains; qiyas provides independent support.
4
Analyze the qiyas reasoning
Understand that mahr is a Shar'i right meant to honor the marriage, so it must be a significant amount; the nisab of theft (ten dirhams) is used as the standard of significance.
This is a qiyas jali based on the illa of significance (al-khatar).
5
Note the consensus on validity
The passage notes there is no disagreement about the validity of marriage without mahr among scholars.
Even Shafi'is agree? Actually, Shafi'is require mahr for validity; the passage might be referring to Hanafis. Check the key terms note: it says some scholars disagree. So perhaps the claim of no khilaf is within Hanafi school or among the cited authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (صح) النكاح بلا ذكره لأن النكاح عقد انضمام وازدواج لغة فيتم بالزوجين، ثم المهر واجب شرعاً إبانة لشرف المحل فلا يحتاج إلى ذكره لصحة النكاح، وكذا إذا تزوجها بشرط أن لا مهر لها لما بيناه واستدل له في غاية البيان بقوله تعالى ولا جناح عليكم إن طلقتم النساء ما لم تمسوهن أو تفرضوا لهن فريضة ومتعوهن [البقرة: ٢٢٦] فقد حكم بصحة الطلاق مع عدم التسمية ولا يكون الطلاق إلا في النكاح الصحيح، فعلم أن ترك التسمية لا يمنع صحة النكاح. وذكر الأكمل والكمال أنه لا خلاف لأحد في صحته بلا ذكر المهر قوله : (وأقله عشرة دراهم) أي أقل المهر شرعاً للحديث «لا مهر أقل من عشرة دراهم» وهو وإن كان ضعيفاً فقد تعددت طرقه والمنقول في الأصول أن الضعيف إذا تعددت طرقه فإنه يصير حسناً إذا كان ضعفه بغير الفسق، ولأنه حق الشرع وجوباً إظهاراً لشرف المحل فيقدر بماله خطر وهو العشرة استدلالاً بنصاب السرقة.
His statement: (Valid) marriage without mentioning it because marriage is a contract of union and pairing linguistically, so it is completed by the spouses. Then the mahr is obligatory by law, as a mark of honor for the position, so it does not need to be mentioned for the validity of marriage. Similarly, if he marries her with the condition that she has no mahr, as we have explained. And it is argued in Ghayat al-Bayan by His statement 'And there is no sin upon you if you divorce women while you have not touched them or specified for them an obligation' [2:226]; He ruled the validity of divorce without specification, and divorce only occurs in a valid marriage, so it is known that leaving out specification does not prevent the validity of marriage. Al-Akmal and al-Kamal mentioned that there is no disagreement about its validity without mentioning mahr. His statement: (and its minimum is ten dirhams) meaning the minimum mahr legally, due to the hadith 'No mahr less than ten dirhams' — and although it is weak, its chains are numerous, and it is transmitted in usul that a weak hadith when its chains are numerous becomes hasan if its weakness is not due to immorality. And because it is a right of the Shari'ah obligatory as a demonstration of the honor of the position, so it is measured by something of value, which is ten, by analogy to the nisab of theft.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author explains the ruling that marriage is valid without specifying the dower (mahr). The reason is that the essence of marriage is a union between spouses, and mahr is an obligatory right imposed by Shari'ah to honor the position of marriage, not a condition for its validity. The commentator cites the Quranic verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:226) which permits divorce without having specified a mahr, implying that the marriage itself is valid without it. He notes that there is consensus among scholars on this point. Then he addresses the minimum mahr, which is ten dirhams. This is established by a hadith, 'No mahr less than ten dirhams,' which although weak in isolation, is strengthened by multiple chains, becoming hasan according to usul al-fiqh. Additionally, the commentator provides a rational analogy (qiyas): since mahr is a right of Shari'ah meant to honor the station of marriage, it must be a significant amount, and the Shar'i standard for significance is the nisab of theft, which is ten dirhams.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife as an obligatory right in marriage, imposed by Shari'ah to honor the station of marriage.
عشرة دراهم (asharat dirham): The minimum amount of mahr in Hanafi fiqh, set at ten dirhams based on hadith and analogy to the nisab of theft.
نصاب السرقة (nisab al-sariqah): The minimum threshold for theft which incurs the hadd punishment, set at ten dirhams. Used here analogically to determine the minimum mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence used to set the minimum mahr at ten dirhams?
A) Only the Quranic verse 2:226
B) Only the hadith 'لا مهر أقل من عشرة دراهم'
C) The hadith and qiyas on nisab of theft
D) Consensus of all scholars

Key Takeaway
Marriage is valid without mentioning mahr; the minimum mahr is ten dirhams, established by hadith and qiyas.

What Qualifies as the Minimum Mahr
Expands the types of property acceptable as minimum mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of property qualify as the minimum mahr (ten dirhams equivalent) and explain why debt is considered property for mahr but not for zakat.

Core Idea
The minimum mahr can be uncoined silver, debt, blood money, or a defect—anything worth ten dirhams.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands the scope of the minimum mahr beyond minted coins. The author clarifies that 'dirhams' in the matn includes uncoined silver (tibr), commodities of equal value, debts owed to the husband, blood money (diyah), and even the defect of a slave purchased from the wife. This reflects the Hanafi principle that mahr is a contractual exchange, and any property of value suffices. Interestingly, the same debt is not considered property for zakat or oaths, highlighting the context-dependent nature of legal concepts in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the minimum mahr: ten dirhams or equivalent value.
2
Recognize the expansion
The term 'dirhams' is general; it includes coined, uncoined, and commodities.
Compare with theft nisab where only coined dirhams count.
3
Analyze debt as mahr
Debt is considered property for mahr; the wife can claim from husband or debtor.
Quran 4:24 cited.
4
Note the anomaly
Debt is not property for zakat or oaths; explain why.
Context matters.
5
Consider other properties
Blood money and defect of a slave also qualify.
Value must be at least ten dirhams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أطلق الدراهم فشمل المصكوك وغيره، فلو سمى عشرة تبراً أو عرضاً قيمته عشرة تبراً لا مضروبة صح، وإنما تشترط المصكوكة في نصاب السرقة للقطع تقليلاً لوجود الحد. وشمل الدين والعين فلو تزوجها على عشرة دين له على فلان صحت التسمية لأن الدين ،مال، فإن شاءت أخذته الزوج وإن شاءت ممن عليه الدين كذا في المحيط. زاد في الخانية : ويؤاخذ الزوح حتى يوكلها بقبض الدين من المديون اهـ. فقد جعلوا الدين مالاً هنا وأدخلوه تحت قوله تعالى إن تبتغوا بأموالكم ﴾ [النساء : ٢٤] ولم يجعلوه مالاً في الزكاة فلم يجز الدين عن العين ولا في الأيمان، فلو حلف لا مال له وله دين على موسر لا يحنث. وشمل الدية أيضاً ولذا قال في الظهيرية : ولو تزوجها على ما وجب له من الدية على عاقلتها فلا شيء لها على عاقلتها لأنها مؤدية عنهم. وفي المحيط : لو تزوجها على عيب عبد اشتراه منها جاز لأنها لما تزوجت على عيبه صارت مقرة بحصة العيب لأن النكاح لا بد له من مهر فيكون نكاحاً بمال، فإن كانت قيمة العيب عشرة فهو مهرها وإلا يكمل عشرة ا هـ . ومراد المصنف أن أقله عشرة أو ما يقوم مقامها بالقيمة، واختلف في وقت القيمة فظاهر الرواية أن الاعتبار وقت العقد ولا اعتبار ليوم القبض، فلو كانت قيمته يوم العقد عشرة وصارت يوم التسليم ثمانية فليس لها إلا هو، ولو كان على عكسه لها العرض المسمى ودرهمان ولا فرق في ذلك بين الثوب والمكيل والموزون لأن ما جعل مهراً لم يتغير في نفسه وإنما التغيير في رغبات الناس. كذا في البدائع . وفي المحيط : ولو تزوجها على ثوب وقيمته عشرة فقبضته وقيمته عشرون وطلقها قبل الدخول والخلوة والثوب مستهلك ردت عشرة لأنه إنما دخل في ضمانها بالقبض فتعتبر قيمته يوم القبض ا هـ . فالحاصل أن الاعتبار ليوم العقد في حق التسمية وليوم القبض في حق دخوله في ضمانها
He said 'dirhams' in an absolute sense, so it includes coined and other. If he mentions ten uncoined silver or a commodity worth ten uncoined without being minted, it is valid. The condition of being coined is required only in the nisab of theft to limit the occurrence of the hadd. And it includes debt and property: if he marries her on a debt of ten owed to him by someone, the specification is valid because debt is property. She may take it from the husband or from the debtor; thus in al-Muhit. Additional in al-Khaniyyah: The husband is held until he appoints her to collect the debt from the debtor. So they considered debt as property here and included it under His statement 'when you seek with your properties' [4:24], but they did not consider it property in zakat, so debt does not substitute for cash, nor in oaths: if one swears he has no property and has a debt owed by a wealthy person, he does not break the oath. And it also includes blood money (diyah). Hence it is said in al-Zahiyyah: If he marries her on what is owed to him as blood money from his 'aqilah, she has nothing against the 'aqilah because they are paying on his behalf. And in al-Muhit: If he marries her on the defect of a slave he bought from her, it is valid, because when she marries based on its defect, she acknowledges the portion of the defect, because marriage must have a mahr, so it is a marriage for property. If the value of the defect is ten, it is her mahr; otherwise, he completes ten. The intent of the author is that its minimum is ten or what stands in place of it by value. They differed regarding the time of valuation: according to zahir al-riwayah, consideration is at the time of contract, not the day of delivery. So if its value on contract day was ten and became eight on delivery, she only gets that item; and if the opposite, she gets the named commodity and two dirhams. There is no difference in this between cloth and measurable/weighable items, because what is made a mahr does not change in itself; rather the change is in people's desires. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And in al-Muhit: If he marries her on a garment worth ten, she takes possession and its value is twenty, and he divorces before consummation and seclusion, and the garment is consumed, she returns ten because it entered her guarantee upon possession, so its value is considered on the day of possession. The conclusion is that the consideration is on the day of contract regarding the specification, and on the day of possession regarding its entry into her guarantee.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the scope of the minimum mahr. The author first clarifies that the term 'dirhams' in the matn is general, including both minted coins and uncoined silver (tibr) as well as commodities (ard) that are equivalent in value. The distinction from the nisab of theft is noted: for theft, only coined dirhams are considered to limit the application of hadd punishment. Then the passage expands to include debts as valid mahr. If the husband owes a debt to someone else, he can assign that debt as mahr, and the wife can claim it from either the husband or the debtor. The Quranic verse (4:24) is invoked as the basis for considering debt as property in this context, though interestingly the Hanafi School does not consider debt as property for zakat or oaths. Blood money (diyah) also qualifies as mahr. A unique case: if a man marries a woman and makes the mahr the defect of a slave he purchased from her, it is valid; the value of the defect constitutes the mahr. Finally, the passage discusses the time for valuing non-monetary mahr. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that valuation is at the time of contract. However, if the wife takes possession and the item increases in value, then if she consumes it and is divorced before consummation, she must return the value at the time of possession (because it was in her guarantee). So there are two points: contract time for specification, possession time for guarantee. Examples are provided.

Key Terms
تبر (tibr): Uncoined silver, acceptable as mahr if its value equals ten dirhams.
دين (dayn): A debt owed to the husband can be assigned as mahr; it is considered property in this context.
القيمة (al-qimah): The value of non-monetary mahr; considered at contract time for specification and at possession for guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is a valid type of mahr?
A) Only coined silver dirhams
B) Uncoined silver or goods worth ten dirhams
C) A promise to pay in the future
D) Only cash

Key Takeaway
The minimum mahr is ten dirhams or its equivalent in value, and it can be satisfied by various forms of property including uncoined silver, debt, blood money, and even a defect in a slave.

Valuation Timing for Non-Monetary Mahr
Details valuation timing for non-monetary mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two valuation points for non-monetary mahr (contract for specification, possession for guarantee) and apply them to scenarios of price fluctuation.

Core Idea
The value of a non-monetary mahr is fixed at contract time for its specification, but if the item is consumed after possession, the guarantee value is at possession.

This passage addresses a key question: when do we determine the value of a mahr that is not cash? The author explains that according to the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah), the valuation for the purpose of meeting the minimum (specification) is at the time of the contract. However, if the wife takes possession and the item is later consumed or lost, the value at the time of possession is used to determine her liability. This dual timing prevents injustice due to market fluctuations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contexts
Specification (tazwīj) and guarantee (ḍamān).
2
Rule for specification
Value at contract time; changes later do not affect the specification.
Example: value drops from 10 to 8, wife still gets the item.
3
Rule for guarantee
If consumed after possession, value at possession time used for return.
Example: value rises to 20, wife returns 10 if consumed.
4
Apply to different items
Same rule applies to cloth, measured, and weighed items; only market desire changes.
5
Conclude
Two valuation times serve different legal purposes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أطلق الدراهم فشمل المصكوك وغيره، فلو سمى عشرة تبراً أو عرضاً قيمته عشرة تبراً لا مضروبة صح، وإنما تشترط المصكوكة في نصاب السرقة للقطع تقليلاً لوجود الحد. وشمل الدين والعين فلو تزوجها على عشرة دين له على فلان صحت التسمية لأن الدين ،مال، فإن شاءت أخذته الزوج وإن شاءت ممن عليه الدين كذا في المحيط. زاد في الخانية : ويؤاخذ الزوح حتى يوكلها بقبض الدين من المديون اهـ. فقد جعلوا الدين مالاً هنا وأدخلوه تحت قوله تعالى إن تبتغوا بأموالكم ﴾ [النساء : ٢٤] ولم يجعلوه مالاً في الزكاة فلم يجز الدين عن العين ولا في الأيمان، فلو حلف لا مال له وله دين على موسر لا يحنث. وشمل الدية أيضاً ولذا قال في الظهيرية : ولو تزوجها على ما وجب له من الدية على عاقلتها فلا شيء لها على عاقلتها لأنها مؤدية عنهم. وفي المحيط : لو تزوجها على عيب عبد اشتراه منها جاز لأنها لما تزوجت على عيبه صارت مقرة بحصة العيب لأن النكاح لا بد له من مهر فيكون نكاحاً بمال، فإن كانت قيمة العيب عشرة فهو مهرها وإلا يكمل عشرة ا هـ . ومراد المصنف أن أقله عشرة أو ما يقوم مقامها بالقيمة، واختلف في وقت القيمة فظاهر الرواية أن الاعتبار وقت العقد ولا اعتبار ليوم القبض، فلو كانت قيمته يوم العقد عشرة وصارت يوم التسليم ثمانية فليس لها إلا هو، ولو كان على عكسه لها العرض المسمى ودرهمان ولا فرق في ذلك بين الثوب والمكيل والموزون لأن ما جعل مهراً لم يتغير في نفسه وإنما التغيير في رغبات الناس. كذا في البدائع . وفي المحيط : ولو تزوجها على ثوب وقيمته عشرة فقبضته وقيمته عشرون وطلقها قبل الدخول والخلوة والثوب مستهلك ردت عشرة لأنه إنما دخل في ضمانها بالقبض فتعتبر قيمته يوم القبض ا هـ . فالحاصل أن الاعتبار ليوم العقد في حق التسمية وليوم القبض في حق دخوله في ضمانها
He said 'dirhams' in an absolute sense, so it includes coined and other. If he mentions ten uncoined silver or a commodity worth ten uncoined without being minted, it is valid. The condition of being coined is required only in the nisab of theft to limit the occurrence of the hadd. And it includes debt and property: if he marries her on a debt of ten owed to him by someone, the specification is valid because debt is property. She may take it from the husband or from the debtor; thus in al-Muhit. Additional in al-Khaniyyah: The husband is held until he appoints her to collect the debt from the debtor. So they considered debt as property here and included it under His statement 'when you seek with your properties' [4:24], but they did not consider it property in zakat, so debt does not substitute for cash, nor in oaths: if one swears he has no property and has a debt owed by a wealthy person, he does not break the oath. And it also includes blood money (diyah). Hence it is said in al-Zahiyyah: If he marries her on what is owed to him as blood money from his 'aqilah, she has nothing against the 'aqilah because they are paying on his behalf. And in al-Muhit: If he marries her on the defect of a slave he bought from her, it is valid, because when she marries based on its defect, she acknowledges the portion of the defect, because marriage must have a mahr, so it is a marriage for property. If the value of the defect is ten, it is her mahr; otherwise, he completes ten. The intent of the author is that its minimum is ten or what stands in place of it by value. They differed regarding the time of valuation: according to zahir al-riwayah, consideration is at the time of contract, not the day of delivery. So if its value on contract day was ten and became eight on delivery, she only gets that item; and if the opposite, she gets the named commodity and two dirhams. There is no difference in this between cloth and measurable/weighable items, because what is made a mahr does not change in itself; rather the change is in people's desires. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And in al-Muhit: If he marries her on a garment worth ten, she takes possession and its value is twenty, and he divorces before consummation and seclusion, and the garment is consumed, she returns ten because it entered her guarantee upon possession, so its value is considered on the day of possession. The conclusion is that the consideration is on the day of contract regarding the specification, and on the day of possession regarding its entry into her guarantee.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the scope of the minimum mahr. The author first clarifies that the term 'dirhams' in the matn is general, including both minted coins and uncoined silver (tibr) as well as commodities (ard) that are equivalent in value. The distinction from the nisab of theft is noted: for theft, only coined dirhams are considered to limit the application of hadd punishment. Then the passage expands to include debts as valid mahr. If the husband owes a debt to someone else, he can assign that debt as mahr, and the wife can claim it from either the husband or the debtor. The Quranic verse (4:24) is invoked as the basis for considering debt as property in this context, though interestingly the Hanafi School does not consider debt as property for zakat or oaths. Blood money (diyah) also qualifies as mahr. A unique case: if a man marries a woman and makes the mahr the defect of a slave he purchased from her, it is valid; the value of the defect constitutes the mahr. Finally, the passage discusses the time for valuing non-monetary mahr. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that valuation is at the time of contract. However, if the wife takes possession and the item increases in value, then if she consumes it and is divorced before consummation, she must return the value at the time of possession (because it was in her guarantee). So there are two points: contract time for specification, possession time for guarantee. Examples are provided.

Key Terms
تبر (tibr): Uncoined silver, acceptable as mahr if its value equals ten dirhams.
دين (dayn): A debt owed to the husband can be assigned as mahr; it is considered property in this context.
القيمة (al-qimah): The value of non-monetary mahr; considered at contract time for specification and at possession for guarantee.
قبض (qabd): Possession; the moment when the wife takes the mahr into her control, triggering guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

At what time is the value of a non-monetary mahr considered for the purpose of specification?
A) At the time of delivery
B) At the time of contract
C) At the time of divorce
D) At the time of possession

Key Takeaway
Valuation of non-monetary mahr is at contract time for specification and at possession time for guarantee.

Minimum Mahr and Time of Valuation
States the minimum mahr and the time for valuation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum mahr according to the Hanafi school and determine the correct time of valuation for mahr items.

Core Idea
The minimum mahr is ten dirhams or its equivalent, and valuation for specification is at the contract, not delivery.

The mahr is a mandatory provision in marriage, but what constitutes a valid mahr and when its value is assessed can be nuanced. In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi ruling on the minimum mahr, the types of property that can serve as mahr, and the critical distinction between valuation for specifying the mahr and valuation for liability after possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the minimum mahr
Note that the Hanafi school sets a minimum of ten dirhams or its equivalent in value. This applies to any form of property, whether minted coins, unminted metal (tibr), goods, or debts.
This minimum is based on the practice of the Companions and is intended to prevent hardship.
2
Recognize acceptable forms of mahr
The passage lists several valid forms: unminted silver (tibr), goods ('arad), debts owed to the husband, and even blood money (diyah) owed by the 'aqila. The key is that the item must have monetary value.
3
Distinguish valuation times
For the purpose of specifying the mahr, the value is assessed at the time of the contract. If the item's value changes later, the wife does not gain or lose from that change. However, if the husband has taken possession and the item is consumed, the liability is based on the value at the time of possession.
This distinction applies to all types of mahr property, whether cloth, measured, or weighed.
4
Apply the rulings to a scenario
Consider a man who marries a woman and gives her a garment worth 10 dirhams at the contract. At possession, it is worth 8 dirhams. If he divorces her before consummation, she keeps the garment as is. If it had increased to 12 dirhams, she would take the garment plus 2 dirhams, because the valuation for specification is at contract.

If he names ten ingots or an item worth ten ingots, not minted, it is valid. Minted coins are only required for the nisab of theft to minimize the occurrence of the hadd penalty. Commentary
This passage presents rulings on the minimum mahr and the time for valuation. It opens by stating that the minimum mahr is ten dirhams or its equivalent in value, whether in unminted silver (tibr) or goods. Minted coins are only required for the nisab of theft to restrict the application of the hadd punishment. The passage then extends the scope of acceptable mahr to include debts owed to the husband by a third party, and even blood money owed by the 'aqila. It cites various sources like al-Muhit, al-Khaniyya, and al-Zahiriyya to show the consensus on these points. The ruling on valuation time is clarified: the value is assessed at the time of the contract for the purpose of specifying the mahr, but if the husband takes possession and then the item is consumed or destroyed, the liability is based on the value at the time of possession. This distinction is crucial for understanding the rights of the wife and the obligations of the husband.

تبر (tibr): Unminted gold or silver; raw metal
عرض ('arad): Goods or merchandise other than cash
قيمة (qimah): Monetary value or market price

Mahr as Debt: Distinction Between Debt on Wife and Third Party
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr as debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the legal effects of mahr when specified as a debt on the wife versus a debt on a third party, and apply the Hanafi ruling to scenarios of co-creditors, set-off, and divorce before consummation.

Core Idea
When mahr is a debt on the wife, it cancels the specific debt; when on a third party, it becomes a like-debt on the husband’s dhimmah.

The mahr in a marriage contract has a dual nature: it is both a compensation (iwad) for the marriage and a gift (sila). This dual nature leads to different rulings when the mahr is specified as a debt. If the debt is owed by the wife herself, the marriage attaches to that specific debt, effecting a set-off. If the debt is owed by a third party (e.g., the ‘aqila), the marriage does not transfer that specific debt but creates a like debt in the husband’s dhimmah. This distinction, drawn from al-Dhakhira, has practical consequences for co-creditors, the wife’s options, and zakat upon divorce before consummation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios of mahr as debt
Note that the source distinguishes between (1) mahr being a debt owed by the wife herself, and (2) mahr being a debt owed by a third party (e.g., the ‘aqila).
The legal effect is different in each case.
2
Understand the ‘illa: dual nature of mahr
The mahr is both compensation (iwad) and gift (sila). This dual nature causes it to attach to the specific debt when the debt is on the wife (gift aspect predominates) and to a like debt when on a third party (compensation aspect predominates because transferring a specific debt from a non-liable person is invalid).
This ‘illa is derived from qiyas khafi.
3
Apply to co-creditor scenario
If one of two creditors marries the woman for his share of a debt she owes them, the silent creditor cannot claim part of that share because the mahr attached specifically to that debt (set-off). If the debt is on a third party, the silent creditor may take half from the husband because it attaches to a like debt in the husband’s dhimmah.
This illustrates the practical thamarah al-khilaf.
4
Apply to divorce before consummation after payment of mahr
If the husband paid the mahr (specific dirhams) then divorced before consummation, the wife returns only the like (mithl) of half the mahr, not the specific coins. This is because the mahr when paid becomes like a debt on the wife, and return is in like, not specific.
This affects zakat: the wife must pay zakat on the half she keeps, as it is like a new debt.
5
Reconcile apparent contradiction with al-Zahiriyya
Al-Dhakhira states that when the debt is on a third party, the wife may choose to take from the husband or from the third party. This seems to contradict the general rule. The reconciliation is that al-Dhakhira’s scenario includes an explicit order from the husband to the wife to collect the debt, making her his agent; otherwise, she cannot claim from the third party directly.
Thus the ruling in al-Zahiriyya (without order) aligns with the general principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة النكاح إذا أضيف إلى دراهم عين لا يتعلق بعينها وإنما يتعلق بمثلها ديناً في الذمة، وإذا أضيف إلى دراهم دين في ذمة المرأة تتعلق بعينها ولا يتعلق بمثلها ديناً في الذمة لأن المهر عوض من وجه من حيث إنه ملك بمقابلة شيء صلة من وجه من حيث إنه لا مالية لما يقابله من كل وجه حتى يجب الحيوان ديناً في الذمة في النكاح والدراهم تتعين في الصلات لا في المعاوضات فعلمنا بحقيقة المعاوضة إذا أضيف إلى الدراهم العين فتعلق بمثلها، وعلمنا بمعنى الصلة إذا أضيف إلى الدين فتعلق بعينها عملاً بالشبهين. وفائدة الأول لو تزوجها أحد الدائنين على حصته من دين لهما عليها فليس للساكت مشاركته متبرع. هذا ما ظهر لي لكن يخالف هذا ما نذكره قريباً عن الذخيرة من أن الدين إذا كان على غير المرأة فالنكاح لا يتعلق بعين ذلك الدين وإنما يتعلق بمثله . قوله : (وفائدة الأول) أقول : تصرف في عبارة الذخيرة بما ليس فيها فإن الذي في الذخيرة لتعلقه بعين الحصة وفائدة الثاني لو تزوجها أحدهما على دراهم مطلقة بقدر حصته من الدين وصار قصاصاً فلشريكه أن يأخذ منه نصفها لتعلقه بمثلها والدين إذا كان على غير المرأة فهو كالعين يتعلق النكاح بمثله لأنه لو تعلق بالعين لكان تمليك الدين من غير من عليه الدين بخلاف ما إذا كان عليها وفائدته أنها مخيرة إن شاءت أخذت من الزوج وإن شاءت من العاقلة اهـ . والأخير مخالف لما قدمناه عن الظهيرية ويمكن التوفيق بأن ما في الذخيرة مصور بأنه تزوجها على أرش له على عاقلتها وأمرها بقبض ذلك، وما في الظهيرية خال عن الأمر بالقبض، وقد علم أنه لو تزوجها على دراهم وأشار إليها فله إمساكها ودفع مثلها، ولو دفع الدراهم إليها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول لا يتعين عليها رد عين نصفها وإنما يتعين رد مثلها كما في جامع الفصولين وفرع عليه ما إذا كان المهر ألفاً دفعه إليها وحال الحول ووجبت الزكاة عليها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول فإنه لا يسقط عنها زكاة النصف لأنه لما لم يتعين رد العين كان بمنزلة دين حادث ا هـ
In al-Dhakhira: Marriage, when added to specific dirhams, does not attach to the specific dirhams but to their like as a debt in the dhimmah. But when added to dirhams that are a debt in the wife's dhimmah, it attaches to the specific debt and not to its like as a debt in the dhimmah, because the dower is a compensation in one respect (since it is owned in exchange for something) and a gift in another respect (since what it corresponds to has no complete monetary value), even to the extent that animals become a debt in the dhimmah in marriage, and dirhams become specific in gifts not in exchanges. Thus we know from the reality of exchange: when added to specific dirhams, it attaches to their like; and from the meaning of a gift: when added to a debt, it attaches to the specific debt, acting on both similarities. The benefit of the first: if one of two creditors marries her for his share of a debt owed to both of them, the silent partner cannot participate in it as a donation. This is what appears to me, but this contradicts what we will soon mention from al-Dhakhira, that if the debt is on someone other than the wife, marriage does not attach to that specific debt but to its like. He commented on 'the benefit of the first' by saying: He has tampered with the text of al-Dhakhira, for what is in al-Dhakhira is that it attaches to the specific share. The benefit of the second: if one of them marries her for unspecified dirhams equal to his share of the debt and it becomes a set-off, his partner may take half from him because it attaches to its like. And a debt on someone other than the wife is like a specific item: marriage attaches to its like, because if it attached to the specific debt, it would be transferring a debt from someone not liable, unlike when it is on her. Its benefit is that she may choose to take from the husband or from the 'aqila. The latter contradicts what we presented from al-Zahiriyya. Reconciliation is possible: what is in al-Dhakhira is the case where he marries her for a claim he has on her 'aqila and orders her to collect it, while al-Zahiriyya lacks the order to collect. And it is known that if he marries her for dirhams and points to them, he may keep them and pay their like. And if he pays the dirhams to her then divorces her before consummation, she is not obligated to return the specific half but only its like, as in Jami' al-Fusulayn. A branch: if the mahr was a thousand paid to her, a year passes and zakat becomes due on her, then he divorces her before consummation, the zakat on half is not waived because since the return of the specific item is not required, it is like a new debt.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the legal nature of the mahr when it is specified as a debt. The discussion is from al-Dhakhira and later commentaries. It distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) when the mahr is a debt owed by the wife herself, and (2) when it is a debt owed by a third party (like the 'aqila). In the first case, the marriage contract attaches to the specific debt, meaning that if the wife is a debtor, the mahr becomes a set-off against her debt. In the second case, it attaches only to a like amount in the dhimmah of the husband, because transferring a debt from a non-liable person is invalid. The passage then examines the implications of this distinction for co-creditors and the wife's options. It also attempts to reconcile apparent contradictions between al-Dhakhira and al-Zahiriyya by noting that the latter's scenario lacks an explicit order to collect the debt. The ruling that upon divorce before consummation, the wife returns only the like of the paid mahr, not the specific coins, is also discussed, with implications for zakat.

Key Terms
تعلق بعينها (ta'allaqa bi 'ayniha): Attaches to the specific debt itself (the very same item or right)
تعلق بمثلها (ta'allaqa bi mithliha): Attaches to a like amount or similar item in the dhimmah, not the specific debt
قصاص (qisas): Set-off or mutual cancellation of debts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view (al-Dhakhira), if a man marries a woman for a debt owed by her father (a third party), what is the legal effect?
A) The marriage attaches to that specific debt, and the father’s debt is transferred to the husband.
B) The marriage attaches to a like amount in the husband’s dhimmah; the wife may also claim from the father if the husband authorized her.
C) The marriage is invalid because mahr cannot be a debt on a third party.
D) The wife must give up her claim against the father in favor of the husband.

Key Takeaway
The dual nature of mahr as compensation and gift determines whether it attaches to a specific debt (if on the wife) or a like debt (if on a third party), affecting co-creditors, set-off, and zakat upon divorce.

Deferring the Mahr to a Known or Unknown Time
Ruling on deferring mahr to an indefinite future time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deferring mahr to a known or unknown time and apply the condition of custom.

Core Idea
Deferring the mahr to an indefinite time like harvest is valid if understood by custom.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a practical issue: can a husband delay the mahr to an unspecified future time? The Hanafi school, considering custom, permits it. We'll explore the ruling and a case where the husband promises to pay as he can.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is deferring the mahr to a future time. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih), even if the time is unknown like harvest.
This is the correct (sahih) position in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the condition of custom
An unknown time must be understandable by custom (urf). Examples given are harvest (al-hisad) and threshing (al-diyas), which are customary agricultural seasons.
Custom gives meaning to indefinite times.
3
Apply the example from the text
If a man marries for 1000 dirhams on the condition that he pays what becomes easy for him and the remainder after a year, the entire 1000 is due after one year. However, if the woman proves that something or all of it became easy for him, she can take it immediately.
The burden of proof is on the woman to show the husband's ability to pay.
4
Note the procedural nuance
The husband's promise to pay 'as it becomes easy' does not make the mahr conditional; it only affects the timing of payment. The wife can demand payment if she proves his ability.
This protects the wife's right without requiring a fixed term.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أحكام المهر أنه يصبح تأجيله إلى وقت مجهول كالحصاد والدياس وهو الصحيح، ولو تزوجها بألف درهم على أن ينقد ما تيسر له والبقية إلى سنة كان الألف كله إلى سنة إلا أن تقيم المرأة البينة أنه تیسر له منها شيء أو كله فتأخده. كذا في الظهيرية .
Among the rulings of mahr is that deferring it to an unknown time, like harvest and threshing, is valid; that is the correct view. And if he marries her for one thousand dirhams on condition that he pays whatever becomes easy for him and the remainder after a year, the entire thousand is due after a year, unless the woman proves that something or all of it became easy for him, then she takes it. Thus in al-Zahiriyya.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on deferring the mahr. It states that it is valid to defer the mahr to an unknown future time, such as the harvest season or threshing time. This is the correct (sahih) position in the Hanafi school. It then gives an example: if a man marries a woman for one thousand dirhams on the condition that he pays whatever becomes easy for him and the remainder after a year, the entire amount is due after one year, unless the woman proves that he had the means to pay earlier, in which case she can demand it. This ruling is from al-Zahiriyya. The lesson emphasizes flexibility in determining the payment time of mahr, allowing custom and mutual agreement.

Key Terms
تأجيل (ta'jil): Deferring payment of the mahr to a future date
الحصاد والدياس (al-hisad wa al-diyas): Harvest and threshing (agricultural seasons used as examples of indefinite times)

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, the time must be known

D) Only if the wife agrees to a known time

Key Takeaway
Deferring the mahr to an indefinite time is valid in Hanafi fiqh if the time is understood by custom, as affirmed by al-Bahr al-Raiq.
