Mahr Specified as a Debt: Attachment and Intra-Hanafi Differences
Commentary on mahr as debt with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute regarding a joint creditor's right to recover from the husband when mahr is set as a debt, and identify the practical consequences of each view.

Core Idea
Whether a joint creditor can claim from the husband depends on whether the marriage attaches to the specific share or to its like.

When a woman owes a debt to two men, and one of them marries her setting his share of the debt as mahr, a key intra-Hanafi dispute arises: can the other creditor follow the husband to recover his share? The answer hinges on whether the marriage attaches to the specific property (ayn) or to its equivalent (mithl). This lesson unpacks the two positions, their underlying reasoning, and the reconciliation attempted by later scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and dispute
Read the opening lines: a woman owes a debt to two men; one marries her for his share. The legal question is whether the other creditor can take half from the husband (partner can follow).
The dispute is between Abu Yusuf (two narrations), Muhammad, and al-Halwani.
2
Understand the two positions on attachment
One position: marriage attaches to the specific share (ayn) of the debt, so the partner cannot follow because the husband only owns his share. Another: marriage attaches to the like (mithl) of the debt, so the partner can recover from the husband as the mahr is an absolute amount.
The text contrasts 'talluq bi 'ayn al-hissah' vs 'talluq bi mithliha'.
3
Analyze the reconciliation attempt
The author reconciles conflicting reports from al-Dhakhira and al-Zahiriyya by noting the presence or absence of an order to collect from the third party. If the husband ordered collection, the partner may not follow; if no order, he may.
This shows the importance of procedural details in resolving apparent contradictions.
4
Apply the principle to related sub-rulings
The passage extends the mithl principle: if husband pays mahr and divorces before consummation, wife returns the like (mithl) not the specific coins. This affects zakat obligations—zakat on the half is not dropped because it is like a new debt.
This sub-ruling is derived from the same 'talluq bi mithl' principle.
5
Note the ruling on deferring mahr to an unknown time
The passage concludes with the validity of deferring mahr to an unknown time (e.g., harvest) and the effect of a mixed immediate-deferred payment, where the entire amount is deferred unless the wife proves ease of payment.
This is a separate ruling from the dispute but follows the overall theme of mahr flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب المهر لتعلقه بعين الحصة وفائدة الثاني لو تزوجها أحدهما على دراهم مطلقة بقدر حصته من الدين وصار قصاصاً فلشريكه أن يأخذ منه نصفها لتعلقه بمثلها والدين إذا كان على غير المرأة فهو كالعين يتعلق النكاح بمثله لأنه لو تعلق بالعين لكان تمليك الدين من غير من عليه الدين بخلاف ما إذا كان عليها وفائدته أنها مخيرة إن شاءت أخذت من الزوج وإن شاءت من العاقلة اهـ . والأخير مخالف لما قدمناه عن الظهيرية ويمكن التوفيق بأن ما في الذخيرة مصور بأنه تزوجها على أرش له على عاقلتها وأمرها بقبض ذلك، وما في الظهيرية خال عن الأمر بالقبض، وقد علم أنه لو تزوجها على دراهم وأشار إليها فله إمساكها ودفع مثلها، ولو دفع الدراهم إليها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول لا يتعين عليها رد عين نصفها وإنما يتعين رد مثلها كما في جامع الفصولين وفرع عليه ما إذا كان المهر ألفاً دفعه إليها وحال الحول ووجبت الزكاة عليها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول فإنه لا يسقط عنها زكاة النصف لأنه لما لم يتعين رد العين كان بمنزلة دين حادث ا هـ . ومن أحكام المهر أنه يصبح تأجيله إلى وقت مجهول كالحصاد والدياس وهو الصحيح، ولو تزوجها بألف درهم على أن ينقد ما تيسر له والبقية إلى سنة كان الألف كله إلى سنة إلا أن تقيم المرأة البينة أنه تیسر له منها شيء أو كله فتأخده. كذا في الظهيرية .
The book of Nikah, chapter of Mahr: because of its connection to the specific share. And the benefit of the second: if one of them marries her on unspecified dirhams equal to his share of the debt and it becomes mutual compensation, then his partner may take half of it from him because of its connection to its like. And if the debt is on someone other than the woman, it is like a specific property; the marriage attaches to its like, because if it attached to the specific property, it would be transferring a debt from someone other than the debtor, unlike when it is on her. And its benefit is that she has the option: if she wishes, she takes it from the husband, and if she wishes, from the 'Aqila. End. And the latter is contradictory to what we presented from al-Zahiriyya, and reconciliation is possible: that what is in al-Dhakhira is formulated as him marrying her on an arsh that he has against her 'Aqila and he ordered her to collect it, while what is in al-Zahiriyya lacks the order to collect. And it is known that if he married her on dirhams and pointed to them, he may keep them and pay their like. And if he paid the dirhams to her and then divorced her before consummation, she is not bound to return the specific half; rather she is only bound to return its like, as in Jami' al-Fusulayn. And based on that, if the mahr was a thousand, he paid it to her and a year passed and zakat became obligatory on her, then he divorced her before consummation, the zakat on the half is not dropped because since the return of the specific property is not determined, it is like a newly occurring debt. End. And from the rulings of mahr: it is valid to defer it to an unknown time like harvest and threshing, and this is the correct view. And if he married her for a thousand dirhams on condition that he pay whatever is easy for him and the balance after a year, the entire thousand is due after a year unless the woman proves that some or all of it became easy for him, then she takes it. Thus in al-Zahiriyya.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on rulings related to mahr when it is specified as a debt. The author first discusses a scenario where a woman owes a debt to two men, and one of them marries her for that debt. The marriage attaches to the specific share of the debt (if the debt is on the woman) or to its like (if the debt is on someone else). The benefit of the latter scenario is that the wife has the option to collect from the husband or from the original debtor ('Aqila). The author then addresses an apparent contradiction between al-Dhakhira and al-Zahiriyya, reconciling it by noting the presence or absence of an order to collect. Further, the author clarifies that if the husband pays the mahr and later divorces before consummation, the wife is not obliged to return the specific coins but only their like, which has practical implications for zakat. The passage ends with the ruling that deferring mahr to an unknown time (like harvest) is valid, and discusses a case of mixed payment with some immediate and some deferred.

Key Terms
الحصة (al-hissah): The specific share of the debt that belongs to the husband.
قصاص (qisas): Mutual compensation or offset of debts.
العاقلة (al-'aqilah): The tribe or group responsible for paying blood money (diyah) on behalf of a member.
المثل (al-mithl): The equivalent or like; used here to describe the return of mahr when not attached to specific property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, always
B) No, never
C) It depends on whether the marriage is considered to attach to the specific share or to its like
D) It depends on whether the husband ordered the wife to collect

Key Takeaway
The partner's right to follow hinges on whether the marriage attaches to the specific share or its like, a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute reconciled by the presence of an order to collect.

The Three Causes of Mahr Confirmation and the Fourth Cause of Iddah
Ruling with proof on mahr confirmation causes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four causes that confirm full mahr in the Hanafi school and explain how valid seclusion (khalwah) equates to intercourse.

Core Idea
Full mahr is confirmed by intercourse, death, valid khalwah, and iddah from a prior consummation.

This passage explains that mahr becomes fully due upon certain events. While the contract itself makes mahr obligatory, it is only fully confirmed by one of three causes: intercourse, death, or valid khalwah. The commentator then adds a fourth cause: the iddah (waiting period) following a prior consummation. Understanding these causes is essential for determining mahr rights in various marital scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three original causes
Find the three events mentioned at the beginning of the passage: intercourse (al-wat'), death (al-mawt), and valid seclusion (al-khalwah).
The text also mentions that khalwah is equivalent to intercourse for confirming mahr.
2
Understand how khalwah equals intercourse
Recognize that the Hanafi rule treats valid khalwah (privacy after marriage) as equivalent to actual intercourse for the purpose of confirming full mahr.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position.
3
Extend to the fourth cause (iddah)
The passage proposes adding a fourth cause: if the husband marries a woman who is in iddah from a previous husband, and her iddah is due to intercourse from that previous marriage, then full mahr is due for the second marriage even without consummation.
This is based on the principle that entry in the first marriage is considered entry in the second (al-dukhul fi al-nikah al-awwal dukhul fi al-thani).

Source Text

His statement: (If he names it or less than it, she gets ten by intercourse or by death) because by entry the delivery of the exchange is realized and thereby the consideration is confirmed, and by death the marriage ends its end, and the thing by its end is established and confirmed, so it is established with all its obligations. His statement: (and reconciliation is possible) you have heard from the phrase of al-Dhakhira that we transmitted the explicit order to collect, and the author did not see it. His statement: (and it is proper to add a fourth, etc.) in it that the iddah is obligatory and the complete mahr on her in this image is by consideration of the previous intercourse due to the persistence of its effect which is the iddah, and it will come in iddah that this issue is one of the ten issues built on the principle that entry in the first marriage is entry in the second. His statement: (and it is proper to add a fifth, etc.) in it that the apparent is that the obligation of the complete mahr here is due to khalwah, for the immediate understanding is that he secluded with her and removed her hymen with his finger or a stone, and that its removal by a push in other than khalwah is different. So in the first, the full is obligatory, and in the second, half. And if each of them occurred in khalwah or without it, what is the difference? Reflect. Then I saw in the Jinaayat of al-Khaniyya what indicates what I said, for he mentioned that if he pushed his wife before consummation and her hymen went, then he divorced her before consummation, half the mahr is due according to Abu Hanifa, and all of it according to Muhammad and Zufr, and the narration from Abu Yusuf differs. End. And similar is in al-Fath from this chapter. So his statement 'if he pushed his wife before consummation' indicates that the issue of removal by stone is after consummation. And in the Jinaayat of al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya from al-Muhit: If he pushed his wife and did not consummate, and her hymen went, then he divorced her, half the mahr is due; and if he pushed another's woman and her hymen went, then he married her and consummated, two mahr are due. End. That is, mahr for the push and mahr for the marriage and consummation. And his speech indicates that if the husband removes his wife's hymen without intercourse, nothing is due on him; rather what is due here is half the mahr by divorce before consummation. And by this it is known that removal by stone or finger is likewise; rather the full mahr is due because it is not usually except in khalwah, so even if he struck her with a stone in other than khalwah and removed her hymen and divorced her before consummation, only half the mahr is due by the ruling of marriage, not by the ruling of striking. His statement: (and if a stranger pushed her and her hymen went, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: Two girls pushed each other and one's hymen went, there is due on her mahr al-mithl. End. That is, if the pushed one is married, then it is derived that it is due on the stranger in full if the husband did not divorce her before consummation, so reflect. Some virtuous scholars said in it: The phrase of Jami' al-Fusulayn indicates the obligation of mahr al-mithl absolutely without distinction between whether he divorced her before consummation or not, as is not hidden, and then it contradicts the author's imposition of half mahr al-mithl on the stranger when the husband divorces before consummation. This, and it is said in al-Minh: But in Javaahir al-Fatawa: and if a madman deflowers a woman's hymen with his finger and causes infibulation, it is indicated in al-Mabsut and al-Jami' al-Saghir that if he forcedly deflowers her with finger or stone or a specific tool, then the mahr is due on him, but our scholars mention that this happened erroneously and it is not due except with the tool placed for the purpose of lust and intercourse, and the arsh is due on his property. End. The speech of al-Minh, so let it be recorded. End. I say: The apparent is that what is in Jami' absolutely includes the full, including infibulation.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the confirmation of mahr. It begins by explaining that the mahr becomes fully due upon three events: intercourse, death, and valid khalwah (seclusion). The author then delves into an extended discussion about scenarios where the mahr is tied to a debt, repeating some of the earlier rules. Then he discusses the addition of a fourth cause: the obligation of iddah. He explains that if a woman is divorced after consummation and then remarried during her iddah, the full second mahr is due without consummation because the iddah is a consequence of the first marriage's intercourse. This is one of the ten principles where entry in the first marriage is considered entry in the second. The fifth addition is removal of the hymen by stone or finger. The author distinguishes between removal in a khalwah situation (full mahr) and removal without khalwah (half mahr). He cites various authorities like Jinaayat al-Khaniyya, al-Fath, al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya, and al-Muhit to present different rulings. A significant intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: according to Abu Hanifa, if the husband pushes his wife before consummation causing hymen loss, half mahr is due; while Muhammad and Zufr say full mahr. The passage concludes with a discussion on a foreigner causing hymen loss, where the obligation of full mahr al-mithl is debated.

Key Terms
الخلوة (al-khalwah): Valid seclusion between spouses after marriage, sufficient to give full mahr.
المهر (al-mahr): The dower obligatory upon the husband by marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following is NOT one of the three originally stated causes that confirm full mahr?
A) Intercourse
B) Death
C) Valid seclusion (khalwah)
D) Iddah from a prior consummation

Key Takeaway
Full mahr is confirmed by intercourse, death, valid khalwah, and iddah from a prior consummation.

Hymen Removal as a Cause of Mahr Confirmation and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling with proof on hymen removal and mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on hymen removal by the husband, distinguish between cases with and without khalwah, and state the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Hymen removal by the husband before consummation only gives half mahr outside khalwah, but full mahr if in khalwah, with a dispute among the Hanafi imams.

This passage discusses a fifth scenario that can affect mahr: the removal of the wife's hymen by the husband's action (e.g., pushing, stone, finger). The commentator analyzes whether this triggers full or half mahr, depending on whether it occurred in seclusion (khalwah) or not. There is a notable intra-Hanafi disagreement on the amount due. Understanding this dispute is essential for accurate fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of hymen removal
The passage considers a husband who, before consummation, causes his wife's hymen to break by an action like pushing, striking with a stone, or inserting a finger.
The text treats this as a fifth cause for mahr confirmation.
2
Apply the distinction of khalwah
If the removal occurs in valid seclusion (khalwah), it triggers full mahr. If it occurs outside khalwah (e.g., in public), it gives only half mahr.
This is the commentator's attempt to reconcile different views.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa says half mahr, Muhammad and Zufr say full mahr, and Abu Yusuf has two narrations. The ikhtilaf is based on whether the removal is considered equivalent to consummation.
The text cites al-Khaniyya and al-Fath for this dispute.
4
Consider the foreigner case
If a stranger (not the husband) causes hymen loss, the ruling differs: the stranger owes mahr al-mithl (not the specified mahr), and there is a discussion on whether this applies before or after divorce.
The passage ends with a debate on this point.

His statement: (If he names it or less than it, she gets ten by intercourse or by death) because by entry the delivery of the exchange is realized and thereby the consideration is confirmed, and by death the marriage ends its end, and the thing by its end is established and confirmed, so it is established with all its obligations. Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the confirmation of mahr. It begins by explaining that the mahr becomes fully due upon three events: intercourse, death, and valid khalwah (seclusion). The author then delves into an extended discussion about scenarios where the mahr is tied to a debt, repeating some of the earlier rules. Then he discusses the addition of a fourth cause: the obligation of iddah. He explains that if a woman is divorced after consummation and then remarried during her iddah, the full second mahr is due without consummation because the iddah is a consequence of the first marriage's intercourse. This is one of the ten principles where entry in the first marriage is considered entry in the second. The fifth addition is removal of the hymen by stone or finger. The author distinguishes between removal in a khalwah situation (full mahr) and removal without khalwah (half mahr). He cites various authorities like Jinaayat al-Khaniyya, al-Fath, al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya, and al-Muhit to present different rulings. A significant intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: according to Abu Hanifa, if the husband pushes his wife before consummation causing hymen loss, half mahr is due; while Muhammad and Zufr say full mahr. The passage concludes with a discussion on a foreigner causing hymen loss, where the obligation of full mahr al-mithl is debated.

Key Terms
البكارة (al-bakar): The hymen, its removal by any means has legal consequences on mahr.
الدفعة (al-daf'ah): A push or shove that causes hymen loss.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Fourth and Fifth Additions: Full Mahr Due to Iddah and Hymen Removal
Commentator proposes expansions to full mahr obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two additional scenarios where full mahr is due and distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a push removing the hymen before consummation.

Core Idea
Full mahr obligation can arise from iddah or specific acts of hymen removal, not only from consummation or seclusion.

The established rules make full mahr obligatory after consummation or valid seclusion (khalwah). However, scholars of the Hanafi school expanded these causes by analogy and custom. In this passage, Ibn Nujaym of al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq proposes two additional scenarios: remarriage during the iddah of a bāʾin divorce, and the husband's removal of his wife's hymen by stone or finger before consummation. He also discusses a dispute among Hanafi imams on the ruling when the hymen is removed by a push (defʿah). Understanding these expansions clarifies the school's nuanced approach to determining the dower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proposed additions
Locate the phrases 'رابع' and 'خامس' in the text. The fourth addition concerns remarriage during iddah; the fifth concerns hymen removal by stone or finger.
The fourth is based on the principle that iddah is a stronger cause than khalwah.
2
Analyse the legal reasoning (taʿlīl) for each
For the fourth: the iddah from the first marriage continues after a bāʾin divorce, so remarrying before its expiry triggers full mahr because the effect of the first consummation remains. For the fifth: custom dictates that hymen removal by stone or finger normally occurs in seclusion, thus it is equivalent to consummation.
The push case is different because it can occur without seclusion.
3
Recognise the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note the reported ikhtilaf: Abū Ḥanīfa holds that half mahr is due when a push removes the hymen before consummation, while Muḥammad and Zufar hold full mahr, and Abū Yūsuf has two narrations. Identify the basis: whether the push itself, regardless of seclusion, is treated like consummation.
The relied-upon (muftā bihī) position is Abū Ḥanīfa's view, as per later authorities like al-Marghinānī.
4
Apply the custom-based distinction
Understand that the ruling on full mahr for stone/finger assumes seclusion; if the act occurs without seclusion (e.g., striking with a stone in public), only half mahr is due by virtue of marriage, not by the injury.
This shows the role of ʿurf (custom) in determining legal consequences.
5
Examine the stranger scenario
If a stranger pushes the wife and her hymen is removed, and then the husband divorces her before consummation, the husband owes half the specified mahr and the stranger owes half the mahr al-mithl. If the stranger later marries her and consummates, two mahr are due: one for the push and one for the marriage.
This illustrates the interplay between tort liability (jināyāt) and marriage obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينبغي أن يزاد رابع وهو وجوب العدة عليها منه كما سيأتي في العدة لو طلقها بائناً بعد الدخول ثم تزوجها ثانياً في العدة وجب كمال المهر الثاني بدون الخلوة والدخول لأن وجوب العدة عليها فوق الخلوة، وينبغي أن يزاد خامس وهو ما لو أزال بكارتها بحجر ونحوه فإن لها كمال المهر كما صرحوا به بخلاف ما إذا أزالها بدفعة فإنه يجب النصف لو طلقها قبل الدخول. ولو دفعها أجنبي فزالت بكارتها وطلقت قبل الدخول وجب نصف المسمى على الزوج وعلى الأجنبي نصف صداق مثلها، وإنما لم يجب مهر المثل إذا سمى دون العشرة كما بالأمر بالقبض وكان المؤلف لم يره قوله : ( وينبغي أن يزاد رابع الخ) فيه أن العدة وجوب وتمام المهر عليها في هذه الصورة باعتبار الوطء السابق لبقاء أثره وهو العدة وسيأتي في العدة أن هذه المسألة إحدى المسائل العشر المبنية على أن الدخول في النكاح الأول دخول في الثاني قوله : (وينبغي أن يزاد خامس الخ) فيه أن الظاهر أن وجوب كمال المهر هنا بسبب الخلوة فإن المتبادر أنه اختلى بها فأزال بكارتها بأصبعه أو حجر وإن إزالتها بالدفعة في غير الخلوة فلذا وجب في الأول التمام وفي الثاني النصف والإبان كان كل منهما في الخلوة أو بدونها فما وجه الفرق بينهما تأمل. ثم رأيت في جنايات الخانية ما يشير إلى ما قلته فإنه ذكر أنه لو دفع امرأته قبل الدخول بها فذهبت عذرتها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول عليه نصف المهر في قول أبي حنيفة وكله في قول محمد وزفر واختلفت الرواية عن أبي يوسف ا هـ. ومثله في الفتح من هذا الباب . فقوله لو دفع امرأته قبل الدخول» يشير إلى أن مسألة إزالتها بالحجر بعد الدخول. وفي جنايات الفتاوي الهندية عن المحيط : ولو دفع امرأته ولم يدخل بها فذهبت عذرتها ثم طلقها فعليه نصف المهر، ولو دفع امرأة الغير وذهبت عذرتها ثم تزوجها ودخل وجب لها مهران ا هـ . أي مهر بالدفع ومهر بالنكاح والدخول، ودل كلامه أن الزوج إذا أزالة بكارة زوجته بغير الوطء لا يلزمه شيء وإنما لزمه هنا نصف المهر بالطلاق قبل الدخول. وبه يعلم أن إزالتها بالحجر أو الأصبع كذلك وإنما لزمه كل المهر لأنه في العادة لا يكون إلا في الخلوة حتى لو ضربها بحجر في غير الخلوة فأزال بكارتها وطلقها قبل الدخول لا يلزمه سوى نصف المهر بحكم النكاح لا بحكم الضرب قوله : (ولو دفعها أجنبي فزالت بكارتها الخ) قال في النهر : وفي جامع الفصولين : تدافعت جارية مع أخرى فزالت بكارتها وجب عليها مهر المثل ا هـ. وهو ما لو كانت المدفوعة متزوجة فيستفاد منه وجوبه على الأجنبي كاملاً فيما إذا لم يطلقها الزوج قبل الدخول فتدبرها هـ. قال بعض الفضلاء فيه : إن عبارة جامع الفصولين تدل على وجوب مهر المثل مطلقاً . من غير تفصيل بين ما إذا طلقها قبل الدخول أو لم يطلقها كما لا يخفى وحينئذ يعارض إيجاب المؤلف نصف مهر المثل على الأجنبي فيما إذا طلقها الزوج قبل الدخول. هذا وقال في المنح : لكن في جواهر الفتاوى كفئاً ولو افتض مجنون بكارة امرأة بأصبع وأفضاها فقد أشار في المبسوط والجامع الصغير إذا افتضها كرهاً بأصبع أو حجر أو آلة . مخصوصة حتى فعليه المهر، ولكن مشايخنا يذكرون أن هذا وقع سهواً ولا يجب إلا بالآلة الموضوعة لقضاء الشهوة والوطء ويجب الأرش في ماله . ا هـ كلام المنح فليحرر ا هـ . قلت : الظاهر أن ما في جامع بإطلاقه كمال يعم أفضاها
It is appropriate to add a fourth (ruling), which is the obligation of iddah upon her from him, as will come in iddah: if he divorced her bāʾinan after consummation, then married her a second time during the iddah, the full second mahr is obligatory without khulwa and consummation because the obligation of iddah upon her is above khulwa. And it is appropriate to add a fifth (ruling), which is if he removed her hymen with a stone or the like, then she has the full mahr, as they stated, unlike if he removed it with a single push, then half is obligatory if he divorced her before consummation. And if a stranger pushed her and her hymen was removed and she was divorced before consummation, half of the specified mahr is obligated upon the husband and upon the stranger half of her mahr al-mithl. And it is not obligatory to pay mahr al-mithl if the specified mahr is less than ten [dirhams] as per the command of qabd, and the author did not see his statement: 'And it is appropriate to add a fourth, etc.' In it, the iddah is an obligation and the completion of the mahr upon her in this scenario due to the previous intercourse, the effect of which remains, namely the iddah. And it will come in iddah that this issue is one of the ten issues based on the principle that consummation in the first marriage is consummation in the second. His statement: 'And it is appropriate to add a fifth, etc.' In it, it appears that the obligation of full mahr here is due to khulwa, for it is understood that he secluded with her and removed her hymen with his finger or a stone, and his removal with a push is without khulwa, so full (mahr) is obligated in the first and half in the second, but if each occurred in khulwa or without it, what is the basis for the difference? Contemplate. Then I saw in Khiyānāt al-Khāniyya what indicates what I said, for it mentions that if he pushed his wife before consummation and her hymen was removed, then he divorced her before consummation, half the mahr is due according to Abū Ḥanīfa, and the whole according to Muḥammad and Zufar, and there is a difference of narration from Abū Yūsuf. End quote. The like is in al-Fatḥ from this chapter. So his words 'if he pushed his wife before consummation' indicate that the issue of removing with a stone is after consummation. And in the Khiyānāt of al-Fatāwā al-Hindiyya from al-Muḥīṭ: 'If he pushed his wife and did not have intercourse with her, and her hymen was removed, then he divorced her, half the mahr is due upon him. And if he pushed another's woman and her hymen was removed, then he married her and had intercourse, two mahr are due to her.' That is, a mahr for the push and a mahr for the marriage and consummation. And his speech indicates that if the husband removes the hymen of his wife without intercourse, nothing is incumbent upon him, but half the mahr is incumbent here due to divorce before consummation. By this it is known that removing with a stone or finger is likewise, and the full mahr is incumbent only because customarily it is not except in khulwa, such that if he struck her with a stone without khulwa and removed her hymen and divorced her before consummation, only half the mahr is incumbent by virtue of marriage, not by virtue of striking. His statement: 'And if a stranger pushed her and her hymen was removed, etc.' Al-Nahr said: In Jāmiʿ al-Fuṣūlayn: 'Two girls pushed each other and one's hymen was removed; mahr al-mithl is incumbent upon the other.' End quote. This applies if the pushed one was married; it benefits that it is incumbent upon the stranger fully when the husband did not divorce her before consummation, so reflect. End quote. Some scholars said: Indeed, the expression of Jāmiʿ al-Fuṣūlayn indicates the obligation of mahr al-mithl absolutely, without detail between if he divorced her before consummation or not, as is not hidden. And thus it contradicts the author's imposition of half mahr al-mithl upon the stranger when the husband divorced her before consummation. Then al-Manḥ said: But in Jawāhir al-Fatāwā: 'If a madman opened a woman's hymen with his finger and caused her ifḍāʾ, it is indicated in al-Mabsūṭ and al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr that if he opened it forcefully with a finger, stone, or a specific instrument, then the mahr is due upon him. But our mashāyikh mention that this occurred forgetfully, and it is not obligatory except with an instrument made for fulfilling desire and intercourse, and the arsh is obligatory from his wealth.' End quote from al-Manḥ, so it should be scrutinized. End quote. I say: It appears that what is in Jāmiʿ (al-Fuṣūlayn) generally encompasses ifḍāʾ.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqāʾiq, expanding on rules regarding when full mahr becomes obligatory. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, proposes two additional scenarios beyond what the author mentioned. The first is when a woman is divorced bāʾinan after consummation and then remarried during her iddah; in this case, full mahr is due for the second marriage even without seclusion (khulwa) or consummation, because the iddah from the first marriage creates a stronger connection than mere seclusion. The second is when the husband removes his wife's hymen with a stone or similar object before consummation; here, full mahr is due, unlike if he removes it with a single push (defʿah), where only half is due if divorced before consummation. The commentator then explores a dispute among Hanafi scholars regarding a push causing loss of virginity before consummation: Abū Ḥanīfa holds half mahr, while Muḥammad and Zufar hold the full mahr, and Abū Yūsuf has two narrations. The discussion extends to cases involving a stranger pushing a woman, leading to two mahr if the stranger later marries and consummates. The passage also touches on madman cases and the opinion of later mashāyikh who restrict mahr liability to instruments specifically designed for sexual gratification, otherwise only compensatory damages (arsh) are due. Throughout, the commentator engages in legal reasoning (taʿlīl) based on custom, qiyas, and istihsan, distinguishing between acts in seclusion and outside it.

Key Terms
العدة (al-ʿiddah): The waiting period after divorce or death, here specifically the iddah of a bāʾin divorce.
الخلوة (al-khalwah): Seclusion between spouses that is legally considered like consummation for some rulings.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower appropriate for a woman of similar status, used when mahr is unspecified or invalid.
الدفعة (al-defʿah): A single push that removes the hymen, as opposed to removal by stone or finger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a stranger pushes a married woman and her hymen is removed, and then the husband divorces her before consummation, what is due to her according to the author?
A) Full mahr al-mithl from the stranger and half specified mahr from the husband
B) Half specified mahr from the husband and half mahr al-mithl from the stranger
C) Only full mahr from the husband
D) Only mahr al-mithl from the stranger

Key Takeaway
Full mahr becomes obligatory not only by consummation or valid khulwa but also by the continuation of iddah after a bāʾin divorce and by certain acts of hymen removal, with a nuanced intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the amount in the push case.

Halving of Specified Mahr upon Divorce Before Consummation
Explains Quranic ruling that specified mahr is halved by divorce before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on halving of specified mahr upon divorce before consummation, and distinguish between automatic return of undelivered mahr and the entitlement to half of delivered mahr.

Core Idea
Divorce before consummation halves the specified mahr; if delivered, half stays wife's until court order or her consent.

Divorce before consummation triggers a unique Quranic ruling: the specified mahr becomes half. Yet the application is not always straightforward. The Hanafi school delves into whether this half automatically returns to the husband's ownership or merely gives him an entitlement, depending on whether the mahr was already delivered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the ruling applies to divorce before consummation (dukhul) including seclusion (khalwah). The specified mahr (musamma) is halved.
Consummation includes seclusion de jure.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Quran 2:237, which commands paying half of the specified mahr upon divorce before consummation.
The verse is qat'i in both thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse explicitly states 'pay them half of what you specified,' implying the specified mahr is divided equally.
The imperative indicates obligation (wujub).
4
Analyze the nuance of ownership
If the mahr has not been delivered, half automatically returns to the husband's ownership. If delivered, the wife's ownership of the half persists unless a court rules or she consents.
Possession (qabd) strengthens ownership even if the underlying cause is defective.
5
Note the textual variant
The word 'yatanaṣṣaf' can be read with ya or ta. Al-Nahr prefers the ta reading, implying entitlement rather than automatic return.
This avoids the need for qualification based on delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وبالطلاق قبل الدخول يتنصف) أي المسمى لقوله تعالى ﴿وإن طلقتموهن من قبل أن تمسوهن﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٧] الآية. والأقيسة متعارضة ففيه تفويت الزوج الملك على نفسه باختيار، وفيه عود المعقود عليه إليها سالماً فكان المرجع فيه النص. كذا في الهداية وهو بيان للواقع لأنه جواب سؤال مقدر كما فهمه الشارحون، وتمامه في فتح القدير. وشمل الدخول الخلوة لما في المجتبى: ولو يذكر الخلوة مع أنها شرط لما أن اسم الدخول يشملها لأنها دخول حكماً ا هـ. وظاهر قوله ينتصف أن النصف يعود إلى ملك الزوج. وأطلقه وفيه تفصيل، فإن كان المهر لم يسلمه إليها عاد إلى ملك الزوج نصفه بمجرد الطلاق، وإن كان مقبوضاً لها فإنه لا يبطل ملك المرأة في النصف إلا بقضاء أو رضا لأن الطلاق قبل الدخول أوجب فساد سبب ملكها في النصف، وفساد السبب في الابتداء لا يمنع ثبوت ملكها بالقبض، فأولى أن لا يمنع بقاءه، فلو أعتق الزوج العبد المهر المقبوض بعد الطلاق قبله لم ينفذ في شيء منه، الفصولين مبني على ما في المبسوط والجامع الصغير قوله: (أي المسمى هذا بناء على أن ينتصف بالياء. قال في النهر إلا أن كونه بالتاء الفوقية أولى وأنه لو سمى ما دونها لا يتنصف المسمى فقط. وفي المبسوط وغيره: تزوجها على ثوب قيمته خمسة فطلقها قبل الدخول كان لها نصف الثوب ودرهمان ونصف. وما في الخلاصة: «لو تزوجها على أقل من العشرة أو ثوب قيمته أقل من عشرة كان لها نصف المسمى عند الطلاق قبل الدخول محمول على هذا قوله: (وظاهر قوله يتنصف الخ) قال في النهر: ومعنى تنصيفها استحقاق الزوج النصف منها لا أنه يعود إلى ملكه كما فهمه في البحر يرد أن هذا إذا لم يكن مقبوضاً لها ا.هـ. ووجهه أن استحقاق النصف أعم من أن يكون نصف العين أو القيمة فلا يحتاج إلى التقييد بخلاف ما ذكره المؤلف . فلا
His statement: (And by divorce before consummation it is halved) means the specified [mahr] due to His statement, Exalted: 'And if you divorce them before you have touched them' [al-Baqarah 2:237] to the end of the verse. And the analogies are conflicting: it involves the husband forfeiting ownership to himself by choice, and it involves the return of the subject matter of the contract to her intact, so the reference is to the text. Thus in al-Hidāyah, and it is an explanation of the reality because it is an answer to an implied question, as the commentators understood, and its completion is in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. And consummation includes seclusion (khalwah) because in al-Mujtabā: 'even if khalwah is not mentioned, although it is a condition, because the term consummation includes it as it is consummation de jure.' End quote. And the apparent meaning of his statement 'it is halved' is that half returns to the ownership of the husband. But he left it unqualified, and there is a detail: if the mahr had not been delivered to her, half of it returns to the husband's ownership merely by the divorce; if it had been received by her, then the wife's ownership of the half is not invalidated except by a court order or her consent, because the divorce before consummation invalidates the cause of her ownership of the half, and the invalidity of the cause initially does not prevent the establishment of ownership through possession, so it is even more apt that it does not prevent its continuation. Hence, if the husband emancipates the slave girl who is the received mahr after the divorce before [consummation], it is not effective in any part of her. In al-Fuṣūlayn it is based on what is in al-Mabsūṭ and al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr. His statement: (i.e., the specified) this is based on the view that it is halved with a yāʾ. Al-Nahr said: 'Except that being with the tāʾ al-tawqiyya is preferable, and that if he named less than the mahr al-mithl, only the specified is halved.' In al-Mabsūṭ and others: 'He married her for a garment worth five dirhams and divorced her before consummation; she gets half the garment and two and a half dirhams.' What is in al-Khulāṣa: 'If he married her for less than ten dirhams or a garment worth less than ten, she gets half of the specified at divorce before consummation' is carried on this. His statement: (And the apparent meaning of his statement 'it is halved' etc.) al-Nahr said: 'And the meaning of its halving is that the husband becomes entitled to half of it, not that it returns to his ownership as understood in al-Baḥr; he would respond that this applies when it is not in her possession.' End quote. And his point is that entitlement to half is more general, whether half of the actual object or its value, so it does not need qualification, unlike what the author mentioned. Then the text ends.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage from al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq unpacks the ruling that divorce before consummation halves the specified mahr, citing Quran 2:237. The commentator notes that the analogies (qiyas) conflict: divorce involves the husband voluntarily forfeiting ownership, but also returning the dower intact, so the text of the Quran is decisive. He clarifies that 'consummation' includes seclusion (khalwah) by legal fiction. A key nuance is whether half returns to the husband's ownership or merely entails his entitlement to it. If the mahr has not been delivered, half automatically reverts to his ownership. If it has been received by the wife, her ownership of the half remains intact unless a judge rules or she consents, because possession establishes ownership even if the underlying cause is defective. Therefore, if the husband emancipates a slave girl who was the mahr and was already received, the emancipation does not affect the half because he does not own it. The commentator also addresses a textual variant (halving with yāʾ vs. tāʾ) and cites supporting cases from al-Mabsūṭ and al-Khulāṣa regarding mahr less than mahr al-mithl. The passage emphasizes the interplay between divine text, analogical reasoning, and practical consequences in marriage contracts.

Key Terms
يتنصف (yatanaṣṣaf): The specified mahr is halved (it becomes half) due to divorce before consummation.
المسمى (al-musammā): The mahr explicitly specified in the marriage contract.
القبض (al-qabḍ): Physical or constructive possession of the mahr by the wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband pays the specified mahr and then divorces his wife before consummation, does half of the mahr automatically return to his ownership?
A) Yes, because divorce before consummation halves the mahr
B) No, because possession establishes ownership and it requires court order or her consent
C) Yes, because the marriage is dissolved
D) No, because the wife keeps the entire mahr

Key Takeaway
The half of specified mahr becomes the husband's entitlement, but if already delivered, it does not automatically revert to his ownership; a court order or wife's consent is needed.

The Half-Dower Rule: Quranic Proof and Scope
Ruling with proof from Quran and discussion of khalwa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that divorce before consummation halves the named dower, cite the Quranic proof, and explain why valid seclusion (khalwa) is treated as consummation for this ruling.

Core Idea
Divorce before consummation halves the dower — the Quran commands it, and conflicting analogies are overridden by the text.

This lesson examines the foundational rule that when a husband divorces his wife before any sexual relationship, the dower is halved. The Quran provides the direct proof, and the Hanafi school clarifies that valid seclusion (khalwa) is legally equivalent to consummation. We will trace the reasoning from the text and understand why this ruling cannot be derived from analogy alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn statement
Locate the exact ruling from the matn: 'And by divorce before consummation it is halved.' What does 'it' refer to? The author specifies 'the named dower' (al-musamma).
The matn is from Kanz al-Daqaiq; the commentary here expands on it.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the Quranic verse cited: Surah al-Baqarah 2:237. The verse is quoted as evidence.
The verse explicitly uses the wording 'half of what you prescribed'.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the verse proves the half-dower. The imperative form and the phrase 'فَنِصْفُ مَا فَرَضْتُمْ' clearly indicate the obligation of half the dower upon divorce before touching.
The text is qat'i al-dalalah in Hanafi usul.
4
Examine the conflicting analogies
The author mentions that analogies (qiyas) are conflicting: one analogy would give the full dower, another would give none. Because of this conflict, the text (nass) is the reference, and the ruling is taken from the Quran directly.
This highlights a principle: when qiyas yields contradictory results, the text prevails.
5
Apply the inclusion of khalwa
Note that the term 'dukhul' in the matn includes valid seclusion (khalwa sahiha) by legal extension, as stated in al-Mujtaba. This is a distinctively Hanafi position.
Khalwa is treated as consummation for the half-dower rule, iddah, and other rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالطلاق قبل الوطء ينتصف وإن لم يسمه أو نفاه فلها مهر مثلها أن وطيء قال زفر لأن فساد هذه التسمية لحق الشرع وقد صار مقضياً بالعشرة، فأما ما يرجع إلى حقها فقد رضيت بالعشرة لرضاها بما دونها ولا معتبر بانعدام التسمية لأنها قد ترضى بالتمليك من غير عوض تكرماً ولا ترضى فيه بالعوض اليسير، وقد علم حكم الأكثر بالأولى لأن التقدير في المهر يمنع النقصان فقط. وفي المحيط. والظهيرية : لو تزوجها على ألفين ألف منها الله تعالى أو للخاطب أو لولدي أو لفلان فالمهر ألف لأن هذا استثناء، في كلام واحد. وفي الظهيرية: لو تزوجها على غنم بعينها أن أصوافها لي كان له الصوف استحساناً ولو تزوجها على جارية حبلى على أن ما في بطنها تكون له الجارية وما في بطنها لها ا هـ. وكأنه لأن الحمل كجزئها فلم يصح استثناؤه. وفي الولوالجية والخانية : لو تزوجها على ألف درهم نقد البلد فكسدت وصار النقد غيرها كان على الزوج قيمة تلك الدراهم يوم . المختار، ولو كان مكان النكاح بيعاً فسد البيع لأن الكساد بمنزلة الهلاك وهلاك البدل يوجب فساد البيع بخلاف النكاح ا اه. قوله: (وبالطلاق قبل الدخول يتنصف) أي المسمى لقوله تعالى وإن طلقتموهن من قبل أن تمسوهن ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۳۷] الآية . والأقيسة متعارضة ففيه تفويت الزوج الملك على نفسه باختيار، وفيه عود المعقود عليه إليها سالماً فكان المرجع فيه النص. كذا في الهداية وهو بيان للواقع لأنه جواب سؤال مقدر كما فهمه الشارحون، وتمامه في فتح القدير. وشمل الدخول الخلوة لما في المجتبى : ولو يذكر الخلوة مع أنها شرط لما أن اسم الدخول يشملها لأنها دخول حكماً اهـ . وظاهر قوله ينتصف أن النصف يعود إلى ملك الزوج. وأطلقه وفيه تفصيل، فإن كان المهر لم يسلمه إليها عاد إلى ملك الزوج نصفه بمجرد الطلاق، وإن كان مقبوضاً لها فإنه لا يبطل ملك المرأة في النصف إلا بقضاء أو رضا لأن الطلاق قبل الدخول أوجب فساد سبب ملكها في النصف، وفساد السبب في الابتداء لا يمنع ثبوت ملكها بالقبض، فأولى أن لا يمنع بقاءه، فلو أعتق الزوج العبد المهر المقبوض بعد الطلاق قبله لم ينفذ في شيء منه، الفصولين مبني على ما في المبسوط والجامع الصغير قوله : (أي المسمى هذا بناء على أن ينتصف بالياء. قال في النهر إلا أن كونه بالتاء الفوقية أولى وأنه لو سمى ما دونها لا يتنصف المسمى فقط . وفي المبسوط وغيره: تزوجها على ثوب قيمته خمسة فطلقها قبل الدخول كان لها نصف الثوب ودرهمان ونصف. وما في الخلاصة: «لو تزوجها على أقل من العشرة أو ثوب قيمته أقل من عشرة كان لها نصف المسمى عند الطلاق قبل الدخول محمول على هذا قوله : (وظاهر قوله يتنصف الخ) قال في النهر : ومعنى تنصيفها استحقاق الزوج النصف منها لا أنه يعود إلى ملكه كما فهمه في البحر يرد أن هذا إذا لم يكن مقبوضاً لها ا.هـ. ووجهه أن استحقاق النصف أعم من أن يكون نصف العين أو القيمة فلا يحتاج إلى التقييد بخلاف ما ذكره المؤلف . فلا ولو قضى القاضي بعد ذلك يعود نصفه إلى ملكه لأنه عتق سبق ملكه فلم ينفذ ونفذ عتق المرأة في الكل، وكذا بيعها وهبتها لبقاء ملكها في الكل قبل القضاء والرضا. وإذا نفذ تصرفها فقد تعذر عليها رد النصف بعد وجوبه فتضمن نصف قيمته للزوج يوم قبضت، ولو وطئت الجارية بشبهة فحكم العقر حكم الزيادة المنفصلة المتولدة من الأصل كالأرش لأنه بدل من جزء من عينها فإن المستوفى بالوطء في حكم العين وفي الظهيرية : ولو زاد المهر زيادة منفصلة كالولد والثمر والأرش والعقر قبل القبض فكلها تتنصف بالطلاق قبل الدخول، وبعد القبض لا تتنصف وعليها نصف قيمة الأصل يوم ،قبضت وكذلك لو ارتدت ـ والعياذ بالله تعالى ـ أو قبلت ابن الزوج وإن كانت بدل المنافع كالكسب والغلة والموهوب للمهر فهي للمرأة وليست بمهر عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يتنصف مع الأصل. وكذلك على هذا كسب المبيع قبل القبض ولو آجره الزوج فالأجرة له ولزمه التصدق بها والزيادة المتصلة قبل القبض تتنصف بالإجماع، وبعد القبض تتنصف عند محمد خلافاً لهما، والزيادة المنفصلة بعد القبض إذا هلكت يتنصف الأصل دون الزيادة ولو استولد الزوج الجارية الممهورة قبل القبض وادعى نسب الولد ثم طلقها قبل الدخول تتنصف الجارية والولد لأن العلوق وجد في ملك الغير فلم تصح الدعوة وذكر في كتاب الدعوى أنه يثبت النسب وتصير الجارية أم ولد له لأنه عاد إليه قديم ملكه وعتق نصف الولد بإقراره لأنه جزء منه ويسعى الولد في نصف قيمته للمرأة على الروايتين جميعاً .
And by divorce before intercourse, it is halved, and if he did not name (the dower) or denied it, then she has a dower like her (peers) if he had intercourse. Zufr said: Because the corruption of this naming is due to the right of the Shari'ah, and it has become decreed by the marital companionship. As for what pertains to her right, she has consented to the companionship because she consented to less than it, and the absence of naming is not considered because she may consent to ownership without compensation generously and does not consent to a small compensation. And the ruling of the greater is known by priority because the estimation in the dower only prevents deficiency. In al-Muhit and al-Zahiriyya: If he married her for two thousand dirhams, one thousand of which is for Allah, the Exalted, or for the suitor, or for my son, or for so-and-so, then the dower is one thousand because this is an exception in one statement. In al-Zahiriyya: If he married her for specific sheep, with the condition that their wool is his, then he has the wool by istihsan. And if he married her for a pregnant slave-girl with the condition that what is in her womb is his and the slave-girl is for her, then it is as if the pregnancy is part of her, so its exception is not valid. In al-Walwaljiyya and al-Khaniyya: If he married her for one thousand dirhams of the current coinage of the town, then the currency became invalid and another currency took its place, then the husband owes the value of those dirhams on the day of the choice. And if it were a sale instead of marriage, the sale would be void because the invalidity is like destruction, and destruction of the substitute necessitates voidness of the sale, unlike marriage. His statement: (And by divorce before consummation it is halved) i.e., the named (dower), due to His statement, the Exalted: 'And if you divorce them before you have touched them' [al-Baqarah 2:237] the verse. The analogies are conflicting: in it, the husband forfeits ownership over himself by choice, and in it, the subject matter of the contract returns to her intact, so the reference is the text. Thus in al-Hidaya, and it is an explanation of the reality because it is the answer to an implied question as understood by the commentators, and its completion is in Fath al-Qadir. And it includes seclusion (khalwa) due to what is in al-Mujtaba: 'He did not mention seclusion even though it is a condition because the name of consummation includes it, as it is consummation legally.' The apparent meaning of 'it is halved' is that the half returns to the ownership of the husband. And he left it unrestricted, but there is detail: if the dower was not handed over to her, half of it returns to the husband's ownership by the mere divorce; and if it was in her possession, then the woman's ownership in half is not invalidated except by court judgment or her consent, because divorce before consummation necessitates corruption of the cause (sabab) of her ownership in half, and corruption of the cause at the beginning does not prevent the establishment of her ownership by possession, so a fortiori it does not prevent its continuation. So if the husband frees the slave (that is the dower) in her possession after the divorce before (the judgment), it is not effective in any part of it... (continued) And if the judge subsequently rules, half returns to his ownership because the freeing preceded his ownership, so it was not effective, and the woman's freeing becomes effective in the whole. Similarly her sale and gift, due to the continuation of her ownership in the whole before judgment and consent. And if her disposition is effective, then she is unable to return the half after its obligation, so she becomes liable for half its value to the husband on the day she took possession. And if the slave-girl is violated by shubha, then the ruling of the 'aqr (compensation for intercourse) is the ruling of the separate increase generated from the original, like the arsh (defect compensation), because it is a substitute for a part of her substance, since what is consumed by intercourse is considered as part of the substance. In al-Zahiriyya: If the dower increases by a separate increase like a child, fruit, arsh, or 'aqr, before possession, then all of it is halved by divorce before consummation. And after possession, it is not halved, and upon her is half the value of the original (without increase) on the day she took possession. Similarly, if she apostatizes or she accepts the son of the husband... And if it is a substitute for benefits like earnings, produce, and what is gifted as dower, then it is for the woman and not part of the dower according to Abu Hanifa. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is halved with the original. Similarly, the earnings of the sold item before possession. And if the husband leases it, the rent is for him but he is obliged to give it in charity. And the connected increase before possession is halved by consensus, and after possession it is halved according to Muhammad contrary to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). And the separate increase after possession, if it perishes, the original is halved without the increase. And if the husband impregnates the slave-girl (the dower) before possession and claims the lineage of the child, then divorces her before consummation, the slave-girl and the child are halved because the conception occurred in the ownership of another, so the claim (of lineage) is not valid. And it is mentioned in Kitab al-Da'wa that lineage is established and the slave-girl becomes umm walad for him because his old ownership returns to him, and half of the child is freed by his acknowledgement because it is part of him, and the child must work for half its value for the woman according to both narrations.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the ruling in Kanz al-Daqaiq that divorce before consummation halves the named dower. The author begins by quoting the matn: 'And by divorce before intercourse, it is halved' and then provides Zufr's reasoning that even if the dower naming is corrupt due to a legal defect (like naming something non-existent), the marriage is valid and she gets mahr al-mithl if intercourse occurred. Then several subsidiary rulings are quoted: (1) If the dower includes an exception like 'one thousand for Allah', the exception is valid and the dower is the remainder. (2) If the dower is specific sheep with the condition that the wool is for the husband, the wool is his by istihsan because it is a separate increase. (3) If the dower is a pregnant slave-girl with the condition that the child is for the husband, it is invalid because the pregnancy is part of her. (4) If the currency of the dower becomes invalid, the husband owes the value on the day of the choice; this is unique to nikah compared to sale where the contract would be void. Then the author returns to the main matn phrase 'And by divorce before consummation it is halved', providing the Quranic proof from al-Baqarah 2:237. He explains that analogies conflict (qiyas would suggest either the dower is completely due or completely forfeited), so the text is followed. The term 'dukhul' includes khalwa (seclusion) by legal extension. The apparent meaning of 'halved' is that half returns to the husband, but this requires detail: if not yet delivered, half returns automatically; if delivered, the wife's ownership in half continues until court judgment or her consent, because the fasad (corruption) of the cause does not invalidate ownership established by qabd. Consequently, if the husband frees the slave-girl (the dower) after divorce but before judgment, it is ineffective because he does not own half yet; the wife's freeing is effective in the whole. If the wife then disposes of the half (e.g., sells it), she becomes liable for half its value. The passage then discusses various increases (ziyada) in the dower: separate increases before qabd are halved; after qabd they are not halved. There is a dispute: according to Abu Hanifa, badal al-manafi' (substitute for benefits like earnings) is not part of the dower and not halved; according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is halved with the original. Connected increases before qabd are halved by consensus; after qabd, Muhammad says they are halved, contrarily to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Finally, a case where the husband impregnates the slave-girl (dower) before qabd and claims the child: the child is halved with the slave-girl, but lineage is established according to Kitab al-Da'wa, and the slave-girl becomes umm walad because the husband's old ownership returns (by the tansif); the child is half-freed and must work for its value.

Key Terms
ينتصف (yantasiif): The dower is halved; half goes to the wife and half returns to the husband upon divorce before consummation.
خلوة (khalwa): Seclusion between husband and wife in a private place where intercourse is possible; legally considered as consummation for the purpose of dower and divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the text (nass) preferred over qiyas for the half-dower rule?
A) Because qiyas is never used in matters of dower.
B) Because analogies are conflicting and inconclusive.
C) Because the Quranic verse is recent revelation.
D) Because the companions all agreed on the half.

Key Takeaway
The half-dower rule upon divorce before consummation is directly from the Quran, and valid seclusion is treated as consummation for this and other related rulings.

Ruling on Increase in Dower and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on increase in dower with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on increase in dower after possession and explain the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
After possession, no increase in dower is halved upon divorce.

This lesson focuses on the rule for increase in the dower when divorce occurs before consummation. The key distinction is whether the increase occurred before or after the wife took possession. The majority of Hanafi imams hold that after possession, no increase is halved, but Imam Muhammad disagrees regarding connected generated increases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the timing of the increase
Determine whether the increase occurred before or after the wife's possession (qabd) of the dower.
Possession here means actual taking control of the dower property.
2
Classify the increase
Is the increase connected (muttasil) or separate (munfasil)? Is it generated (mutawallid) from the original or not?
Connected: calf still with mother; Separate: calf weaned; Generated: fruit; Non-generated: dye.
3
Apply the majority rule
If after possession, the increase is not halved regardless of type, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Note the exception
Imam Muhammad holds that connected generated increases after possession are halved along with the original.
His view is not acted upon in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن حاصل الزيادة في المهر أنها إذا حدثت بعد قبض المرأة ثم طلقها قبل الدخول فإنها لا تتنصف سواء كانت متصلة متولدة أو منفصلة متولدة أولاً إلا متصلة متولدة عند محمد، وأما إذا حدثت قبل القبض فإن المتولدة تتنصف متصلة أو منفصلة، وغير المتولدة لا تتنصف، وفي خيار العيب الزيادة المتولدة متصلة أو منفصلة غير متولدة فإنها لا تمنع الرد به والمتصلة غير المتولدة والمنفصلة المتولدة يمنعان الرد به وفي البيع الفاسد كل زيادة فإنها لا تمنع الاسترداد والفسخ إلا زيادة متصلة غير متولدة وفي باب الرجوع في الهبة فإن الزيادة المتصلة متولدة أو غير متولدة مانعة من الرجوع والمنفصلة متولدة أو لا غير مانعة، وفي باب الغصب لا يمنع من رد العين إلا الزيادة المتصلة الغير المتولدة التي لا يمكن فصل المغصوب عنها، فلتحفظ هذه المواضع فإنها نفيسة. وأما المتصلة الغير المتولدة كالصبغ في مسألة الزيادة في المهر فخارجة عن البحث واعلم بأن الأوصاف لا تفرد بالعقد ولا تفرد بضمان العقد، والإتلاف يرد على الأوصاف فأمكن إظهار حكم الإتلاف فيها فنقول : إذا حدث في المهر عيب سماوي إن شاءت أخذته ناقصاً بلا غرمه النقصان، وإن شاءت أخذت قوله : (بعد الطلاق (قبله الظرفان متعلقان بأعتق» والضمير في قبلة» للقضاء أو الرضا وأفرد
Then know that the essence of increase in the dower is that if it occurs after the woman's possession, then he divorces her before consummation, then it is not halved, whether it is connected and generated or separate and generated, except connected and generated according to Muhammad. As for if it occurs before possession, then the generated (increase) is halved, whether connected or separate, and the non-generated is not halved. In the option of defect, the generated increase, whether connected or separate and non-generated, does not prevent the return (of the defective item), and the connected non-generated and separate generated prevent the return. In invalid sale, every increase does not prevent recovery and rescission except a connected non-generated increase. In the chapter of revocation of gift, the increase that is connected, whether generated or not, prevents revocation, and the separate increase, whether generated or not, does not prevent. In the chapter of usurpation, nothing prevents the return of the object except the connected non-generated increase that cannot be separated from the usurped item. So memorize these topics, for they are precious. As for the connected non-generated like dye in the issue of increase in the dower, it is outside the discussion. And know that attributes (awsaf) are not singled out by contract nor singled out by the guarantee of the contract, and destruction (itlaf) applies to attributes, so it is possible to manifest the ruling of destruction in them. So we say: If a heavenly defect occurs in the dower, if she wishes, she takes it deficient without charging him for the deficiency, and if she wishes, she takes (the full value?) His statement: (after divorce (before it) the two adverbs are related to 'freeing', and the pronoun in 'before it' refers to the judgment or consent, and it is singular.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a comprehensive summary of the rulings on increases (ziyada) in the context of the dower, and then compares them with other legal chapters. The author begins by stating the rule for increase in the dower: if the increase occurs after the wife has taken possession (qabd) of the dower, and then the husband divorces her before consummation, the increase is not halved with the original—except according to Imam Muhammad, who says that a connected generated increase (ziyada muttasila mutawallida) is halved. If the increase occurs before possession, then generated increases (both connected and separate) are halved, while non-generated increases (like natural growth not due to the property) are not halved. The author then compares this with rulings in other chapters: (1) Option of defect (khiyar al-ayb): A generated increase (whether connected or separate, though non-generated separate does not prevent return) does not prevent the buyer from returning a defective item, but a connected non-generated increase and a separate generated increase do prevent return. (2) Invalid sale (bay' fasid): Any increase does not prevent recovery and rescission except a connected non-generated increase. (3) Revocation of gift (ruju' fil-hiba): Connected increases prevent revocation; separate increases do not. (4) Usurpation (ghasb): Only connected non-generated increases prevent return of the usurped object. The author urges memorization of these rules. He then clarifies that connected non-generated increases (e.g., dye in fabric) are outside the current discussion on dower increase. Finally, he notes that attributes (physical qualities like dye) are not independently transacted but can be subject to compensation if destroyed; if a heavenly defect (not caused by the wife) occurs in the dower, she has the option to keep it with a reduction in price or return it. The last part seems to be a separate comment on a previous passage about the timing of freeing and the pronoun references.

Key Terms
زيادة متصلة متولدة (ziyada muttasila mutawallida): A connected increase that is generated from the object itself, such as fruit from a tree or a calf from a cow.
زيادة منفصلة متولدة (ziyada munfasila mutawallida): A separate increase that is generated from the object, such as a calf after separation from the mother, or rent from a house.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-ayb): The buyer's option to return a defective item to the seller.
الرجوع في الهبة (al-ruju' fil-hiba): The donor's right to revoke a gift under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a connected generated increase (ziyada muttasila mutawallida) in the dower NOT get halved upon divorce before consummation?
A) When it occurs before the wife takes possession.
B) When it occurs after the wife takes possession.
C) It is always halved regardless of timing.
D) It is never halved.

Key Takeaway
After possession, no increase in dower is halved — this is the operative Hanafi position.

Comparative Rulings on Increases in Different Legal Chapters
Comparative summary of increase rulings in different chapters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi taxonomy of increases (connected/separate, generated/non-generated) to determine whether an increase prevents return or revocation in khiyar al-ayb, bay' fasid, hibah, and ghasb.

Core Idea
Connected non-generated increase prevents return; generated separate prevents in some chapters.

The same categories of increase appear across multiple fiqh chapters. Mastering their effects is essential for a Hanafi jurist. This lesson compares the rules for khiyar al-ayb, invalid sale, gift revocation, and usurpation.

Guided Path
1
Recall the four categories
Increase can be connected or separate, and generated or non-generated. Combine them into four types: muttasila mutawallida, muttasila ghayr mutawallida, munfasila mutawallida, munfasila ghayr mutawallida.
Example: paint on a fabric is connected non-generated; calf is connected generated.
2
Learn the rule for khiyar al-ayb
Generated increase (any) and separate non-generated do not prevent return; connected non-generated and separate generated do prevent return.
Memorize which types block the option.
3
Learn the rule for bay' fasid
All increases allow recovery, except connected non-generated increase.
This is the only barrier in invalid sale.
4
Learn the rule for ruju' fil-hiba
Connected increase (any) prevents revocation; separate increase (any) does not.
Only connected vs separate matters; generation is irrelevant.
5
Learn the rule for ghasb
Only connected non-generated increase that cannot be separated prevents return of the usurped item.
Similar to invalid sale but stricter: it must be inseparable.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن حاصل الزيادة في المهر أنها إذا حدثت بعد قبض المرأة ثم طلقها قبل الدخول فإنها لا تتنصف سواء كانت متصلة متولدة أو منفصلة متولدة أولاً إلا متصلة متولدة عند محمد، وأما إذا حدثت قبل القبض فإن المتولدة تتنصف متصلة أو منفصلة، وغير المتولدة لا تتنصف، وفي خيار العيب الزيادة المتولدة متصلة أو منفصلة غير متولدة فإنها لا تمنع الرد به والمتصلة غير المتولدة والمنفصلة المتولدة يمنعان الرد به وفي البيع الفاسد كل زيادة فإنها لا تمنع الاسترداد والفسخ إلا زيادة متصلة غير متولدة وفي باب الرجوع في الهبة فإن الزيادة المتصلة متولدة أو غير متولدة مانعة من الرجوع والمنفصلة متولدة أو لا غير مانعة، وفي باب الغصب لا يمنع من رد العين إلا الزيادة المتصلة الغير المتولدة التي لا يمكن فصل المغصوب عنها، فلتحفظ هذه المواضع فإنها نفيسة. وأما المتصلة الغير المتولدة كالصبغ في مسألة الزيادة في المهر فخارجة عن البحث واعلم بأن الأوصاف لا تفرد بالعقد ولا تفرد بضمان العقد، والإتلاف يرد على الأوصاف فأمكن إظهار حكم الإتلاف فيها فنقول : إذا حدث في المهر عيب سماوي إن شاءت أخذته ناقصاً بلا غرمه النقصان، وإن شاءت أخذت قوله : (بعد الطلاق (قبله الظرفان متعلقان بأعتق» والضمير في قبلة» للقضاء أو الرضا وأفرد
Then know that the essence of increase in the dower is that if it occurs after the woman's possession, then he divorces her before consummation, then it is not halved, whether it is connected and generated or separate and generated, except connected and generated according to Muhammad. As for if it occurs before possession, then the generated (increase) is halved, whether connected or separate, and the non-generated is not halved. In the option of defect, the generated increase, whether connected or separate and non-generated, does not prevent the return (of the defective item), and the connected non-generated and separate generated prevent the return. In invalid sale, every increase does not prevent recovery and rescission except a connected non-generated increase. In the chapter of revocation of gift, the increase that is connected, whether generated or not, prevents revocation, and the separate increase, whether generated or not, does not prevent. In the chapter of usurpation, nothing prevents the return of the object except the connected non-generated increase that cannot be separated from the usurped item. So memorize these topics, for they are precious. As for the connected non-generated like dye in the issue of increase in the dower, it is outside the discussion. And know that attributes (awsaf) are not singled out by contract nor singled out by the guarantee of the contract, and destruction (itlaf) applies to attributes, so it is possible to manifest the ruling of destruction in them. So we say: If a heavenly defect occurs in the dower, if she wishes, she takes it deficient without charging him for the deficiency, and if she wishes, she takes (the full value?) His statement: (after divorce (before it) the two adverbs are related to 'freeing', and the pronoun in 'before it' refers to the judgment or consent, and it is singular.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a comprehensive summary of the rulings on increases (ziyada) in the context of the dower, and then compares them with other legal chapters. The author begins by stating the rule for increase in the dower: if the increase occurs after the wife has taken possession (qabd) of the dower, and then the husband divorces her before consummation, the increase is not halved with the original—except according to Imam Muhammad, who says that a connected generated increase (ziyada muttasila mutawallida) is halved. If the increase occurs before possession, then generated increases (both connected and separate) are halved, while non-generated increases (like natural growth not due to the property) are not halved. The author then compares this with rulings in other chapters: (1) Option of defect (khiyar al-ayb): A generated increase (whether connected or separate, though non-generated separate does not prevent return) does not prevent the buyer from returning a defective item, but a connected non-generated increase and a separate generated increase do prevent return. (2) Invalid sale (bay' fasid): Any increase does not prevent recovery and rescission except a connected non-generated increase. (3) Revocation of gift (ruju' fil-hiba): Connected increases prevent revocation; separate increases do not. (4) Usurpation (ghasb): Only connected non-generated increases prevent return of the usurped object. The author urges memorization of these rules. He then clarifies that connected non-generated increases (e.g., dye in fabric) are outside the current discussion on dower increase. Finally, he notes that attributes (physical qualities like dye) are not independently transacted but can be subject to compensation if destroyed; if a heavenly defect (not caused by the wife) occurs in the dower, she has the option to keep it with a reduction in price or return it. The last part seems to be a separate comment on a previous passage about the timing of freeing and the pronoun references.

Key Terms
زيادة متصلة متولدة (ziyada muttasila mutawallida): A connected increase that is generated from the object itself, such as fruit from a tree or a calf from a cow.
زيادة منفصلة متولدة (ziyada munfasila mutawallida): A separate increase that is generated from the object, such as a calf after separation from the mother, or rent from a house.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-ayb): The buyer's option to return a defective item to the seller.
الرجوع في الهبة (al-ruju' fil-hiba): The donor's right to revoke a gift under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the chapter of gift revocation (ruju' fil-hiba), which type of increase prevents the donor from revoking the gift?
A) Any connected increase, whether generated or not
B) Any separate increase, whether generated or not
C) Only connected generated increases
D) Only separate non-generated increases

Key Takeaway
The legal effect of an increase depends on the specific chapter; memorize the distinct rule for each.
