Mahr Increases Upon Divorce Before Consummation: A Hanafi Typology
Explaining the legal rules for various types of increases in mahr when divorce occurs before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on mahr increases when divorce occurs before consummation, distinguishing between increases before and after possession, connected/disconnected, and generated/non-generated, and identify the mufta bihi position regarding badal al-manafi.

Core Idea
In divorce before consummation, increases split or stay based on time of possession and whether they are generated or not.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq sharpens the rules on mahr increases. Ibn Nujaym builds a precise typology: the critical fork is before or after possession, and then whether the increase is connected, disconnected, generated, or not. The ruling changes with each combination. Understanding this typology is essential for correctly applying mahr rules in pre-consummation divorce cases and for recognizing the nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute over badal al-manafi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time of the increase
Determine whether the increase occurred before or after the wife's possession (qabd) of the mahr. This is the primary categorization that determines the baseline ruling.
Possession (qabd) refers to the wife taking physical control of the mahr, not merely the contract.
2
Classify the increase type: connected vs. disconnected, generated vs. non-generated
Connected increase (ziyada muttasila) is physically attached to the mahr object (e.g., fattening, growth). Disconnected increase (ziyada munfasila) is separate (e.g., offspring, fruit, earnings). Generated increase (mutawallida) arises from the mahr itself (e.g., offspring of a slave-girl), while non-generated (ghayr mutawallida) is extrinsic (e.g., compensation for defect).
The text gives examples: offspring and fruit are generated disconnected; compensation for defect (arsh) is non-generated disconnected.
3
Apply the split rule for increases before possession
If the increase is generated (mutawallida) – whether connected or disconnected – it splits half to the husband upon divorce. Non-generated increases do not split; they remain entirely with the wife.
This is the general rule. Special case: substitutes for benefits (badal al-manafi) like earnings are treated as non-generated according to Abu Hanifa, but as generated by the Sahibayn.
4
Apply the split rule for increases after possession
After possession, increases generally do not split. The wife keeps the full increase, and the husband gets half the original mahr value (or the original object if it exists). The only exception is connected generated increase according to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, who says it splits; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf disagree.
If the increase perishes, only the original mahr value splits; the increase is not replaced.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute on substitutes for benefits (badal al-manafi)
Abu Hanifa holds that disconnected generated increases that are substitutes for benefits (e.g., rent, earnings, produce) belong entirely to the wife and do not split, even before possession. The Sahibayn consider them part of the mahr for splitting. The mufta bihi position follows Abu Hanifa.
This dispute is highlighted separately in the text and has practical implications for cases where the mahr is a productive asset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو زاد المهر زيادة منفصلة كالولد والثمر والأرش والعقر قبل القبض فكلها تتنصف بالطلاق قبل الدخول، وبعد القبض لا تتنصف وعليها نصف قيمة الأصل يوم قبضت وكذلك لو ارتدت ـ والعياذ بالله تعالى ـ أو قبلت ابن الزوج وإن كانت بدل المنافع كالكسب والغلة والموهوب للمهر فهي للمرأة وليست بمهر عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يتنصف مع الأصل. وكذلك على هذا كسب المبيع قبل القبض ولو آجره الزوج فالأجرة له ولزمه التصدق بها والزيادة المتصلة قبل القبض تتنصف بالإجماع، وبعد القبض تتنصف عند محمد خلافاً لهما، والزيادة المنفصلة بعد القبض إذا هلكت يتنصف الأصل دون الزيادة ولو استولد الزوج الجارية الممهورة قبل القبض وادعى نسب الولد ثم طلقها قبل الدخول تتنصف الجارية والولد لأن العلوق وجد في ملك الغير فلم تصح الدعوة وذكر في كتاب الدعوى أنه يثبت النسب وتصير الجارية أم ولد له لأنه عاد إليه قديم ملكه وعتق نصف الولد بإقراره لأنه جزء منه ويسعى الولد في نصف قيمته للمرأة على الروايتين جميعاً . ثم اعلم أن حاصل الزيادة في المهر أنها إذا حدثت بعد قبض المرأة ثم طلقها قبل الدخول فإنها لا تتنصف سواء كانت متصلة متولدة أو منفصلة متولدة أولاً إلا متصلة متولدة عند محمد، وأما إذا حدثت قبل القبض فإن المتولدة تتنصف متصلة أو منفصلة، وغير المتولدة لا تتنصف، وفي خيار العيب الزيادة المتولدة متصلة أو منفصلة غير متولدة فإنها لا تمنع الرد به والمتصلة غير المتولدة والمنفصلة المتولدة يمنعان الرد به وفي البيع الفاسد كل زيادة فإنها لا تمنع الاسترداد والفسخ إلا زيادة متصلة غير متولدة وفي باب الرجوع في الهبة فإن الزيادة المتصلة متولدة أو غير متولدة مانعة من الرجوع والمنفصلة متولدة أو لا غير مانعة، وفي باب الغصب لا يمنع من رد العين إلا الزيادة المتصلة الغير المتولدة التي لا يمكن فصل المغصوب عنها، فلتحفظ هذه المواضع فإنها نفيسة.
If the mahr increases by a disconnected increase such as offspring, fruit, compensation for defect (arsh), or compensation for intercourse ('uqar) before possession, all of it is split by divorce before consummation. After possession, it is not split, and she must pay half the value of the original on the day she took possession. Likewise if she apostatizes or becomes a foster-son's wife, and if it is a substitute for benefits like earning, produce, or a gift to the mahr, it belongs to her and is not part of the mahr according to Abu Hanifa; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it splits with the original. Similarly for earnings of a sold item before possession. If the husband leases it, the rental is his and he must give it in charity. Connected increase before possession splits by consensus; after possession it splits according to Muhammad, contrary to the two. Disconnected increase after possession, if it perishes, the original splits without the increase. If the husband makes the mahr slave-girl pregnant before possession and claims paternity, then divorces before consummation, the slave-girl and child split, because the conception occurred in another's ownership so the claim is invalid. In the Book of Claims, it is mentioned that paternity is established and she becomes an umm walad for him because his old ownership returns; half the child is freed by his acknowledgment, and the child must earn half its value for the woman on both narrations. Then know that the summary of increase in mahr: if it occurs after the woman's possession, then he divorces before consummation, it does not split, whether connected/generated or disconnected/generated, except connected/generated according to Muhammad. If it occurs before possession, the generated splits whether connected or disconnected; non-generated does not split. In the option of defect, generated increase (connected or disconnected non-generated) does not prevent return; connected non-generated and disconnected generated prevent return. In invalid sale, every increase does not prevent recovery and rescission except connected non-generated increase. In the chapter of revocation of gift, connected increase (generated or not) prevents revocation; disconnected (generated or not) does not prevent. In the chapter of usurpation, nothing prevents return of the object except connected non-generated increase that cannot be separated from the usurped item. Memorize these points, for they are precious.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion on the rulings of increases (ziyada) in the mahr when divorce occurs before consummation (talaq qabl al-dukhul). The author, Ibn Nujaym, distinguishes between different types of increases: connected (muttasila) vs. disconnected (munfasila), and generated (mutawallida) vs. non-generated (ghayr mutawallida). The key time factor is whether the increase occurred before or after the wife's possession (qabda) of the mahr. The general rule: if the increase occurred before possession, the mahr (including the increase) splits half to the husband upon divorce. If after possession, the increase remains with the wife and only the original value of the mahr is considered for splitting. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that disconnected generated increases (like offspring, fruit) that are substitutes for benefits (badal al-manafi) belong entirely to the wife and are not part of the mahr for splitting, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say they do split. The passage also draws comparisons with rulings from other chapters like option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb), invalid sale (bay' fasid), revocation of gift (ruju' fi al-hiba), and usurpation (ghasb) to highlight consistent principles. The final exhortation to memorize these points indicates their importance and subtlety.

Key Terms
زيادة منفصلة (ziyada munfasila): An increase that is separate from the original mahr, such as offspring, fruit, or compensation.
زيادة متصلة (ziyada muttasila): An increase that is physically connected to the original mahr, such as fattening or growth.
بدل المنافع (badal al-manafi): Compensation for benefits or usufruct, such as rent or earnings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They split half to the husband.
B) They are entirely for the wife and do not split.
C) They are returned in full to the husband.
D) They are given in charity.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on mahr increases hinges on three factors: time of possession, connected/disconnected, and generated/non-generated; the position of Imam Abu Hanifa on 'badal al-manafi' is the mufta bihi.

The Twenty Defects and Eight Increases: Classifying Mahr Scenarios
Enumerating the twenty types of defects and eight types of increases, then applying rulings to specific scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the five causes and four loci of defects in mahr, and the two-by-two classification of increases, and derive the total counts of 20 defects and 8 increases.

Core Idea
Defects in mahr are classified by cause and location; increases are classified by connectivity and generation — these categories dictate the ruling upon divorce.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a systematic classification of defects and increases that can occur in the mahr before consummation. The author derives 20 types of defects (5 causes × 4 loci) and 8 types of increases (2 connectivity × 2 generation × 2 possession). This taxonomy is not merely theoretical; it provides the framework for determining how much the wife takes back upon divorce. Let us understand this classification step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five causes of defects
The author lists five causes: a heavenly calamity, the husband's action, the wife's action, the mahr's own action, or a third party's action. Each cause can affect the mahr in different ways.
These causes cover all possible sources of defect.
2
Identify the four loci of defects
The defect can occur in four contexts: in the husband's possession, in her possession before divorce, in her possession after divorce but before the judge's ruling to return it, or after the ruling. Multiplying the five causes by these four loci gives twenty types.
The author notes that if we consider 'in husband's hand' includes both before and after divorce, the count becomes 25.
3
Classify increases by connectivity and generation
Increases are either connected (muttasil) or disconnected (munfasil), and either generated (mutawallid) or not generated (ghayr mutawallid). The author also considers whether the increase occurs in the husband's hand or the wife's hand. This gives a total of 8 types.
Connected non-generated increase (like dye) does not split, as stated.
4
Understand that these categories govern the rulings
The author mentions that the rulings for each type are known from the earlier discussion. This classification is the foundation for the specific cases that follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصار حاصل وجوه النقصان عشرين، لأنه إما أن يكون بآفة سماوية أو بفعله أو بفعلها أو بفعل المهر أو بفعل الأجنبي، وكل من الخمسة على أربعة لأنه إما أن يكون في يد الزوج أو في يدها قبل الطلاق أو في يدها بعده قبل الحكم بالرد أو بعده بعد الحكم وأحكامها مذكورة، كما أن حاصل وجوه الزيادة ثمانية لأنها إما أن تكون متصلة متولدة أو لا، أو منفصلة متولدة أو لا، وكل منها إما أن تكون في يده أو في يدها والأحكام مذكورة إلا حكم المتصلة الغير المتولدة كالصبغ لظهور أنها لا تتنصف، تكون وجوه النقصان خمسة وعشرين فإن النقصان في يد الزوج أعم من أن يكون قبل الطلاق أو بعده فهي خمسة في خمسة. وإذا ولدت الجارية الممهورة في يد الزوج فهلكا ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها أخذت نصف قيمة الأم لا غير، وإن قتلهما الزوج فإن شاءت ضمنته العقد، وإن شاءت ضمنت عاقلته نصف قيمتها وتضمن العاقلة نصف نصف قيمة الأم يوم قيمة الولد يوم القتل ولا يضمن الزوج نقصان الولادة إلا أن يكون فاحشاً. ولو تزوجها على زرع بقل فاستحصد الزرع في يدها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها فلا سبيل للزوج على الزرع، ولو تزوجها على عشرين شاة عجفاء فحملت في يدها ودر اللبن في ضروعها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها يأخذ الزوج نصفها ، ولو تزوجها على أرض قراح على أنها ثلاثون جريباً فإذا هي عشرون إن شاءت أخذت القراح ناقصاً لا غير، وإن شاءت أخذت قيمته ثلاثين جريباً مثل هذه الأرض، ولو تزوجها على نخل صغار فطالت وكبرت في يدها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها فلها نصفها. نص عليها في المنتفى. قال رحمه الله : وعندي هذا محمول على قول محمد لأن المذهب عنده أن الزيادة المتصلة لا تمنع التنصيف ا هـ . ما في الظهيرية بحروفه.
So the total types of defects become twenty, because it is either by a heavenly calamity, by his action, by her action, by the mahr's action, or by a third party's action; and each of the five is multiplied by four because it occurs either in the husband's hand, in her hand before divorce, in her hand after divorce before the ruling of return, or after the ruling, and their rulings are mentioned. Similarly, the total types of increases are eight because they are either connected/generated or not, or disconnected/generated or not, and each is either in his hand or her hand, and their rulings are mentioned except for connected non-generated increase like dye, as it is obvious that it does not split. The types of defects become twenty-five, because defect in the husband's hand includes both before and after divorce, so it is five times five. If the mahr slave-girl gives birth in the husband's hand and both die, then he divorces before consummation, she takes half the mother's value only. If the husband kills them both, if she wills she holds him liable for the contract value; if she wills she holds his 'aqila liable for half their value, the 'aqila being liable for half the half of the mother's value and the child's value on the day of killing, and the husband is not liable for the deficiency of birth unless it is gross. If he marries her on a crop of greens that ripens in her hand, then divorces before consummation, the husband has no claim on the crop. If he marries her on twenty lean sheep that become pregnant in her hand and milk flows in their udders, then divorces before consummation, the husband takes half of them. If he marries her on a cleared land said to be thirty jaribs but it is twenty, if she wills she takes the land defective only; if she wills she takes its value as thirty jaribs of such land. If he marries her on small palm trees that grow tall and large in her hand, then divorces before consummation, she gets half of them. This is stated in al-Muntafa. He (the author) said: In my view, this is based on Muhammad's opinion, because his madhhab is that connected increase does not prevent splitting. End of what is in al-Zahiriyya verbatim.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage provides a systematic enumeration of the categories of defects and increases in the context of mahr upon divorce before consummation, followed by specific case examples. The author calculates that there are twenty types of defects (five causes × four locations relative to possession and ruling) and eight types of increases (two connectivity states × two generated states × two possession states). He notes that the ruling for connected non-generated increases (like dye) is obvious: they do not split. Then he gives practical examples: (1) A mahr slave-girl gives birth and both die; the wife takes only half the mother's value. (2) If the husband kills them, the wife can choose to claim the contract value from the husband or hold his 'aqila (tribal group) liable for half the combined value. (3) If the mahr is greens (zar' baql) that ripen, the husband gets nothing. (4) If the mahr is lean sheep that become pregnant and produce milk, the husband takes half the sheep. (5) If the mahr is land claimed to be 30 jaribs but found to be 20, the wife chooses to take the land defective or its value as 30 jaribs. (6) If the mahr is small palm trees that grow, the wife takes half. The author cites al-Muntafa and clarifies that this last case follows Muhammad's view that connected increase does not prevent splitting. The passage is a summary and application of the earlier principles.

Key Terms
وجوه النقصان (wujuh al-nuqsan): The types of defects categorized by cause and location for the purpose of legal rulings.
عاقلة ('aqila): The tribe or group responsible for paying blood money (diyat) on behalf of a member who commits homicide.
منتفى (al-Muntafa): A Hanafi legal text, possibly a reference to al-Muntafa fi al-Fatawa or similar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 8
C) 10
D) 16

Key Takeaway
The systematic classification of defects and increases in mahr provides a clear framework for determining the wife's entitlement upon divorce before consummation.

Applying the Rules: Specific Cases of Mahr Defects and Increases
Enumerating the twenty types of defects and eight types of increases, then applying rulings to specific scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the classification of defects and increases to determine the correct ruling in scenarios such as death of mahr, killing by husband, ripening crops, and growth of trees.

Core Idea
Each specific scenario falls into one of the classified categories, and the ruling follows from that category.

After establishing the taxonomy, the author provides six practical examples that illustrate how the rules play out. These examples cover a range of situations: death of a slave-girl, killing by the husband, natural increase in livestock and crops, hidden defects in land, and growth of trees. By working through these examples, we see how the classification directly determines the wife's entitlement to the mahr upon divorce before consummation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and categorize the defect/increase
For each example, first determine whether the change in the mahr is a defect or increase, its cause, location, and if increase, whether connected/disconnected and generated/non-generated. Use the taxonomy from Lesson 1.
For the slave-girl example, the defect is death from natural causes (heavenly) in husband's hand. For the killing, it is a defect by husband's action in his hand.
2
Recall the general ruling for that category
The general ruling for a defect in the husband's hand is that the wife takes half the value at the time of the defect. For increases, connected non-generated do not split, while others may split depending on the hand.
The author refers to 'the rulings are mentioned' from prior sections.
3
Apply the ruling to the specific facts
Apply the general ruling to each scenario. For example, if the mahr slave-girl dies in the husband's hand, the wife takes half her value at death. If the husband kills her, she has an option to claim full contract value from him or half from his 'aqila.
Note the special option in the killing case: the wife can choose.
4
Identify any intra-madhhab differences
The last example (palm trees growing) is noted to follow Muhammad's view that connected increase does not prevent splitting. This indicates an ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, as some may hold that such increase belongs to the wife entirely.
The author adopts Muhammad's view, which is the position applied in this case.

فصار حاصل وجوه النقصان عشرين، لأنه إما أن يكون بآفة سماوية أو بفعله أو بفعلها أو بفعل المهر أو بفعل الأجنبي، وكل من الخمسة على أربعة لأنه إما أن يكون في يد الزوج أو في يدها قبل الطلاق أو في يدها بعده قبل الحكم بالرد أو بعده بعد الحكم وأحكامها مذكورة، كما أن حاصل وجوه الزيادة ثمانية لأنها إما أن تكون متصلة متولدة أو لا، أو منفصلة متولدة أو لا، وكل منها إما أن تكون في يده أو في يدها والأحكام مذكورة إلا حكم المتصلة الغير المتولدة كالصبغ لظهور أنها لا تتنصف، تكون وجوه النقصان خمسة وعشرين فإن النقصان في يد الزوج أعم من أن يكون قبل الطلاق أو بعده فهي خمسة في خمسة. وإذا ولدت الجارية الممهورة في يد الزوج فهلكا ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها أخذت نصف قيمة الأم لا غير، وإن قتلهما الزوج فإن شاءت ضمنته العقد، وإن شاءت ضمنت عاقلته نصف قيمتها وتضمن العاقلة نصف نصف قيمة الأم يوم قيمة الولد يوم القتل ولا يضمن الزوج نقصان الولادة إلا أن يكون فاحشاً. ولو تزوجها على زرع بقل فاستحصد الزرع في يدها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها فلا سبيل للزوج على الزرع، ولو تزوجها على عشرين شاة عجفاء فحملت في يدها ودر اللبن في ضروعها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها يأخذ الزوج نصفها ، ولو تزوجها على أرض قراح على أنها ثلاثون جريباً فإذا هي عشرون إن شاءت أخذت القراح ناقصاً لا غير، وإن شاءت أخذت قيمته ثلاثين جريباً مثل هذه الأرض، ولو تزوجها على نخل صغار فطالت وكبرت في يدها ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها فلها نصفها. نص عليها في المنتفى. قال رحمه الله : وعندي هذا محمول على قول محمد لأن المذهب عنده أن الزيادة المتصلة لا تمنع التنصيف ا هـ . ما في الظهيرية بحروفه.
So the total types of defects become twenty, because it is either by a heavenly calamity, by his action, by her action, by the mahr's action, or by a third party's action; and each of the five is multiplied by four because it occurs either in the husband's hand, in her hand before divorce, in her hand after divorce before the ruling of return, or after the ruling, and their rulings are mentioned. Similarly, the total types of increases are eight because they are either connected/generated or not, or disconnected/generated or not, and each is either in his hand or her hand, and their rulings are mentioned except for connected non-generated increase like dye, as it is obvious that it does not split. The types of defects become twenty-five, because defect in the husband's hand includes both before and after divorce, so it is five times five. If the mahr slave-girl gives birth in the husband's hand and both die, then he divorces before consummation, she takes half the mother's value only. If the husband kills them both, if she wills she holds him liable for the contract value; if she wills she holds his 'aqila liable for half their value, the 'aqila being liable for half the half of the mother's value and the child's value on the day of killing, and the husband is not liable for the deficiency of birth unless it is gross. If he marries her on a crop of greens that ripens in her hand, then divorces before consummation, the husband has no claim on the crop. If he marries her on twenty lean sheep that become pregnant in her hand and milk flows in their udders, then divorces before consummation, the husband takes half of them. If he marries her on a cleared land said to be thirty jaribs but it is twenty, if she wills she takes the land defective only; if she wills she takes its value as thirty jaribs of such land. If he marries her on small palm trees that grow tall and large in her hand, then divorces before consummation, she gets half of them. This is stated in al-Muntafa. He (the author) said: In my view, this is based on Muhammad's opinion, because his madhhab is that connected increase does not prevent splitting. End of what is in al-Zahiriyya verbatim.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage provides a systematic enumeration of the categories of defects and increases in the context of mahr upon divorce before consummation, followed by specific case examples. The author calculates that there are twenty types of defects (five causes × four locations relative to possession and ruling) and eight types of increases (two connectivity states × two generated states × two possession states). He notes that the ruling for connected non-generated increases (like dye) is obvious: they do not split. Then he gives practical examples: (1) A mahr slave-girl gives birth and both die; the wife takes only half the mother's value. (2) If the husband kills them, the wife can choose to claim the contract value from the husband or hold his 'aqila (tribal group) liable for half the combined value. (3) If the mahr is greens (zar' baql) that ripen, the husband gets nothing. (4) If the mahr is lean sheep that become pregnant and produce milk, the husband takes half the sheep. (5) If the mahr is land claimed to be 30 jaribs but found to be 20, the wife chooses to take the land defective or its value as 30 jaribs. (6) If the mahr is small palm trees that grow, the wife takes half. The author cites al-Muntafa and clarifies that this last case follows Muhammad's view that connected increase does not prevent splitting. The passage is a summary and application of the earlier principles.

Key Terms
وجوه النقصان (wujuh al-nuqsan): The types of defects categorized by cause and location for the purpose of legal rulings.
عاقلة ('aqila): The tribe or group responsible for paying blood money (diyat) on behalf of a member who commits homicide.
منتفى (al-Muntafa): A Hanafi legal text, possibly a reference to al-Muntafa fi al-Fatawa or similar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where the husband kills the mahr slave-girl and her child, what is the liability of the 'aqila?
A) Full value of the mother and child.
B) Half the value of the mother plus half the value of the child.
C) Only half the value of the mother.
D) Nothing, because the husband is fully liable.

Key Takeaway
The specific rulings for mahr defects and increases follow logically from the systematic classification, and each case is determined by its category and the controlling hand.

Nikah — Marriage

Defects and Increases in Mahr After Divorce Before Consummation
Detailed enumeration of defect and increase scenarios with rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on half-mahr after divorce before consummation and distinguish the wife's options for compensation based on the cause and timing of a defect in the mahr.

Core Idea
After divorce before consummation, half the mahr falls; defects and increases are split according to cause and possession.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq systematically maps the rulings for when the mahr changes value before the marriage is consummated. The key rule: half of the specified mahr is due to the wife upon divorce before consummation. But what happens if the mahr itself is defective, destroyed, or increases? The author categorizes twenty defect scenarios and eight increase scenarios based on who caused the change and whether the wife had taken possession. Understanding these branches helps you see how the principle 'half falls' applies in real cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base rule
State the Hanafi rule: after divorce before consummation, half the mahr is fixed as a right of the wife; the other half falls. This is the governing principle for all subsequent scenarios.
This rule is derived from Quran 2:237 and is wajib.
2
Classify the defect by cause
For each defect, identify the cause: heavenly calamity, husband's act, wife's act, act of the mahr itself, or outsider's act. The cause determines whether the wife can claim compensation from the husband or must seek it from the outsider.
The passage lists five causes.
3
Consider the hand of possession
Determine whether the wife has taken possession (qabd) of the mahr at the time of the defect. This affects the husband's liability. For example, if the defect occurs while the mahr is still in the husband's hand, the wife's options differ.
Possession transfers liability for certain defects.
4
Apply the timing of divorce and ruling of return
Check whether the defect occurs before divorce, after divorce but before a judicial ruling of return, or after such ruling. Different rules apply to each period, especially regarding the husband's right to take the mahr with compensation.
See the four time periods for each cause (hand of husband, hand of wife before divorce, hand of wife after divorce before ruling, after ruling).
5
Handle increases: connected vs. disconnected
For increases, distinguish connected (e.g., growth, dyeing) from disconnected (e.g., fruit, rent). Connected increases that are inseparable do not prevent splitting; the increase is included proportionally. Disconnected increases are split separately.
Imam Muhammad holds that connected increases do not prevent splitting; this is the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أخذته قيمته من الزوج ولا حق لها في النقصان. وإن حدث بفعل المهر فكالآفة السماوية في رواية، وفي ظاهر الرواية هو كحكم جناية الزوج، والحدوث بفعل المهر أن يكون المهر عبداً فقطع يده أو فقأ عينه، وإذا قبضت المهر فتعيب بفعلها أو بآفة سماوية أو بفعل المهر قبل الطلاق أو بعده قبل الحكم بالرد فإن شاء الزوج أخذ نصفه ولا يضمنها النقصان، وإن شاء ضمنها نصف قيمته صحيحاً . القبض، وإن كان ذلك بعد الطلاق والحكم بالرد فللزوج أن يأخذه ونصف الأرش، وإن تعيب بفعل الأجنبي يضمنها نصف القيمة لا غير وإن تعيب بفعل الزوج فهو بالخيار كما في الأجنبي. كذا في الظهيرية. فصار حاصل وجوه النقصان عشرين، لأنه إما أن يكون بآفة كما أن حاصل وجوه الزيادة ثمانية لأنها إما أن تكون متصلة متولدة أو لا، أو منفصلة متولدة أو لا، وكل منها إما أن تكون في يده أو في يدها والأحكام مذكورة إلا حكم المتصلة الغير المتولدة كالصبغ لظهور أنها لا تتنصف، تكون وجوه النقصان خمسة وعشرين فإن النقصان في يد الزوج أعم من أن يكون قبل الطلاق أو بعده فهي خمسة في خمسة. وإذا ولدت الجارية الممهورة في يد الزوج فهلكا ثم طلقها قبل الدخول بها أخذت نصف قيمة الأم لا غير، وإن قتلهما الزوج فإن شاءت ضمنته العقد، وإن شاءت ضمنت عاقلته نصف قيمتها وتضمن العاقلة نصف نصف قيمة الأم يوم قيمة الولد يوم القتل ولا يضمن الزوج نقصان الولادة إلا أن يكون فاحشاً. ولو تزوجها على فائدة فيه وأن طريق أصحابنا هو الأول. وذكر الاختلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد في الرهن ؛ فعند محمد هو رهن بها، وعند أبي يوسف لا . وفي القنية : افترقا فقالت افترقنا بعد الدخول. وقال الزوج قبل الدخول فالقول إذا ارتفع السبب يعود إلى ملك القاضي إن كان بغير أمره وتمامه فيها من كتاب المداينات .
Its value on the day of the contract. If the defect occurs by the husband's action, then if she wishes she takes it and the value of the decrease, and if she wishes she takes its value on the day of the contract. And if it occurs by the husband's action she becomes a possessor. If it occurs by an outsider's action, then if she wishes she takes it and the value of the decrease from the outsider, and if she wishes she takes its value from the husband and she has no right to the decrease. If it occurs by the action of the mahr itself, then it is like a heavenly calamity in one narration, and in the well-known narration it is like the ruling of the husband's injury. The occurrence by the action of the mahr is when the mahr is a slave and he cuts his hand or gouges his eye. When she has taken possession of the mahr and it becomes defective by her action, or by a heavenly calamity, or by the action of the mahr before divorce or after it but before the ruling of return, then if the husband wishes he takes half of it and does not guarantee the decrease, and if he wishes he guarantees half of its value sound. If that was after divorce and after the ruling of return, then the husband may take it and half the compensation. If it becomes defective by an outsider's action, he guarantees half the value only. If it becomes defective by the husband's action, he has the choice as with the outsider. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. So the total aspects of decrease become twenty: because either it is by a heavenly calamity, or by his action, or by her action, or by the action of the mahr, or by the action of an outsider. And each of the five is over four: because either it is in the husband's hand, or in her hand before divorce, or in her hand after divorce but before the ruling of return, or after the ruling of return. Their rulings are mentioned. Similarly, the total aspects of increase are eight: because either it is connected and generated, or not; or disconnected and generated, or not. And each of them is either in his hand or in her hand, and the rulings are mentioned except the ruling of connected non-generated increase like dyeing, as it is apparent that it is not split. The aspects of decrease become twenty-five, for the decrease in the husband's hand is general whether before or after divorce—so it is five times five. If the female slave given as mahr gives birth in the husband's hand and they both die, then he divorces her before consummation, she takes half the value of the mother only. If the husband kills them both, then if she wishes she makes him liable for the contract value, and if she wishes she makes his 'aaila liable for half its value. The 'aaila guarantees half the value of the mother on the day of the killing and the value of the child on the day of the killing. The husband does not guarantee the defect of childbirth unless it is excessive. If he married her on growing crops that ripened in her hand, then he divorces her before consummation, the husband has no way to the crops. If he married her on twenty skinny sheep that became pregnant in her hand and milk appeared in their udders, then he divorces her before consummation, the husband takes half of them. If he married her on a piece of land said to be thirty jaribs, but it turned out to be twenty, she may take the land with the deficiency only, or take its value as thirty jaribs of similar land. If he married her on small date palms that grew tall in her hand, then he divorces her before consummation, she has half of them. This is stated in al-Muntaha. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): In my view, this is taken to be according to Muhammad's view, for the school in his view is that connected increase does not prevent splitting. End quote from al-Zahiriyya verbatim. And it should be that the case of the sheep is like the case of the date palms, taken according to Muhammad's view. And the apparent meaning of al-Mukhtasar is that by divorce before consummation half of the mahr falls and half remains, which is the view of the verifying scholars. It is also said that all of it falls and half the mahr is obligatory by way of gift, and this was chosen in al-Hidaya in the chapter of retracting from testimonies. He said in al-Jawhara: The benefit is that if he married her for one hundred dirhams and pledged a pledge for it, then divorced her, according to the first view she may keep the pledge, and according to the second she may not. In al-Bada'i' the view that all falls is weak. Then making half obligatory has no benefit, and our colleagues' way is the first. And the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the pledge is mentioned: according to Muhammad it is a pledge for it, and according to Abu Yusuf it is not. In al-Qunniya: They separated: she said 'We separated after consummation', and the husband said 'Before consummation', the sayings are from her because she denies the fall of half the mahr. Also in it: If someone voluntarily paid the mahr on behalf of the husband, then he divorced her before consummation, or separation came from her side, half the mahr in the first case and the whole in the second returns to the husband's ownership, unlike the one who voluntarily pays a debt if the cause is removed, it returns to the ownership of the judge if it was without his order. Its completion is in the Book of Loans.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings of defects and increases in the mahr after divorce before consummation. The author systematically categorizes scenarios by the cause of change—heavenly calamity, husband's act, wife's act, act of the mahr itself, or outsider's act—and by the hand holding the mahr at the time. For each, the wife's options are detailed. The underlying principle is that after possession, the mahr becomes the wife's property; if it is still in the husband's hand, different rules apply. The passage also addresses connected vs. disconnected increases and gives examples like a pregnant slave, sheep, land, and date palms. An intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: Imam Muhammad holds that connected increases do not prevent splitting, while the majority (including the matn author) hold that half the mahr falls and half remains. Practical consequences appear in cases like a pledged mahr: if half falls, the wife keeps the pledge; if all falls, she does not.

Key Terms
نقصان (nuqsān): A defect or decrease in the value of the mahr after possession and before or after divorce.
زيادة (ziyādah): An increase in the mahr, either connected (e.g., growth) or disconnected (e.g., fruit), affecting its division after divorce.
قبض (qabḍ): Taking possession of the mahr, which transfers it to the wife's ownership and affects subsequent rulings.
حكم الرد (ḥukm al-radd): The judicial ruling that the mahr is returned due to a defect or other cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a defect in the mahr occurs by the action of an outsider while the mahr is in the wife's possession before divorce, which options does the wife have?
A) She may either take the defective mahr and claim compensation from the outsider, or take its full value from the husband without any decrease claim.
B) She must take the full value from the husband, and the husband then claims from the outsider.
C) She can only take the defective mahr and must pursue the outsider for compensation.
D) The husband has the choice to either take half the mahr or compensate half its value.

Key Takeaway
After divorce before consummation, half the specified mahr is fixed; the wife's options for defects and increases depend on the cause and whether she has taken possession.

Ruling When Mahr Is Not Named or Is Negated: Mahr Misl
Commentary on the matn ruling with proof and multiple examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when it is not named or invalid, identify the conditions that trigger mahr misl, and apply the ruling to various invalid mahr scenarios.

Core Idea
If no mahr is named or the specification is invalid, the wife is entitled to mahr misl upon consummation or death.

Marriage contracts often include a specified dower (mahr). But what happens if the mahr is omitted, explicitly negated, or specified in an invalid way? The Hanafi school holds that the marriage remains valid, and the wife is entitled to mahr misl – the dower of women of her standing – once the marriage is consummated or the husband dies. This lesson examines the proof from the Sunnah and works through numerous examples that clarify when mahr misl applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
Read the matn statement: if the mahr is not named or negated, the wife gets mahr misl IF consummation (wat') occurs or the husband dies. This establishes the hukm level of wajib.
The condition is either consummation or death, not both.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq: a man married and died without setting a mahr; the Prophet ruled she gets full dower, must observe 'idda, and inherits. This proves mahr is obligatory even without specification.
The hadith is hasan sahih according to al-Tirmidhi.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit judgment that the woman receives the full dower implies that mahr is a right inherent in the contract. The absence of specification does not void the obligation; rather, the mahr misl fills the gap.
This is a qat'i dalala even though the hadith is ahad in transmission.
4
Explore the examples of invalid specifications
The commentary lists many cases: conditional exchange of equal amounts, marriage on a bride's own slave, mahr stated as 'permissible', on the judgment of a third party, on an unborn animal, on a conditional gift to the father, on simply 'dirhams', on something forbidden, or on something completely unknown. In all, the specification is invalid so mahr misl is due.
The pattern: any specification that is uncertain, impossible, or unlawful triggers mahr misl.
5
Contrast with valid scenarios and effects
If the mahr is validly specified (lawful, known, owned by husband), that amount is the mahr. The wife may waive mahr after the contract but cannot negate it. If the husband gives a gift to the father as part of the contract, he can revoke it.
Mahr is a Shari'a right; it becomes a debt once due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن لم يسمه أو نفاه فلها مهر مثلها إن وطئ أو مات عنها) لما روي في السنن والجامع الترمذي عن عبد الله بن مسعود في رجل تزوج امرأة فمات عنها ولم يدخل بها ولم يفرض لها الصداق فقال لها الصداق كاملاً وعليها العدة ولها الميراث فقال معقل بن سنان : سمعت رسول الله الله قضى به في تزويج بنت واشق . قال الترمذي : هو حسن صحيح. ولأنه حق الشرع وجوباً وإنما يصير حقها في حالة البقاء فتملك الإبراء دون النفي ومن صوره ما إذا تزوجها على ألف على أن ترد إليه ألفاً لأن الألف بمقابلة مثلها فبقي النكاح بلا تسمية كما في المحيط ومنها ما إذا تزوجها على عبدها وليس منها ما إذا تزوجها على عبد الغير فإنه إذا لم يجز مالكه وجبت قيمته ومنها ما في القنية قالت زوجت نفسي منك بخمسين ديناراً وأبرأتك من الخمسين فقال قبلت ينعقد بمهر المثل لعدم التسمية. ومنها ما فيها : تزوجتك بمهر جائز في الشرع وجب مهر المثل ولا ينصرف إلى العشرة لأن مهر المثل جائز شرعاً أيضاً، وفي المعراج لها العشرة. ومنها ما إذا تزوجها على حكمها أو حكمه أو في حكم رجل آخر أو على ما في بطن جاريتي أو أغنامي كما في فتح القدير. ومنها ما الظهيرية : لو تزوجها على أن يهب الزوج لأبيها ألف درهم كان لها مهر المثل. وهب لأبيها ألفاً أو لم يهب، فإن وهب كان له أن يرجع في الهبة. ومنها ما فيها أيضاً: لو تزوجها على دراهم كان لها مهر المثل ولا يشبه الخلع ومنها تسمية المحرم ومنها تسمية المجهولة جهالة قوله : (قضى به في تزويج بنت واشق) الذي في الفتح قضى في بروع بنت واشق بمثله وقال : هذا لفظ أبي داود وله روايات أخر بألفاظ وذكر قبله «وبروع» بكسر الباء الموحدة في المشهور ويروى بفتحها قوله : (ومنها ما فيها) أي في القنية .
His statement: (And if he did not name it or negated it, then she has her mahr misl if he had intercourse with her or died upon her) because of what was narrated in al-Sunan and Jami' al-Tirmidhi from 'Abd Allah b. Mas'ud regarding a man who married a woman, then died upon her without having consummated and without fixing a dower: he said she has the full dower, she must observe 'idda, and she has inheritance. Ma'qil b. Sinan said: I heard the Messenger of Allah rule so in the marriage of Bint Washiq. Al-Tirmidhi said: It is hasan sahih. And because it is a right of the Shari'a by obligation; it becomes her right in the state of survival; so she may waive it but not negate it. Among its forms are: if he married her on one thousand on condition that she give him back one thousand, because the thousand is in exchange for its similar, so the marriage remains without specification as in al-Muhit. Among them: if he married her on her own slave, but not if he married her on another's slave, for if its owner does not consent, its value becomes obligatory. Among them is what is in al-Qunniya: she said 'I married myself to you for fifty dinars and I exonerate you from the fifty' and he said 'I accept,' then it is concluded with mahr misl due to lack of specification. Among them: 'I married you for a mahr permissible in the Shari'a,' then mahr misl is obligatory, and it does not refer to ten (dirhams) because mahr misl is also permissible in the Shari'a, and in al-Mi'raj she has ten. Among them: if he married her on her own judgment, or his judgment, or the judgment of another man, or on what is in the belly of my slave girl or my sheep, as in Fath al-Qadir. Among them is in al-Zahiriyya: if he married her on condition that the husband give her father one thousand dirhams, she has mahr misl, whether he gave the thousand or not; if he gave, he may revoke the gift. Among them also: if he married her on dirhams, she has mahr misl, and it is not like khul'. Among them: the naming of something forbidden, and the naming of something unknown with extreme ignorance. His statement: (he ruled so in the marriage of Bint Washiq) what is in al-Fath is that he ruled in the case of Barwa' bint Washiq similarly, and he said: this is the wording of Abu Dawud, and he has other narrations with different wordings. He mentioned before: 'Barwa'' with kasr of the ba' is well-known, and it is also narrated with fatha. His statement: (Among them is what is in it) i.e., in al-Qunniya.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn ruling that when the mahr is not named or is explicitly negated, the wife is entitled to mahr misl (the dower of her peers) if consummation occurred or if the husband died. The proof is a hadith from 'Abd Allah b. Mas'ud regarding a man who died without setting a mahr: the Prophet ruled that the woman gets full mahr, 'idda, and inheritance. The hadith is hasan sahih. The principle is that the mahr is a Shari'a right that becomes incumbent by marriage; it cannot be negated but can be waived. The commentary then lists numerous examples of invalid or unspecified mahr designations: a conditional exchange of equal amounts, marriage on a bride's own slave (if the slave is not owned by the husband, it is invalid), a mahr expressed as 'permissible', marriage on the judgment of a third party, on an unborn animal, on a conditional gift to the father, on simply 'dirhams', on something forbidden, or on something completely unknown. In all such cases, the contract is valid but the wife receives mahr misl. The scholar also clarifies the name of the woman in the hadith (Barwa' bint Washiq) and cites al-Fath's notes.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to that given to women of similar status (family, beauty, wealth, etc.) in the community.
تسمية (tasmiyah): The specification of a mahr amount or item in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man marries a woman saying 'I marry you on the condition that you give me 500 dirhams' and she accepts. What is the mahr?
A) The 500 dirhams is the mahr.
B) The marriage is invalid because the mahr is a debt on the wife.
C) The wife is entitled to mahr misl because the mahr specification is invalid.
D) No mahr is due because it was not named for the husband.

Key Takeaway
When the mahr is not named or is invalid, the wife is still entitled to mahr misl upon consummation or death, because mahr is a Shari'a right that cannot be negated.

Half the Mahr Falls Upon Divorce Before Consummation: Resolving an Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr after divorce before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi Hanafi ruling on the mahr after divorce before consummation and explain the practical difference arising from the minority view.

Core Idea
Half the mahr remains after divorce before consummation; the wife keeps any pledge given.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of divorce before consummation on the mahr. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) holds that half the specified mahr falls and half remains owed. A minority view holds that the entire mahr falls and half becomes wajib as mut'ah. Understanding the impact on a pledged mahr reveals the practical significance of the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the majority and minority positions
The majority (verifying scholars) say half falls and half remains; the minority says all falls and half as mut'ah.
2
Examine the thamarah (practical consequence)
The key difference emerges when a pledge (rahn) was given for the mahr: the wife may keep the pledge according to the majority view.
3
Note the additional intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on the validity of the pledge itself for the mahr.
4
Apply the ruling to donation and dispute scenarios
If someone donated the mahr, half returns to the donor upon divorce before consummation; if the wife disputes the timing, her word is accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن تكون مسألة الشاة كمسألة النخل محمولة على قول محمد، وظاهر ما في المختصر أن بالطلاق قبل الدخول يسقط نصف المهر ويبقى النصف وهو قول المحققين. وقيل يسقط كله ويجب نصف المهر بطريق المتعة واختاره في الهداية في باب الرجوع عن الشهادات . قال في الجوهرة: وفائدته أنه لو تزوجها على مائة درهم ورهنها بها رهناً ثم طلقها، فعلى القول الأول لها إمساك الرهن، وعلى الثاني لا ا هـ . وفي البدائع : ضعف القول بسقوط الكل. ثم إيجاب النصف بأنه لا فائدة فيه وأن طريق أصحابنا هو الأول. وذكر الاختلاف بين أبي يوسف ومحمد في الرهن ؛ فعند محمد هو رهن بها، وعند أبي يوسف لا . وفي القنية : افترقا فقالت افترقنا بعد الدخول. وقال الزوج قبل الدخول فالقول قولها لأنها تنكر سقوط نصف المهر هـ. وفيها أيضاً : لو تبرع بالمهر عن الزوج ثم طلقها قبل الدخول أو جاءت الفرقة من قبلها يعود نصف المهر في الأول والكل في الثاني إلى ملك الزوج بخلاف المتبرع بقضاء الدين إذا ارتفع السبب يعود إلى ملك القاضي إن كان بغير أمره وتمامه فيها من كتاب المداينات .
The issue of the sheep is like the issue of the palm trees, carried on the saying of Muhammad. The apparent in al-Mukhtasar is that by divorce before consummation, half of the mahr falls and half remains, and that is the saying of the verifying scholars. And it was said: it all falls and half the mahr becomes obligatory by way of mut'ah, and it was chosen in al-Hidayah in the chapter of retracting from testimonies. Al-Jawharah said: Its benefit is that if he married her for one hundred dirhams and gave a pledge for it, then divorced her, according to the first saying she may keep the pledge, and according to the second not. In al-Bada'i': The saying of total fall is weak, then obligating half is useless, and the way of our companions is the first. And the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the pledge is mentioned; according to Muhammad it is a pledge for it, and according to Abu Yusuf no. In al-Qunyah: They separated, and she said we separated after consummation, and the husband said before consummation, so her word is accepted because she denies the fall of half the mahr. Also in it: If someone donated the mahr on behalf of the husband, then he divorced her before consummation, or separation occurred from her side, half the mahr returns in the first and all in the second to the husband's ownership, unlike the one who donated to pay a debt if the cause ceases, it returns to the ownership of the judge if it was without his order, and its completion is in the Book of Loans.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of divorce before consummation on the mahr. The author first notes that according to the verifying scholars (al-muhaqqiqun), half the mahr falls and half remains as the mufta bihi view. A minority view claims that the entire mahr falls and half becomes wajib as mut'ah, but al-Bada'i' weakens this, stating that obligating half is useless and the relied-upon position is the first. The practical difference appears in a case of a pledged item: if the mahr was secured by a pledge, the first view entitles the wife to keep the pledge (since half mahr remains her right), while the second view denies her that. The author then notes a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Muhammad considers the pledge valid for the mahr, while Abu Yusuf does not. Additionally, in a case of dispute about when separation occurred, the wife's word is taken because she denies the fall of half mahr. Finally, the text covers a scenario where someone donates the mahr: if the husband divorces before consummation, half returns to him; if separation is from the wife, all returns. The lesson ends with a cross-reference to the Book of Loans.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A pledge given as security for a debt or obligation, here for the mahr.
متعة (mut'ah): A consolation gift given to a divorced woman when no mahr was specified or before consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, what happens to the mahr when a husband divorces his wife before consummation?
A) The entire mahr falls and she gets nothing.
B) Half the mahr falls and half remains owed to the wife.
C) The entire mahr is owed and she must return half.
D) The mahr becomes a loan.

Key Takeaway
Upon divorce before consummation, the Hanafi mufta bihi is that half the mahr remains owed, and a pledge given for the mahr may be kept by the wife.

Mahr al-Mithl: The Dower When No Mahr Is Specified
Ruling with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of mahr al-mithl when no mahr is specified and identify the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
If no mahr is named and consummation or death occurs, mahr al-mithl is wajib — a shari'ah right.

In a valid marriage, the mahr is a mandatory payment from husband to wife. But what happens if the contract does not specify any mahr amount, or explicitly denies it? The Hanafi school, based on a clear hadith, rules that upon consummation or the husband's death, the wife becomes entitled to mahr al-mithl — the dower of her like. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the conditions, and some practical applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Focus on the core scenario: a marriage without a specified mahr. State the general ruling given in the matn: 'she gets mahr al-mithl if he consummates or dies.'
The ruling is conditional on either consummation (actual or constructive) or death.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq narrated by Ibn Mas'ud. The Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled that a woman whose husband died without fixing a dowry receives full mahr, observes 'iddah, and inherits.
This hadith is classified as hasan sahih by Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof applies)
The ruling from the Prophet covers death without specification. The Hanafi school extends the same ruling to consummation via qiyas (analogy), since both events trigger the full obligation of mahr.
The hadith does not mention consummation; the extension is based on the underlying ratio legis.
4
Note the conditions and examples
Mahr al-mithl applies when no valid mahr is named (or a void condition like 'no mahr' is stipulated). The passage lists several scenarios: marriage on condition of return of the same sum, marriage for a slave, marriage with a vague 'valid mahr', etc.
There are also cases where mahr al-mithl is not due, e.g., pilgrimage (value of middle pilgrimage) or freeing the wife's brother (ownership already established).
5
Distinguish from other schools
Note that the Hanafi position differs from the Shafi'i view that marriage without mahr is invalid (batil). Here, the marriage remains valid but mahr al-mithl is wajib.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences for the validity of the marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن لم يسمه أو نفاه فلها مهر مثلها إن وطئ أو مات عنها) لما روي في السنن والجامع الترمذي عن عبد الله بن مسعود في رجل تزوج امرأة فمات عنها ولم يدخل بها ولم يفرض لها الصداق فقال لها الصداق كاملاً وعليها العدة ولها الميراث فقال معقل بن سنان : سمعت رسول الله الله قضى به في تزويج بنت واشق . قال الترمذي : هو حسن صحيح. ولأنه حق الشرع وجوباً وإنما يصير حقها في حالة البقاء فتملك الإبراء دون النفي ومن صوره ما إذا تزوجها على ألف على أن ترد إليه ألفاً لأن الألف بمقابلة مثلها فبقي النكاح بلا تسمية كما في المحيط ومنها ما إذا تزوجها على عبدها وليس منها ما إذا تزوجها على عبد الغير فإنه إذا لم يجز مالكه وجبت قيمته ومنها ما في القنية قالت زوجت نفسي منك بخمسين ديناراً وأبرأتك من الخمسين فقال قبلت ينعقد بمهر المثل لعدم التسمية. ومنها ما فيها : تزوجتك بمهر جائز في الشرع وجب مهر المثل ولا ينصرف إلى العشرة لأن مهر المثل جائز شرعاً أيضاً، وفي المعراج لها العشرة. ومنها ما إذا تزوجها على حكمها أو حكمه أو في حكم رجل آخر أو على ما في بطن جاريتي أو أغنامي كما في فتح القدير. ومنها ما الظهيرية : لو تزوجها على أن يهب الزوج لأبيها ألف درهم كان لها مهر المثل. وهب لأبيها ألفاً أو لم يهب، فإن وهب كان له أن يرجع في الهبة. ومنها ما فيها أيضاً: لو تزوجها على دراهم كان لها مهر المثل ولا يشبه الخلع ومنها تسمية المحرم ومنها تسمية المجهولة جهالة قوله : (قضى به في تزويج بنت واشق) الذي في الفتح قضى في بروع بنت واشق بمثله وقال : هذا لفظ أبي داود وله روايات أخر بألفاظ وذكر قبله «وبروع» بكسر الباء الموحدة في المشهور ويروى بفتحها قوله : (ومنها ما فيها) أي في القنية . هـ. فاحشة كما سيأتي كما إذا تزوجها على ما يكسبه العام أو يرثه كما في البدائع. ومنها تسمية ما لا يصلح مهراً كتأخير الدين عنها سنة والتأخير باطل كما في الظهيرية، أو أبرئ فلان من الدين فيجب مهر المثل كما في الخانية وليس منها ما إذا تزوجها على حجة فإن لها قيمة حجة وسط لا مهر المثل كما في الظهيرية وفسر في المعراج الوسط بركوب الراحلة . وليس منها ما إذا تزوجها على عتق أخيها عنها فإنه لا شيء لها لثبوت الملك لها اقتضاء في الأخ بخلاف ما إذا تزوجها على عتق أخيها أو طلاق ضرتها فإنه يجب مهر المثل لأنهما ليسا بمال، وتمامه في المحيط.
His statement: (And if he did not name it or denied it, then she has mahr al-mithl if he consummated or died) because it is narrated in al-Sunan and Jami' al-Tirmidhi from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud concerning a man who married a woman, and he died without consummating and without fixing a dowry; he said: 'She has the full dowry, she must observe 'iddah, and she inherits.' Ma'qil ibn Sinan said: 'I heard the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) rule similarly in the marriage of the daughter of Washiq.' Tirmidhi said: 'It is hasan sahih.' And because it is a right of the shari'ah obligatorily, and it only becomes her right in the state of survival, so she owns the right to remission but not denial. Among its forms: if he married her for a thousand on condition that she return a thousand to him, because the thousand is in exchange for its like, so the marriage remains without a specification, as in al-Muhit. And among them: if he married her for her slave, but not if he married her for the slave of another, for if the owner does not permit, its value becomes obligatory. And among them: in al-Qunyah, she said: 'I married myself to you for fifty dinars and I remit you from fifty,' and he said 'I accept,' it is concluded with mahr al-mithl due to lack of specification. And among them: in it: 'I married you with a valid mahr in the shari'ah,' mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory and it does not revert to ten, because mahr al-mithl is also valid in the shari'ah; but in al-Mi'raj, she gets ten. And among them: if he married her on her ruling or his ruling or the ruling of another man, or on what is in the belly of my slave-girl or my sheep, as in Fath al-Qadir. And among them: in al-Zahiriyyah: if he married her on condition that the husband gift her father a thousand dirhams, she has mahr al-mithl, whether he gifted or not; if he gifted, he can revoke the gift. And among them: also in it: if he married her for dirhams, she has mahr al-mithl, and it does not resemble khul'. And among them: specifying the forbidden, and specifying the unknown with gross ignorance. His statement: ('He ruled similarly in the marriage of the daughter of Washiq') — what is in al-Fath is that he ruled in Barwa' bint Washiq similarly, and he said: 'This is the wording of Abu Dawud'; there are other narrations with different wordings. And before it is mentioned 'Barwa'' with kasra of the baa' letter in the well-known version, and it is also narrated with fatha. His statement: ('And among them what is in it') meaning in al-Qunyah. It ends. Gross ignorance as will come, such as when he marries her on what he will earn that year or inherit, as in al-Bada'i'. And among them: specifying what is not suitable as mahr, like deferring a debt for a year — the deferral is void, as in al-Zahiriyyah, or 'I declare so-and-so free of debt' — then mahr al-mithl is obligatory, as in al-Khaniyyah. And it is not among the cases: if he marries her on pilgrimage, then she has the value of a middle pilgrimage, not mahr al-mithl, as in al-Zahiriyyah; and in al-Mi'raj the 'middle' is interpreted as riding a mount. And it is not among the cases: if he marries her on freeing her brother for her, then she gets nothing due to ownership established for her by exigency in the brother, unlike if he marries her on freeing her brother or divorcing her co-wife — then mahr al-mithl is obligatory because they are not wealth. Its completion is in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It explains the consequence when a marriage contract lacks a specified mahr (or the mahr is denied). If the husband consummates or dies, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl (the dower of her like). The proof is the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq, where the Prophet ruled that a woman whose husband died without fixing a dowry gets full mahr, 'iddah, and inheritance. The author notes that this ruling is also based on it being a right established by shari'ah. Several examples follow: marrying with a condition to return the same amount (hidden lack of specification), marrying for the wife's own slave (valid) versus a third party's slave (value due if owner disapproves), mahr al-mithl in cases of remission or unspecified valid mahr, marriage on the ruling of a third party, on unborn property, on a gift to the father, on dirhams without specification, and on forbidden or grossly unknown items. The author also clarifies what is not from this category: pilgrimage (value of a middle pilgrimage), freeing the wife's brother (no mahr al-mithl due to established ownership), and other cases where the subject is wealth or property. The lesson concludes with cross-references.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to what women of similar status (age, beauty, wealth, etc.) receive in her family and locale.
تسمية (tasmiyah): Naming or specifying a particular mahr amount or item in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for mahr al-mithl when no mahr is specified and the husband dies before consummation?
A) A verse from the Quran
B) The hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogy to divorce cases

Key Takeaway
When no mahr is specified and consummation or death occurs, the wife is entitled to mahr al-mithl as a shari'ah right, based on the hadith of Barwa' bint Washiq.

Dividing Mahr al-Mithl When Husband Stipulates Payment from Wife
Ruling with distinction: when husband stipulates wife gives a slave, mahr al-mithl is divided between sale and mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between 'daf'' (pay) and 'i'ta'' (give) to determine whether the mahr al-mithl is divided when the husband stipulates a transfer of property from the wife.

Core Idea
The verb used in the condition determines if the transfer is a sale or a gift, affecting the mahr.

When a marriage contract includes a condition that the wife gives something to the husband, the legal effect depends on the specific Arabic verb used. In Hanafi fiqh, 'pay' (daf') implies a sale, while 'give' (i'ta') implies a gift. This subtle distinction changes the entire ruling on mahr al-mithl, as demonstrated in this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline ruling
State the default rule: when no mahr is specified, the wife is entitled to her mahr al-mithl in full, provided the husband did not stipulate anything from her.
This is the starting point for the distinction.
2
Distinguish the two wordings
The text contrasts two scenarios: husband uses 'pay' (tadfa'a) vs 'give' (tu'teeni). Recognize that the choice of verb changes the legal classification of the transfer (sale vs gift).
Hanafi fiqh gives weight to literal wording.
3
Apply the qiyas on compensation division
When 'pay' is used, the compensation (the slave) is treated as a sale in exchange for part of the mahr. Since the sale is invalid (unknown price), the mahr al-mithl is divided proportionally: the value of the slave is deducted as a defective sale, and the remainder becomes the valid mahr.
The illa is the condition creating a defective sale.
4
Consider the subsidiary sale scenario
If a specific mahr (e.g., 1000) is named along with the condition, both marriage and sale are valid because the sale is subsidiary to the marriage. Note the author's remark that inclusion of death would be more comprehensive.
This case is an exception where the sale is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن وجوب مهر المثل بتمامه عند عدم التسمية مشروط بأن لا يشترط الزوج عليها شيئاً لما في الولوالجية والمحيط : لو تزوجها على أن تدفع إليه هذا العبد يقسم مهرها على قيمة العبد وعلى مهر مثلها لأن المرأة بذلت البضع والعبد بإزاء مهر مثلها ، والبدل ينقسم على قدر قيمة المبدل فما أصاب قيمة العبد فالبيع فيه فاسد لأنها باعته بشيء مجهول والباقي يصير مهراً ) ويخالفه ما نقلاه أيضاً لو قال لامرأة أتزوجك على أن تعطيني عبدك هذا فقبلت جاز النكاح بمهر المثل ولا شيء له من العبد فيحتاج إلى الفرق . وقد يقال : إن في الثانية لم يجعل العبد مبيعاً بل هبة فلا ينقسم مهر المثل على العبد وعلى مهر المثل بدليل أنه ذكر الإعطاء والعطية الهبة، وفي الأولى جعل العبد مبيعاً فانقسم مهر المثل بدليل أنه ذكر الدفع لا الإعطاء. وأما إذا تزوجها على ألف على أن تدفع إليه هذا العبد فقال في المحيط : صح النكاح والبيع لأن البيع مشروط في النكاح ؛ فأما النكاح غير مشروط في البيع فثبت البيع ضمناً للنكاح ولو قال في المختصر أو مات أحدهما» لكان أولى لأن موتها كموته كما في التبيين.
Then know that the obligation of mahr al-mithl in full when there is no specification is conditional on the husband not stipulating anything upon her, as in al-Walwaljiyyah and al-Muhit: If he marries her on condition that she pay this slave to him, her mahr is divided between the value of the slave and her mahr al-mithl, because the woman has offered the vulva (sexual right) and the slave is in exchange for her mahr al-mithl, and the compensation is divided according to the value of what is compensated; so whatever corresponds to the value of the slave, the sale therein is invalid because she sold it for an unknown thing, and the remainder becomes mahr. And it is contradicted by what they also reported: if he said to a woman, 'I marry you on condition that you give me this slave' and she accepted, the marriage is valid with mahr al-mithl and he gets nothing of the slave—so a distinction is needed. It may be said: in the second case, he did not make the slave a sold item but a gift, so mahr al-mithl is not divided onto the slave and onto mahr al-mithl, as evidenced by his using 'give' (i'ta') and gift ('atiyyah), while in the first case he made the slave a sold item, so mahr al-mithl is divided, as evidenced by his using 'pay' (daf') not 'give'. As for if he marries her for a thousand on condition that she pay this slave to him, al-Muhit said: the marriage and sale are valid because the sale is conditioned in the marriage; as for the marriage, it is not conditioned in the sale, so the sale is established as subsidiary to the marriage. And if it was said in al-Mukhtasar 'or one of them dies', it would be more appropriate because her death is like his death, as in al-Tabyin.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents a conditional ruling with a fine legal distinction. The full obligation of mahr al-mithl when no mahr is specified is only applicable if the husband does not stipulate anything from the wife. The text presents a problematic case: if the husband says 'I marry you on condition that you pay (tadfa'a) this slave to me,' then the mahr al-mithl is divided proportionally between the value of the slave (which is a defective sale due to the unknown exchange) and the remainder as mahr. However, if he uses the word 'give' (tu'teeni), the situation differs: the marriage is valid with mahr al-mithl and he gets nothing; the slave is a gift, not a sale, so no division occurs. The key distinction is linguistic: 'daf'' implies sale, 'i'ta' implies gift. A third case is when the husband marries her for a specified mahr of a thousand plus a condition to pay a slave; here both marriage and sale are valid because the sale is subsidiary to the marriage. The author notes that if the text had included death of either spouse, it would be more comprehensive, as death has the same effect as consummation.

Key Terms
دفع (daf'): To pay or hand over, implying a sale or exchange transaction.
إعطاء (i'ta'): To give, implying a gift without exchange.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the husband says, 'I marry you on condition that you pay (tadfa'a) this slave to me,' what is the ruling regarding the mahr?
A) The marriage is batil because of the condition.
B) The mahr is the full value of the slave only.
C) Mahr al-mithl is divided: part for the slave (invalid sale) and remainder as mahr.
D) The wife gets nothing because the condition is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The wording of the husband's condition—'pay' vs 'give'—determines whether the transfer is a sale or a gift, affecting the division of mahr al-mithl.

Cases Not Considered as Absence of Mahr Specification
Clarification of two exceptions to absence of mahr specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify two scenarios that are not considered absence of mahr specification and state the rulings for each, including the husband's khiyar.

Core Idea
Marrying for an unknown reference amount is valid with husband's khiyar; remarrying with owed mahr creates a new mahr, not debt.

This passage clarifies two borderline cases that might be mistaken as absence of mahr specification (tark al-tasmiyah). In both, the mahr is validly specified, and the rules differ from a completely unspecified mahr. Understanding these exceptions prevents incorrect application of mahr al-mithl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first exception: marriage for mother's mahr
When a woman marries for the like of her mother's mahr, and the husband does not know the amount, the mahr is valid and fixed at that amount. Upon pre-consumption divorce, she gets half. The husband has khiyar (option) upon learning the amount; the wife does not.
Analogy: buying something for the weight of a stone without knowing its weight.
2
Identify the second exception: remarriage with owed mahr
After separation, the husband still owes ten dinars of the original mahr. He then marries her for those ten dinars. The new mahr is a separate ten, not the debt. This is not absence of specification.
The mahr is clearly specified as 'ten dinars'.
3
Distinguish from complete absence of specification
In both exceptions, the mahr is specified by reference or by a specific amount. In complete absence, no amount or reference is mentioned, leading to mahr al-mithl.
The passage begins by stating these are NOT from the forms of absence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس من صور عدم التسمية ما لو تزوجت بمثل مهر أمها والزوج لا يعلم مقدار مهر أمها فإنه جائز بمقدار مهر أمها ولو طلقها الزوج قبل الدخول بها فلها نصف ذلك وللزوج الخيار إذا علم مقدار مهر أمها كما لو اشترى بوزن هذا الحجر ذهباً ثم علم بوزنه ولا خيار للمرأة. كذا في الذخيرة وليس منها ما إذا افترقا وبقي عليه عشرة دنانير من المهر ثم تزوجها بتلك العشر فإن المصرح به في القنية أنه تزوج بمثل العشرة فيكون المهر عشرة أخرى غير عشرة الدين :
And it is not among the forms of absence of specification: the case where she marries for the like of her mother's mahr, and the husband does not know the amount of her mother's mahr; then it is valid for the amount of her mother's mahr, and if the husband divorces her before consummation, she gets half of that, and the husband has the option upon learning the amount of her mother's mahr, just as if he bought something for the weight of this gold stone and then learned its weight; and the woman has no option. Thus in al-Dhakhirah. And it is not among them: the case where they separated and ten dinars of the mahr remained owed by him, then he married her for those ten; what is explicitly stated in al-Qunyah is that he married for the like of ten, so the mahr is another ten, not the ten of the debt:
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This short passage lists two exceptions to the category of 'absence of specification.' First, if a woman marries for the like of her mother's mahr, it is a valid specification (though the amount is initially unknown to the husband). The mahr is fixed at the mother's mahr; upon divorce before consummation, she gets half. The husband has an option (khiyar) when he discovers the amount, but the woman does not. This is analogous to buying something by weight of a stone without knowing its precise weight. Second, if a husband divorces her and still owes ten dinars from the original mahr, then later marries her again for those ten, the new mahr is a separate ten dinars, not the debt. This is not a case of unspecified mahr; it is a valid specification of a new amount.

Key Terms
عدم التسمية ('adam al-tasmiyah): Absence of specification, when the mahr is not mentioned or specified at all in the marriage contract.
خيار (khiyar): Option or right to rescind, here given to the husband upon learning the unknown mahr amount.
مهر (mahr): Dower, the obligatory gift from husband to wife in a marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of marrying for the like of the mother's mahr, who has the option (khiyar) upon learning the amount?
A) The wife only
B) The husband only
C) Both parties
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Marrying for a mother's mahr or for a previously owed mahr are both valid specifications, not absence of mahr; the first gives the husband khiyar, the second does not.

Mut'ah is Wajib for the Divorced Woman (Before Consummation, No Mahr)
Ruling with Quran proof on obligation of mut'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that mut'ah is wajib for a woman divorced before consummation without a specified mahr, cite the Quranic proof (2:236), and explain why the imperative indicates obligation despite the phrase 'muhsinin'.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is wajib because the Quranic command (amr) in 2:236 establishes obligation; the word 'muhsinin' does not weaken it to recommendation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position on mut'ah—a consolation gift for a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was fixed. The author cites Quran 2:236 and argues that the imperative form obligates mut'ah, rebutting the view that it is merely recommended. We will examine the dalil and the Hanafi usul principle that commands indicate obligation unless a clear context shifts them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving mut'ah to a woman divorced before consummation without a specified mahr. The ruling is wajib (obligatory).
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 2:236: 'And give them mut'ah, for the affluent according to his means...' The imperative 'matti' is the key.
The full verse context includes the phrase 'upon the doers of good'.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
Per Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a clear contextual indicator (qarina sarifa) shifting it to recommendation.
This is a fundamental rule in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
4
Address the counterargument
The phrase 'upon the doers of good' might suggest recommendation. The author argues that 'muhsin' is a general term that can include obligatory acts, so it is not a sufficient qarina to override the default obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والمتعة إن طلقها الوطء) أي لها المتعة إن لم يسم شيئاً وطلقها قبل الوطء والخلوة لقوله تعالى ومتعوهن على الموسع قدره ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٣٦] الآية . ثم هذه المتعة واجبة رجوعاً إلى الأمر، ولا يكون لفظ المحسنين قرينة صارفة إلى الندب لأن المحسن أعم من قوله : (لأن موتها كموته قال الرملي فلو ماتا ذكر قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير فيما لو مات الزوج أولاً ماتا معاً أو لا يعلم أيهما مات أولاً خلافاً بين الإمام وصاحبيه، فعندهما لورثة المرأة مهر مثلها في تركة الزوج وعنده لا يقضى بمهر المثل بعد موتها ،فراجعه، وكان ينبغي ذكر ذلك البحر الرائق ج٣/ ١٧
His statement: (And mut'ah if he divorces her before intercourse) i.e., she has mut'ah if he did not name anything and divorced her before intercourse and seclusion, due to the saying of the Most High: 'And give them mut'ah, for the affluent according to his means' [Quran 2:236]. Then this mut'ah is wajib, returning to the command, and the word 'muhsinin' (those who do good) is not a context that turns it to recommendation, because 'muhsin' is more general. His statement: (Because her death is like his death). Al-Ramli said: So if both died, Qadikhan mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir regarding if the husband dies first, or both die together, or it is not known who died first, there is a difference between the Imam (Abu Hanifa) and his two companions. According to the two companions, the heirs of the woman have her mahr al-mithl from the husband's estate, but according to the Imam, mahr al-mithl is not decreed after her death. Refer to it. And it would have been fitting to mention that in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, volume 3, page 17.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on mut'ah (consolation gift) for a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified. The Quranic verse 2:236 is cited as proof: '...and give them mut'ah, for the affluent according to his means...' The author argues that mut'ah is wajib (obligatory) because it is a command (amr). The phrase 'those who do good' (muhsinin) does not turn it into recommendation, as 'muhsin' is a general term that can include obligatory acts. The second part discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the case where the wife dies before consummation without a specified mahr. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions), the wife's estate is entitled to mahr al-mithl from the husband's inheritance, but according to Abu Hanifa, mahr al-mithl is not decreed after her death because the right does not survive her. This dispute arises in scenarios of multiple deaths. The author notes that this detail should have been included in the original text.

Key Terms
متعة (mut'ah): A remedial gift given to a woman divorced before consummation without a fixed mahr.
أمر (amr): Command; in usul al-fiqh, the imperative form generally indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a contextual indicator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on mut'ah for a woman divorced before consummation without a specified mahr?
A) It is mustahabb (recommended).
B) It is wajib (obligatory).
C) It is not due at all.
D) It is due only if specified in the contract.

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is wajib for a woman divorced before consummation without a specified mahr, established by the command in Quran 2:236.
