Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Mahr al-Mithl After Wife's Death
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr al-mithl after wife's death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding mahr al-mithl when a wife dies before consummation without a specified mahr, and identify the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds that no mahr is due after the wife's death before consummation; the two companions hold that her estate claims mahr al-mithl.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq also addresses an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: if a woman dies before consummation without a specified mahr, does her estate have right to mahr al-mithl? Abu Hanifa distinguishes the wife's death from the husband's, while the two companions analogize the two cases. We will analyze the reasoning and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Does mahr al-mithl become part of the wife's estate if she dies before consummation without a specified mahr?
2
Identify the positions
Abu Hanifa: No, mahr al-mithl is not decreed after her death. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): Yes, her heirs inherit the right to mahr al-mithl.
3
Analyze each side's proof
Abu Hanifa: The right to mahr is established only upon survival or consummation; it does not survive her death. The companions: Analogy to the case of the husband's death, where mahr is due to the wife.
The companions use qiyas; Abu Hanifa relies on the principle that the right is contingent.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
According to the companions, the wife's heirs claim mahr from the husband's estate; according to Abu Hanifa, they get nothing.
This difference affects inheritance calculations.
5
Note the unresolved tarjih
The text does not specify which position is mufta bihi, leaving it as an open dispute within the school.
Later Hanafi works may offer a preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والمتعة إن طلقها الوطء) أي لها المتعة إن لم يسم شيئاً وطلقها قبل الوطء والخلوة لقوله تعالى ومتعوهن على الموسع قدره ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٣٦] الآية . ثم هذه المتعة واجبة رجوعاً إلى الأمر، ولا يكون لفظ المحسنين قرينة صارفة إلى الندب لأن المحسن أعم من قوله : (لأن موتها كموته قال الرملي فلو ماتا ذكر قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير فيما لو مات الزوج أولاً ماتا معاً أو لا يعلم أيهما مات أولاً خلافاً بين الإمام وصاحبيه، فعندهما لورثة المرأة مهر مثلها في تركة الزوج وعنده لا يقضى بمهر المثل بعد موتها ،فراجعه، وكان ينبغي ذكر ذلك البحر الرائق ج٣/ ١٧
His statement: (And mut'ah if he divorces her before intercourse) i.e., she has mut'ah if he did not name anything and divorced her before intercourse and seclusion, due to the saying of the Most High: 'And give them mut'ah, for the affluent according to his means' [Quran 2:236]. Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on mut'ah (consolation gift) for a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified. Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The customary dowry equivalent to what women of similar status receive in her family.
خلاف (ikhtilaf): Disagreement, especially among mujtahid imams.

Invalid Mahr Specifications and the Obligation of Tamtī
Commentary on mahr and tamtī from Kanz al-Daqā'iq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions triggering mahr al-mithl when mahr specification is invalid, and identify when tamtī is wajib for a divorced wife.

Core Idea
Tamtī is wajib—a substitute for mahr al-mithl when divorce occurs before consummation with no valid mahr.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqā'iq, details the Hanafi rulings on mahr when the specified condition is invalid. It explains when mahr al-mithl replaces the invalid specification and when tamtī (a consolation gift) becomes obligatory. The text also addresses key conditions, definitions, and major intra-Hanafi disagreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify invalid mahr specifications
The passage lists specifications that are invalid (e.g., deferring debt, absolving debt) and those that are valid but not requiring mahr al-mithl (e.g., Hajj, freeing the bride's brother). Determine which lead to mahr al-mithl and which lead to other substitutes.
Note the distinction between invalid specifications and valid but non-monetary conditions.
2
Understand the condition for full mahr al-mithl
When no mahr is specified, full mahr al-mithl is due only if the husband did not impose a condition on the wife. If he did (e.g., she must give a slave), the mahr is split between the condition's value and mahr al-mithl.
The split occurs because the condition is treated as a separate sale.
3
Analyze the obligation of tamtī
Tamtī is due when a wife is divorced before consummation (and without seclusion) and no mahr was specified. The Quranic command (al-Baqarah 2:236) is the proof. Tamtī is not due if the separation originates from the wife's side.
The imperative form indicates wujub in Hanafi usul.
4
Examine intra-Hanafi disputes and mufta bihi
Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn disagree on whether mahr al-mithl is due when a specified amount like 1000 or 2000 dirhams is mentioned. The passage also mentions a dispute on mahr al-mithl after death. For tamtī components, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
The mufta bihi for tamtī definition is dir', khimār, and milhafa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب المهر. ومنها تسمية ما لا يصلح مهراً كتأخير الدين عنها سنة والتأخير باطل كما في الظهيرية، أو أبرئ فلان من الدين فيجب مهر المثل كما في الخانية وليس منها ما إذا تزوجها على حجة فإن لها قيمة حجة وسط لا مهر المثل كما في الظهيرية وفسر في المعراج الوسط بركوب الراحلة . وليس منها ما إذا تزوجها على عتق أخيها عنها فإنه لا شيء لها لثبوت الملك لها اقتضاء في الأخ بخلاف ما إذا تزوجها على عتق أخيها أو طلاق ضرتها فإنه يجب مهر المثل لأنهما ليسا بمال، وتمامه في المحيط. ثم اعلم أن وجوب مهر المثل بتمامه عند عدم التسمية مشروط بأن لا يشترط الزوج عليها شيئاً لما في الولوالجية والمحيط : لو تزوجها على أن تدفع إليه هذا العبد يقسم مهرها على قيمة العبد وعلى مهر مثلها لأن المرأة بذلت البضع والعبد بإزاء مهر . مثلها ، والبدل ينقسم على قدر قيمة المبدل فما أصاب قيمة العبد فالبيع فيه فاسد لأنها باعته بشيء مجهول والباقي يصير مهرا مهراً ) ويخالفه ما نقلاه أيضاً لو قال لامرأة أتزوجك على أن تعطيني عبدك هذا فقبلت جاز النكاح بمهر المثل ولا شيء له من العبد فيحتاج إلى الفرق . وقد يقال : إن في الثانية لم يجعل العبد مبيعاً بل هبة فلا ينقسم مهر المثل على العبد وعلى مهر المثل بدليل أنه ذكر الإعطاء والعطية الهبة، وفي الأولى جعل العبد مبيعاً فانقسم مهر المثل بدليل أنه ذكر الدفع لا الإعطاء. وأما إذا تزوجها على ألف على أن تدفع إليه هذا العبد فقال في المحيط : صح النكاح والبيع لأن البيع مشروط في النكاح ؛ فأما النكاح غير مشروط في البيع فثبت البيع ضمناً للنكاح ولو قال في المختصر أو مات أحدهما» لكان أولى لأن موتها كموته كما في التبيين. وليس من صور عدم التسمية ما لو تزوجت بمثل مهر أمها والزوج لا يعلم مقدار مهر أمها فإنه جائز بمقدار مهر ،أمها ولو طلقها الزوج قبل الدخول بها فلها نصف ذلك وللزوج الخيار إذا علم مقدار مهر أمها كما لو اشترى بوزن هذا الحجر ذهباً ثم علم بوزنه ولا خيار للمرأة. كذا في الذخيرة وليس منها ما إذا افترقا وبقي عليه عشرة دنانير من المهر ثم تزوجها بتلك العشر فإن المصرح به في القنية أنه تزوج بمثل العشرة فيكون المهر عشرة أخرى غير عشرة الدين : . قوله : (والمتعة إن طلقها الوطء) أي لها المتعة إن لم يسم شيئاً وطلقها قبل الوطء والخلوة لقوله تعالى ومتعوهن على الموسع قدره ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٣٦] الآية . ثم هذه المتعة واجبة رجوعاً إلى الأمر، ولا يكون لفظ المحسنين قرينة صارفة إلى الندب لأن المحسن أعم من قوله : (لأن موتها كموته قال الرملي فلو ماتا ذكر قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير فيما لو : مات الزوج أولاً ماتا معاً أو لا يعلم أيهما مات أولاً خلافاً بين الإمام وصاحبيه، فعندهما لورثة المرأة مهر مثلها في تركة الزوج وعنده لا يقضى بمهر المثل بعد موتها ،فراجعه، وكان ينبغي ذكر ذلك البحر الرائق ج٣/ ١٧  أو مات عنها والمتعة إن طلقها قبل الوطء وهي درع وخمار وملحفة وما فرض بعد فيه تجب المتطوع والقائم بالواجب أيضاً فلا ينافي الوجوب مع ما انضم إليه من لفظ «حقاً» و «على» وفي الأسرار للدبوسي قال علماؤنا : والمتعة بعد الطلاق قبل الدخول في نكاح لا تسمية خلفاً عن مهر المثل الذي كان واجباً به قبل الطلاق بدلاً عن الملك الواقع بالعقد للرجل على المرأة في الحالين جميعاً ا.هـ. ثم اعلم أن المتعة إنما تجب في موضع لم تصبح التسمية من كل وجه، أما إذا صحت من وجه دون وجه فإنه لا تجب المتعة وإن وجب مهر المثل بالدخول كما إذا تزوجها على ألف درهم وكرامتها أو على ألف وعلى أن يهدي لها هدية، فإنه إذا طلقها قبل الدخول كان لها نصف الألف لا المتعة . مع أنه لو دخل بها وجب مهر المثل لا ينقص من الألف - كما في غاية البيان - لأن المسمى لم يفسد من كل وجه لأنه على تقدير كرامتها والإهداء يوجب الألف لا مهر المثل قيد بالطلاق والمراد منه فرقة جاءت من قبله ولم يشاركه صاحب المهر في سببها، طلاقاً كانت أو فسخاً كالطلاق والفرقة بالإيلاء واللعان والجب والعنة وردته وإبائه الإسلام وتقبيله ابنتها أو أمها بشهوة للاحتراز عن فرقة جاءت من قبلها قبل الدخول فإنه لا متعة لها، لا وجوباً ولا استحباباً كما في فتح القدير . كما لا يجب نصف المسمى لو كان موجوداً كردتها وإبائها الإسلام وتقبيلها ابنه بشهوة والرضاع وخيار البلوغ والعتق وعدم الكفاءة، وقيدنا بأنه لم يشاركه في سبيها للاحتراز عما إذا اشترى منكوحته من المولى أو اشتراها وكيله منه فإن مالك المهر يشارك الزوج في السبب الملك فلذا لا تجب المتعة ولا نصف المسمى بخلاف ما لو باعها المولى من رجل ثم اشتراها الزوج منه فإنها واجبة كما في التبيين . وهو قوله : (وهي درع وخمار وملحفة) وهو مروي عن عائشة وابن عباس رضي الله عنهما . ودرع المرأة بالدال المهملة ما تلبسه فوق القميص وهو مذكر، والخمار ما تغطي به المرأة رأسها، والملحفة هي الملاءة وهي ما تلتحف به المرأة. كذا في المغرب. ولم يذكر في الذخيرة أيضاً لكن الفتوى في المسألة على قولهما كما ذكره البزازي قوله : (أما إذا صحت من وجه الخ) قال في النهر أقول : قدمنا عن المحيط أنه لو تزوجها على ألف أو ألفين وجب مهر المثل عند الإمام خلافاً لهما . قال : ولو طلقها قبل الدخول كان لها خمسمائة بالإجماع وهي عنده بحكم المتعة لأن الظاهر أن قيمة المتعة عنده لا تزيد على خمسمائة حتى لو زادت كان لها المتعة عنده كما في العشرة والعشرين ا هـ. وهذا يقتضي أن إيجاب الخمسمائة فيما إذا تزوجها على ألف وكرامتها أو على أن ليس لصحة التسمية من وجه لأن قيمة المتعة لا تزيد عليها، وحينئذ فلا حاجة إلى هذا التقييد ا هـ . قلت: وهذا بناء على تسليم فساد التسمية وسيأتي الكلام فيه عند قوله ولو نكحها بألف على أن لا يخرجها الخ» قوله: (وهي ما تلتحف به المرأة زاد في النهر من قرنها إلى قدمها قوله : (ولم يذكر في الذخيرة الدرع) قال في النهر أقول : درع المرأة قميصها والجمع أدرع وعليه جرى العيني، وعزاه في
Book of Marriage, Chapter of Mahr. Among them [is] specifying what is not valid as mahr, like deferring a debt for a year—the deferment is void as in al-Zahiriyyah—or 'I absolve so-and-so from debt'—then mahr al-mithl is obligatory as in al-Khaniyyah. And not among them is if he marries her on [the condition of] Hajj: for her is the value of an average Hajj, not mahr al-mithl as in al-Zahiriyyah; and in al-Mi'raj [the term] 'average' was interpreted as riding a mount. And not among them is if he marries her on [the condition of] freeing her brother: she gets nothing because ownership is established for her by necessary implication in the brother, contrary to if he marries her on [the condition of] freeing her brother or divorcing her co-wife: then mahr al-mithl is obligatory because neither is property. Its completion is in al-Muhit. Then know that the obligation of the full mahr al-mithl when no specification [of mahr] exists is conditional upon the husband not imposing any condition on her. According to al-Walwalijiyyah and al-Muhit: if he marries her on condition that she give him this slave, her mahr is divided between the value of the slave and her mahr al-mithl because the woman offered the private part and the slave in exchange for her mahr al-mithl; the consideration is divided according to the value of the counter-value. Whatever [portion] corresponds to the value of the slave, the sale thereof is invalid because she sold it for something unknown; the remainder becomes mahr. This contradicts what they also narrated: if he said to a woman 'I marry you on condition that you give me this slave of yours' and she accepted, the marriage is valid with mahr al-mithl and he gets nothing from the slave. This requires a distinction. It may be said: in the second [case], the slave was not made a commodity of sale but a gift, so mahr al-mithl is not divided between the slave and mahr al-mithl; the proof is that he used 'giving' (i'ta') which [implies] gift. In the first [case], the slave was made a commodity of sale, so mahr al-mithl was divided; the proof is that he used 'payment' (daf') not 'giving'. As for if he marries her for one thousand [dirhams] on condition that she give him this slave: in al-Muhit it says the marriage and the sale are valid because the sale is conditional on the marriage; however, the marriage is not conditional on the sale, so the sale is established incidentally to the marriage. If [the author] in al-Mukhtasar had said 'or one of them dies' it would have been more appropriate because her death is like his death as in al-Tabyin. Not among the cases of absence of specification is if she marries for the like of her mother's mahr while the husband does not know the amount of her mother's mahr: it is permissible for the amount of her mother's mahr; and if the husband divorces her before consummation, she gets half of that, and the husband has an option when he learns the amount of her mother's mahr, just like if he bought [something] for the weight of this stone in gold and then learned its weight; and the woman has no option. Thus in al-Dhakhirah. And not among them is if they separate and ten dinars of the mahr remain outstanding, then he marries her with those ten: what is explicitly stated in al-Qunyah is that he married for [the like of] the ten, so the mahr is another ten besides the ten of the debt. His statement: (And [there is] tamtī if he divorces before intercourse) means she gets tamtī if he did not specify [mahr] and divorced her before intercourse and seclusion, due to the verse: 'And provide for them—out of the means of the wealthy according to his means' (al-Baqarah 2:236). Then this tamtī is obligatory by returning to the command, and the word 'doers of good' is not a context diverting to recommendation because 'doer of good' is more general than ... His statement: (Because her death is like his death). Al-Ramli said: if they both die, Qadi Khan mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that if the husband dies first, or both die together, or it is unknown which died first, there is a disagreement between Imam [Abu Hanifa] and his two companions: according to the two, the wife's heirs get her mahr al-mithl from the husband's estate; according to him [Abu Hanifa], mahr al-mithl is not adjudged after her death. So refer to it, and it was fitting to mention that. (Page 258) Or [if] he dies and [there is] tamtī if he divorces before intercourse. It is a dir', a khimār, and a milhafa. Whatever is prescribed later, it is obligatory; the volunteer and the one performing the obligatory [are included?] so it does not negate obligation with what is added of the word 'right' and 'upon'. In al-Asrar by al-Dabbusi: our scholars said: tamtī after divorce before consummation in a marriage without specification is a substitute for the mahr al-mithl that was obligatory before divorce, as a replacement for the ownership that the contract established for the husband over the woman in both states. End. Then know that tamtī is only obligatory in a place where the specification [of mahr] is not valid in every respect; as for if it is valid in one respect but not another, then tamtī is not obligatory, though mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory by consummation—as if he marries her for one thousand dirhams and her honour, or for one thousand on condition that he give her a gift: then if he divorces her before consummation, she gets half the thousand, not tamtī. But if he consummates, mahr al-mithl is obligatory, not less than the thousand—as in Ghayat al-Bayan—because the specified [mahr] is not invalid in every respect; for on the interpretation of her honour and the gift, the thousand is obligatory, not mahr al-mithl. He restricted it to divorce, and what is meant is a separation originating from his side, and the owner of the mahr did not participate in its cause—whether divorce or annulment like divorce, separation by ilā', li'ān, impotence, 'unna, his apostasy, his refusal to accept Islam, his kissing her daughter or mother with desire—to exclude a separation originating from her side before consummation, for which she has no tamtī, neither obligatory nor recommended as in Fath al-Qadir. Similarly, half the specified [mahr] does not become obligatory if it existed, like her apostasy, her refusal to accept Islam, her kissing his son with desire, suckling, option of puberty, emancipation, and lack of compatibility (kafā'a). And we qualified that he did not participate in its cause to exclude the case where he buys his married slave woman from her master or his agent buys her from him: for the owner of the mahr participates with the husband in the cause of ownership, so tamtī and half the specified [mahr] are not obligatory. This is contrary to if the master sells her to a man and then the husband buys her from him: then it is obligatory as in al-Tabyin. And it is his statement: (It is a dir', khimār, and milhafa). This is narrated from Aisha and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them). Dir' of a woman—with the important letter dāl—is what she wears over the qamis; it is masculine. Khimār is what the woman covers her head with. Milhafa is the mulā'a, which is what the woman wraps herself in. Thus in al-Maghrib. It is not mentioned in al-Dhakhirah either, but the fatwa on the matter is according to the two of them as al-Bazzazi mentioned. His statement: (As for if it is valid from one perspective...) He said in al-Nahr: I say: we have mentioned before from al-Muhit that if he marries her for one thousand or two thousand, mahr al-mithl is obligatory according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] contrary to the two. He said: and if he divorces her before consummation, she gets five hundred by consensus, and according to him it is by way of tamtī because the apparent [value] of tamtī according to him does not exceed five hundred—so if it were more, she would have tamtī according to him as in the ten and twenty. End. This implies that the obligation of the five hundred in the case of marrying for one thousand and her honour or for [something else] is because the specification is not valid in one respect, because the value of tamtī does not exceed it; then there is no need for this restriction. End. I say: this is built on accepting the invalidity of the specification, and discussion will come on it at his statement 'and if he marries her for one thousand on condition that he does not take her out...' His statement: (It is what the woman wraps herself in). In al-Nahr he added: from her crown to her foot. His statement: (And he did not mention in al-Dhakhirah the dir'). He said in al-Nahr: I say: dir' of a woman is her qamis, plural adra'; al-Ayni followed this and attributed it to...
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqā'iq, specifically the chapter on mahr in the book of marriage. The author, Imam al-Marghinani, explains rulings related to invalid mahr specifications and the obligation of mahr al-mithl (dower of the like). The commentary also covers the ruling of tamtī (consolation gift) due to a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified. The author begins by listing cases where mahr specification is invalid: deferring a debt for a year, or saying 'I absolve so-and-so from debt'—these are not valid mahr, and mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory. However, marriage on condition of Hajj or freeing the bride's brother does not invalidate the mahr; for Hajj, she gets the value of an average Hajj; for freeing her brother, she gets nothing because it is implied that she owns her brother. But if the condition is freeing her brother (i.e., her own brother) or divorcing her co-wife, these are not property, so mahr al-mithl is due. The author then discusses a key condition: for mahr al-mithl to be fully obligatory when no mahr is specified, the husband must not have imposed any condition on the wife. If he imposed a condition (e.g., she must give him a slave), then her dower is split between the value of the condition and her mahr al-mithl. The sale of the slave is invalid because the consideration is unknown, but the remainder becomes valid mahr. This is contrasted with a case where the husband says 'give me your slave' and she accepts: the slave is a gift, not a sale, so mahr al-mithl is not split. The commentary also addresses marriage with a mahr and a simultaneous sale of a slave: the sale is valid if it is conditional on the marriage, not vice versa. The author then discusses cases that are not considered 'absence of specification' (i.e., where mahr al-mithl is not applicable): marriage for the like of her mother's mahr without knowing the amount—the mahr is valid at that amount, and in case of divorce before consummation, she gets half; the husband has an option upon learning the amount. Another case: if a man owes his wife ten dinars from a previous mahr, then marries her again with those ten dinars, the second mahr is another ten, not the same debt. The second part of the passage deals with tamtī. The matn states: 'And tamtī if he divorces before intercourse and she has no specified mahr.' The author explains that tamtī is obligatory, based on the Quranic command (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:236). The phrase 'doers of good' in the verse does not make it merely recommended because 'doer of good' includes the obligatory performer. Tamtī is a substitute for mahr al-mithl that was obligatory at the time of contract but is replaced by tamtī upon divorce before consummation. Tamtī consists of a dir' (shift), a khimār (head covering), and a milhafa (wrap). These are defined according to Hanafi sources. Tamtī is only due when the mahr specification is completely invalid; if the specification is valid in some respects (e.g., mahr plus a condition like a gift), then tamtī is not due, and the woman gets half the mahr if divorced before consummation. The passage also notes exceptions: if the separation originates from the wife's side (e.g., her apostasy, her refusal of Islam, etc.), no tamtī is due. Additionally, if the husband buys his wife (a slave woman) from her owner, the owner participates in the cause of marriage, so neither tamtī nor half the mahr is due. The commentary includes an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) held that if both spouses die before consummation and no mahr was specified, the wife's heirs do not get mahr al-mithl, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held that they do. There is also a dispute regarding marriage for a specified amount like one or two thousand: Abu Hanifa said mahr al-mithl is obligatory, contrary to the Sahibayn. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is mentioned for the definition of tamtī: it is according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), i.e., dir', khimār, and milhafa, as stated by al-Bazzazi.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower equivalent to what is given to women of similar status to the bride, used when no mahr is specified or the specification is invalid.
المتعة (al-mut'a (tamtī)): A consolation gift given to a wife divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified. It consists of a dir', khimār, and milhafa according to the relied-upon view.
الدرع (al-dir'): A garment worn over the qamis (shift); it is the upper garment of a woman.
الخمار (al-khimār): A head covering worn by women, covering the head and neck.
الملحفة (al-milhafa): A wrap or cloak that a woman wraps herself in, covering from head to foot (as added in al-Nahr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on tamtī (consolation gift) for a wife divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified?
A) It is recommended (mandub)
B) It is obligatory (wajib)
C) It is not required at all
D) It depends on the economic status of the husband

Key Takeaway
Tamtī is wajib for a wife divorced before consummation without a valid mahr, and it consists of a dir', khimār, and milhafa.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Ruling and Content of Mut'ah (Consolatory Gift) in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling with proof on wajib mut'ah garments and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which mut'ah is wajib and identify the three specific garments that constitute it, citing the companion narration.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is a wajib gift of three specific garments for a woman divorced before consummation when no valid mahr was specified.

When a marriage ends by divorce before consummation and no valid mahr amount was fixed, the husband must give a consolatory gift called mut'ah. The Hanafi school specifies this gift as three distinct garments, based on the practice of the Companions. This lesson establishes the core ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering event
Determine the situation that makes mut'ah obligatory: divorce by the husband before consummation, where the mahr specification was invalid or absent.
If the mahr specification is valid from any aspect, half the specified mahr is due, not mut'ah.
2
List the three garments
Memorize the three items: dir' (shift), khimar (head-cover), milhafah (wrap). These are the minimum wajib components.
In some regions, additional items like izār may be added due to custom.
3
Recall the dalil
The source is a mawquf narration from Aisha and Ibn Abbas (radiya Allahu anhuma) defining the mut'ah as these three garments.
This is not a prophetic hadith but a companion practice, yet it is considered authoritative in the school.
4
Apply the bounds
The mut'ah cannot be less than 5 dirhams and cannot exceed half of the wife's mahr al-mithl (equivalent mahr).
These limits apply regardless of which status (husband's or wife's) is considered in valuation.

المتعة وإن وجب مهر المثل بالدخول كما إذا تزوجها على ألف درهم وكرامتها أو على ألف وعلى أن يهدي لها هدية، فإنه إذا طلقها قبل الدخول كان لها نصف الألف لا المتعة . مع أنه لو دخل بها وجب مهر المثل لا ينقص كانت أو فسخاً كالطلاق والفرقة بالإيلاء واللعان والجب والعنة وردته وإبائه الإسلام وتقبيله ابنتها أو أمها بشهوة للاحتراز عن فرقة جاءت من قبلها قبل الدخول فإنه لا متعة لها، لا وجوباً ولا استحباباً كما في فتح القدير . كما لا يجب نصف المسمى لو كان موجوداً كردتها وإبائها الإسلام وتقبيلها ابنه بشهوة والرضاع وخيار البلوغ والعتق وعدم الكفاءة، وقيدنا بأنه لم يشاركه في سبيها للاحتراز عما إذا اشترى منكوحته من المولى أو اشتراها وكيله منه فإن مالك المهر يشارك الزوج في السبب الملك فلذا لا تجب المتعة ولا نصف المسمى بخلاف ما لو باعها المولى من رجل ثم اشتراها الزوج منه فإنها واجبة كما في التبيين . قوله : (وهي درع وخمار وملحفة) وهو مروي عن عائشة وابن عباس رضي الله عنهما . ودرع المرأة بالدال المهملة ما تلبسه فوق القميص وهو مذكر، والخمار ما تغطي به المرأة رأسها، والملحفة هي الملاءة وهي ما تلتحف به المرأة. كذا في المغرب. ولم يذكر في الذخيرة الدرع وإنما ذكر القيمص وهو الظاهر وفي المعراج قال فخر الإسلام: هذا في ديارهم أما في ديارنا تلبس أكثر من ذلك فيزاد على هذا إزار ومكعب ا هـ. . وفي البدائع : ولو أعطاها قيمة الأثواب دراهم أو دنانير تجبر على القبول لأن الأثواب ما وجبت لعينها بل من حيث إنها مال كالشاة في خمس من الأبل في باب الزكاة ا هـ. ولم يذكر المصنف اعتبارها بحاله أو بحالها للاختلاف فالكرخي اعتبر حالها واختاره القدوري فإن كانت سفلة فمن الكرباس، وإن كانت وسطة فمن القز، وإن كانت مرتفعة الحال فمن الإبريسم فإنها بدل بضعها فتعتبر بحالها، والإمام السرخسي اعتبار حاله وصححه في الهداية عملاً بقوله تعالى على الموسع قدره وعلى المقتر قدره [البقرة : ٢٣٦] لكن ليس على إطلاقه قالوا فلا تزاد على نصف مهر مثلها لأن الحق عند التسمية أكد وأثبت منه عند عدم التسمية. ثم عندها لا يزاد على نصف المسمى فلأن لا يزاد عند عدمها على نصف مهر المثل أولى. ولا تنقص المتعة عن خمسة دراهم لأنها تجب على طريق العوض وأقل عوض ثبت في النكاح نصف عشرة فلا بد في المتعة ملاحظة هذين الأمرين فليس ملاحظة الأمرين مناقضاً للقول باعتبار حاله كما في فتح القدير، ودعواه بأن الملاحظة المذكورة صريحة في اعتبار حالها ممنوعة لأنها لو كانت غنية قيمة متعتها مائة درهم والزوج فقير يناسبه أن تكون المتعة في حقه عشرين درهماً فعلى من اعتبر حاله الواجب عشرون، وعلى من اعتبر حالها الواجب المائة. نعم لو كان غنياً وحاله يقتضي وهي فقيرة متعتها عشرون فحينئذ لا يزاد على العشرين لا باعتبار حالها بل لما ذكرناه الخصاف اعتبر حالهما قالوا وهو أشبه بالفقه وصححه الولوالجي لأن في اعتبار حالة تسوية بين الشريفة والخسيسة وهو منكر بين الناس فقد اختلف الترجيح، والأرجح قول الخصاف لأن الولوالجي في فتاواه صححه وقال : وعليه الفتوى. كما أفتوا به في النفقة، وظاهر كلامهم أن ملاحظة الأمرين على جميع الأقوال معتبرة فلا يزاد على نصف مهر المثل ولا ينقص عن خمسة دراهم كما هو صريح الأصل والمبسوط وفي فتح القدير وإطلاق الذخيرة : كونها وسطاً لا بغاية الجودة ولا بغاية الرداءة لا يوافق رأياً . من الثلاثة الاعتبار بحاله أو حالها أو حالهما ا هـ . ولعله سهو لأن اعتبار الوسط موافق للأقوال كلما لأنه على قول من اعتبر حالها وكانت فقيرة مثلاً فإنه يجب لها الكرباس الوسط لا الجيد ولا الرديء، وفي مائة والإمام هي البناية لابن الأثير، فعلى هذا فكونه في الذخيرة لم يذكره مبني على تفسير المطرزي قوله: (فيزاد على هذا إزار ومكعب) قال في النهر : ولا يخفى إغناء الملحفة عن الإزار إذ بهذا التفسير إزار إلا أن يتعارف تغاير هما كما في مكة المشرفة قوله : (كما في فتح القدير) أي كما ظنه في فتح القدير فهو قيد للمنفي وهو كون الملاحظة المذكورة مناقضة قوله : (بل لما ذكرناه) أي من أنها لا تزاد على نصف مهر المثل فليتأمل في ذلك فإنه لم يذكر كم مقدار مهر المثل فإطلاق عدم الزيادة على العشرين غير ظاهر ولعل قول النهر بعد نقله كلام المؤلف وفيه نظر إشارة إلى هذا
Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr: or she dies and the mut'ah if he divorces her before intercourse, and it is a dir', khimar, and milhafah, and what is specified afterwards in it is obligatory. And the mut'ah is only obligatory when the specification is not valid from every aspect. As for if it is valid from one aspect but not another, then mut'ah is not obligatory, although mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory with consummation, such as if he married her for one thousand dirhams and her dignity, or for one thousand and on condition that he give her a gift. Then if he divorces her before intercourse, she gets half of the thousand, not mut'ah. Yet if he consummated, mahr al-mithl would be obligatory, not reduced from the thousand - as in Ghayat al-Bayan - because the specified mahr is not invalid from every aspect, since on the assumption of her dignity and the gift, it obligates the thousand, not mahr al-mithl. Restriction to divorce: what is meant is a separation coming from him, and the owner of the mahr (the one who pays it) does not share in its cause, whether divorce or annulment like divorce, separation through ila', li'an, jabb, 'unnah, his apostasy, his refusal of Islam, his kissing her daughter or mother with desire, to exclude separation coming from her before intercourse, for then she has no mut'ah, not obligatory nor recommended, as in Fath al-Qadir. Just as half of the specified mahr is not obligatory if it existed, such as her apostasy, her refusal of Islam, her kissing his son with desire, rada', option of puberty, emancipation, and lack of kafa'ah. We restricted with 'he does not share in its cause' to exclude the case where he buys his married slave woman from the master or his agent buys her from him, for the owner of the mahr shares with the husband in the cause of ownership, so neither mut'ah nor half of the specified mahr is obligatory. Unlike if the master sold her to a man and then the husband bought her from him, for it is obligatory, as in al-Tabyin. His saying: (And it is a dir', khimar, and milhafah) - reported from Aisha and Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them. Dir' of a woman: what she wears over the chemise, it is masculine. Khimar: what the woman covers her head with. Milhafah: it is the mila' - what the woman wraps herself with. Thus in al-Mughrib. But al-Dhakhira did not mention the dir'; it only mentioned the chemise, and that is apparent. In al-Mi'raj, Fakhr al-Islam said: This is in their lands; as for our lands, they wear more than that, so an izār and a muk'[؟] are added to this. In al-Bada'i: If he gives her the value of the garments in dirhams or dinars, she is compelled to accept, because the garments are not obligatory for their specific identity but because they are wealth, like the sheep in the five camels in the chapter of zakat. The author did not mention whether it is considered according to his status or her status due to the ikhtilaf. So al-Karkhi considered her status, and al-Quduri chose it. If she is lowly, then from coarse cloth; if middle, from silk; if high status, from brocade, because it is compensation for her private part, so it is considered according to her status. Imam al-Sarakhsi considered his status and deemed it correct in al-Hidayah, acting on His statement: 'Upon the wealthy according to his capacity, and upon the poor according to his capacity' [2:236], but not absolutely. They said: It should not exceed half of her mahr al-mithl, because the right upon specification is more confirmed and established than upon non-specification. Then upon specification it does not exceed half of the specified mahr, so it is more fitting that upon non-specification it should not exceed half of mahr al-mithl. The mut'ah should not be less than five dirhams, because it is obligatory as compensation, and the least compensation established in marriage is half of ten, so these two matters must be observed in mut'ah. Observing these two matters does not contradict the view of considering his status, as in Fath al-Qadir, and his claim that the mentioned observation is clear in considering her status is disputed, because if she is wealthy, her mut'ah value is one hundred dirhams, and the husband is poor, it is suitable that the mut'ah for him be twenty dirhams. According to the one who considers his status, the obligatory is twenty; according to the one who considers her status, the obligatory is one hundred. Yes, if he is wealthy and his status requires, and she is poor, her mut'ah is twenty, then it does not exceed twenty, not by considering her status but due to what we mentioned. al-Khassaf considered both their statuses; they said it is more akin to fiqh, and al-Walwaji deemed it correct, because considering only one status creates equality between the noble and the base, which is objectionable among people. So tarjih differed, and the most preponderant is the view of al-Khassaf, because al-Walwaji in his fatawa deemed it correct and said: And upon it is the fatwa, just as they gave fatwa in maintenance. Their apparent speech indicates that observing both matters is considered in all views, so it should not exceed half of mahr al-mithl and not be less than five dirhams, as is clear in al-Asl and al-Mabsut. In Fath al-Qadir and the absolute statement of al-Dhakhira: It being middle, not of the best quality nor the worst, does not agree with any view of the three: considering his status, her status, or both. Probably it is an oversight, because considering the middle agrees with all views, since according to the one who considers her status and she is poor, for example, the coarse cloth is obligatory, not the good nor the bad. In the hundred and the Imam, it is al-Binaya by Ibn al-Athir. Upon this, that it was not mentioned in al-Dhakhira is based on the interpretation of al-Mutarrizi. His saying: (Then an izār and a muk'[؟] are added to this) - al-Nahr said: It is not hidden that the milhafah suffices for the izār because by this interpretation it is an izār, unless they are customarily different, as in honored Mecca. His saying: (As in Fath al-Qadir) - i.e., as he thought in Fath al-Qadir, so it is a restriction of the negated, which is that the mentioned observation contradicts his saying: (But due to what we mentioned) i.e., that it does not exceed half of mahr al-mithl. So one should ponder that, because he did not mention how much the amount of mahr al-mithl is, so the absolute negation of increase over twenty is not apparent. Perhaps the statement of al-Nahr after quoting the author's words 'and there is consideration' alludes to this.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the obligatory mut'ah (consolatory gift) given to a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified or the specification was invalid. The commentary opens by stating that mut'ah consists of three specific garments: a dir' (shift), a khimar (head-cover), and a milhafah (wrap). This definition is traced back to Aisha and Ibn Abbas, radiya Allahu anhuma, strengthening its authority. The text then clarifies that mut'ah is only wajib when the specification (tashmiyah) of mahr is invalid from every aspect. If the specification is valid from one aspect (e.g., mahr specified but with a condition that does not totally invalidate it), then mut'ah is not wajib; instead, half of the specified mahr is due upon divorce before consummation, or the full mahr al-mithl upon consummation. The commentary also discusses the cause of separation: mut'ah is only wajib when the separation originates from the husband (e.g., divorce, ila', li'an) and not from the wife (e.g., her apostasy). The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about how to evaluate the garments for mut'ah. Three views are presented: (1) based on the wife's status (Karkhi, Quduri), (2) based on the husband's status (Sarakhsi), and (3) based on both (Khassaf). The commentary notes that Khassaf's view is the most preponderant (arajah) and that the fatwa is upon it, as also applied in maintenance (nafaqah). Additionally, the mut'ah is bounded by a minimum of five dirhams and a maximum of half the wife's mahr al-mithl. The passage concludes with a discussion about the specific garments in different lands, noting that in some regions an izār (lower wrap) is added.

Key Terms
متعة (mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a woman divorced before consummation when no valid mahr was specified.
درع (dir'): A shift or garment worn over the chemise, specific to describing the mut'ah gift.
خمار (khimar): A head-cover worn by women, part of the mut'ah.
ملحفة (milhafah): A wrap or cloak that covers the body, part of the mut'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the three specific garments that constitute the wajib mut'ah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Dir', khimar, and milhafah
B) Dir', qamis, and izar
C) Khimar, milhafah, and qamis
D) Dir', khimar, and izar

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is a wajib gift of three specific garments for a woman divorced before consummation without valid mahr, based on companion practice.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Evaluating Mut'ah Garments (Husband's or Wife's Status?)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on valuation of mut'ah garments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on evaluating mut'ah garments (by husband's status, wife's status, or both) and identify the mufta bihi view with its rationale.

Core Idea
The value of mut'ah garments is evaluated by considering both spouses' statuses, per the preponderant view, to avoid discrimination.

Once the obligation of mut'ah and its specific garments is established, the next question is how to determine the quality and value of those garments. The Hanafi school has a well-known internal dispute based on the Quranic verse and principles of compensation. This lesson unpacks the three views, their proofs, and the final relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the ikhtilaf
There are three views: (1) consider only the wife's status (Karkhi, Quduri), (2) consider only the husband's status (Sarakhsi), (3) consider both (Khassaf).
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute, not inter-madhhab.
2
Examine the dalil for each view
Karkhi: mut'ah is compensation for her private part, so her status matters. Sarakhsi: Quran 2:236 says 'upon the wealthy...' so the husband's capacity governs. Khassaf: equity and the rule in maintenance (nafaqah) require considering both.
The text also mentions bounds that apply to all views.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider a wealthy wife and poor husband: by wife's status, mut'ah might be 100 dirhams; by husband's, 20; by both, the lower bound (20) applies because of the max limit (half mahr al-mithl).
The practical difference is the amount actually due.
4
Identify the tarjih
The author states that Khassaf's view is 'ashbah bil-fiqh' (more akin to fiqh) and that al-Walwaji declared the fatwa upon it.
Tarjih is based on equity and consistency with maintenance rulings.

كتاب النكاح باب المهر أو مات عنها والمتعة إن طلقها قبل الوطء وهي درع وخمار وملحفة وما فرض بعد فيه تجب . والمتعة إنما تجب في موضع لم تصبح التسمية من كل وجه، أما إذا صحت من وجه دون وجه فإنه لا تجب المتعة وإن وجب مهر المثل بالدخول كما إذا تزوجها على ألف درهم وكرامتها أو على ألف وعلى أن يهدي لها هدية، فإنه إذا طلقها قبل الدخول كان لها نصف الألف لا المتعة . مع أنه لو دخل بها وجب مهر المثل لا ينقص من الألف - كما في غاية البيان - لأن المسمى لم يفسد من كل وجه لأنه على تقدير كرامتها والإهداء يوجب الألف لا مهر المثل قيد بالطلاق والمراد منه فرقة جاءت من قبله ولم يشاركه صاحب المهر في سببها، طلاقاً الوسط لا الجيد ولا الرديء، وفي مائة والإمام هي البناية لابن الأثير، فعلى هذا فكونه في الذخيرة لم يذكره مبني على تفسير المطرزي قوله: (فيزاد على هذا إزار ومكعب) قال في النهر : ولا يخفى إغناء الملحفة عن الإزار إذ بهذا التفسير إزار إلا أن يتعارف تغاير هما كما في مكة المشرفة قوله : (كما في فتح القدير) أي كما ظنه في فتح القدير فهو قيد للمنفي وهو كون الملاحظة المذكورة مناقضة قوله : (بل لما ذكرناه) أي من أنها لا تزاد على نصف مهر المثل فليتأمل في ذلك فإنه لم يذكر كم مقدار مهر المثل فإطلاق عدم الزيادة على العشرين غير ظاهر ولعل قول النهر بعد نقله كلام المؤلف وفيه نظر إشارة إلى هذا
Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr: or she dies and the mut'ah if he divorces her before intercourse, and it is a dir', khimar, and milhafah, and what is specified afterwards in it is obligatory. And the mut'ah is only obligatory when the specification is not valid from every aspect. As for if it is valid from one aspect but not another, then mut'ah is not obligatory, although mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory with consummation, such as if he married her for one thousand dirhams and her dignity, or for one thousand and on condition that he give her a gift. Then if he divorces her before intercourse, she gets half of the thousand, not mut'ah. Yet if he consummated, mahr al-mithl would be obligatory, not reduced from the thousand - as in Ghayat al-Bayan - because the specified mahr is not invalid from every aspect, since on the assumption of her dignity and the gift, it obligates the thousand, not mahr al-mithl. Restriction to divorce: what is meant is a separation coming from him, and the owner of the mahr (the one who pays it) does not share in its cause, whether divorce or annulment like divorce, separation through ila', li'an, jabb, 'unnah, his apostasy, his refusal of Islam, his kissing her daughter or mother with desire, to exclude separation coming from her before intercourse, for then she has no mut'ah, not obligatory nor recommended, as in Fath al-Qadir. Just as half of the specified mahr is not obligatory if it existed, such as her apostasy, her refusal of Islam, her kissing his son with desire, rada', option of puberty, emancipation, and lack of kafa'ah. We restricted with 'he does not share in its cause' to exclude the case where he buys his married slave woman from the master or his agent buys her from him, for the owner of the mahr shares with the husband in the cause of ownership, so neither mut'ah nor half of the specified mahr is obligatory. Unlike if the master sold her to a man and then the husband bought her from him, for it is obligatory, as in al-Tabyin. His saying: (And it is a dir', khimar, and milhafah) - reported from Aisha and Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them. Dir' of a woman: what she wears over the chemise, it is masculine. Khimar: what the woman covers her head with. Milhafah: it is the mila' - what the woman wraps herself with. Thus in al-Mughrib. But al-Dhakhira did not mention the dir'; it only mentioned the chemise, and that is apparent. In al-Mi'raj, Fakhr al-Islam said: This is in their lands; as for our lands, they wear more than that, so an izār and a muk'[؟] are added to this. In al-Bada'i: If he gives her the value of the garments in dirhams or dinars, she is compelled to accept, because the garments are not obligatory for their specific identity but because they are wealth, like the sheep in the five camels in the chapter of zakat. The author did not mention whether it is considered according to his status or her status due to the ikhtilaf. So al-Karkhi considered her status, and al-Quduri chose it. If she is lowly, then from coarse cloth; if middle, from silk; if high status, from brocade, because it is compensation for her private part, so it is considered according to her status. Imam al-Sarakhsi considered his status and deemed it correct in al-Hidayah, acting on His statement: 'Upon the wealthy according to his capacity, and upon the poor according to his capacity' [2:236], but not absolutely. They said: It should not exceed half of her mahr al-mithl, because the right upon specification is more confirmed and established than upon non-specification. Then upon specification it does not exceed half of the specified mahr, so it is more fitting that upon non-specification it should not exceed half of mahr al-mithl. The mut'ah should not be less than five dirhams, because it is obligatory as compensation, and the least compensation established in marriage is half of ten, so these two matters must be observed in mut'ah. Observing these two matters does not contradict the view of considering his status, as in Fath al-Qadir, and his claim that the mentioned observation is clear in considering her status is disputed, because if she is wealthy, her mut'ah value is one hundred dirhams, and the husband is poor, it is suitable that the mut'ah for him be twenty dirhams. According to the one who considers his status, the obligatory is twenty; according to the one who considers her status, the obligatory is one hundred. Yes, if he is wealthy and his status requires, and she is poor, her mut'ah is twenty, then it does not exceed twenty, not by considering her status but due to what we mentioned. al-Khassaf considered both their statuses; they said it is more akin to fiqh, and al-Walwaji deemed it correct, because considering only one status creates equality between the noble and the base, which is objectionable among people. So tarjih differed, and the most preponderant is the view of al-Khassaf, because al-Walwaji in his fatawa deemed it correct and said: And upon it is the fatwa, just as they gave fatwa in maintenance. Their apparent speech indicates that observing both matters is considered in all views, so it should not exceed half of mahr al-mithl and not be less than five dirhams, as is clear in al-Asl and al-Mabsut. In Fath al-Qadir and the absolute statement of al-Dhakhira: It being middle, not of the best quality nor the worst, does not agree with any view of the three: considering his status, her status, or both. Probably it is an oversight, because considering the middle agrees with all views, since according to the one who considers her status and she is poor, for example, the coarse cloth is obligatory, not the good nor the bad. In the hundred and the Imam, it is al-Binaya by Ibn al-Athir. Upon this, that it was not mentioned in al-Dhakhira is based on the interpretation of al-Mutarrizi. His saying: (Then an izār and a muk'[؟] are added to this) - al-Nahr said: It is not hidden that the milhafah suffices for the izār because by this interpretation it is an izār, unless they are customarily different, as in honored Mecca. His saying: (As in Fath al-Qadir) - i.e., as he thought in Fath al-Qadir, so it is a restriction of the negated, which is that the mentioned observation contradicts his saying: (But due to what we mentioned) i.e., that it does not exceed half of mahr al-mithl. So one should ponder that, because he did not mention how much the amount of mahr al-mithl is, so the absolute negation of increase over twenty is not apparent. Perhaps the statement of al-Nahr after quoting the author's words 'and there is consideration' alludes to this.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the obligatory mut'ah (consolatory gift) given to a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified or the specification was invalid. The commentary opens by stating that mut'ah consists of three specific garments: a dir' (shift), a khimar (head-cover), and a milhafah (wrap). This definition is traced back to Aisha and Ibn Abbas, radiya Allahu anhuma, strengthening its authority. The text then clarifies that mut'ah is only wajib when the specification (tashmiyah) of mahr is invalid from every aspect. If the specification is valid from one aspect (e.g., mahr specified but with a condition that does not totally invalidate it), then mut'ah is not wajib; instead, half of the specified mahr is due upon divorce before consummation, or the full mahr al-mithl upon consummation. The commentary also discusses the cause of separation: mut'ah is only wajib when the separation originates from the husband (e.g., divorce, ila', li'an) and not from the wife (e.g., her apostasy). The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about how to evaluate the garments for mut'ah. Three views are presented: (1) based on the wife's status (Karkhi, Quduri), (2) based on the husband's status (Sarakhsi), and (3) based on both (Khassaf). The commentary notes that Khassaf's view is the most preponderant (arajah) and that the fatwa is upon it, as also applied in maintenance (nafaqah). Additionally, the mut'ah is bounded by a minimum of five dirhams and a maximum of half the wife's mahr al-mithl. The passage concludes with a discussion about the specific garments in different lands, noting that in some regions an izār (lower wrap) is added.

Key Terms
حال الزوج (hal al-zawj): The economic status of the husband, used as a measure for mut'ah valuation by Sarakhsi.
حال الزوجة (hal al-zawjah): The economic status of the wife, used as a measure by Karkhi and Quduri.
التحسين (al-tahsin): The process of tarjih (weighing evidences) to determine the preponderant view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Hanafi scholar's view on mut'ah valuation is considered the mufta bihi (operative for fatwa)?
A) Al-Karkhi
B) Al-Sarakhsi
C) Al-Quduri
D) Al-Khassaf

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position for valuing mut'ah garments is to consider both the husband's and wife's economic status, ensuring equity and avoiding discrimination.

Nikah — Marriage

Determining the Value of Mut'ah: Three Hanafi Views
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mut'ah value with tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on determining the value of mut'ah and apply the mufta bihi (Khassaf's view) with the fixed limits of 5 dirhams minimum and half mahr al-mithl maximum.

Core Idea
Mut'ah value depends on both parties' status, with a minimum of 5 dirhams and a maximum of half her mahr al-mithl.

Mut'ah is an obligatory consolatory gift for a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified. But how much should be given? The Hanafi school has three opinions: some scholars consider only the wife's status, others only the husband's, and the relied-upon view considers both. Additionally, there are two fixed limits: a minimum of 5 dirhams and a maximum of half the woman's mahr al-mithl. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Mut'ah is wajib for a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified in the marriage contract (Quran 2:236). The problem is determining its value.
This is distinct from mahr; mut'ah is a gift, not a dower.
2
State the three Hanafi views
Al-Karkhi and al-Quduri consider the wife's status (low/middle/high quality fabric). Al-Sarakhsi considers the husband's status, following the verse's phrase 'according to his capacity'. Al-Khassaf considers both parties' status, which is the mufta bihi.
The difference stems from whether mut'ah is seen as compensation for the wife (substitute for part of mahr) or as a gift based on the husband's means.
3
Apply the fixed limits
Regardless of which view, mut'ah cannot be less than 5 dirhams (the minimum compensation in marriage) and cannot exceed half of the woman's mahr al-mithl (standard dower). These limits are based on qiyas on mahr.
The half mahr al-mithl limit is because at the time of naming mahr, the maximum is half; so without naming, it should not exceed that.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Al-Walwalji in his Fatawa preferred al-Khassaf's view and stated 'upon it is the fatwa'. This is the operative position in the Hanafi school.
Tarjih is based on avoiding inequality and being more in line with fiqh (asbah bil fiqh).
5
Consider quality of garment
Even within each view, the garment should be of middle quality (not the best nor the worst). For example, if husband is poor, give middle cotton; if middle class, middle silk blend; etc. This reconciles all views.
The passage notes that the 'middle' is actually consistent with all opinions when applied to the specific circumstances.

According to the view considering both conditions: if both are poor, the obligatory is middle cotton; if both rich, middle silk; if one rich and one poor, the obligatory is middle silk blend. Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on mut'ah, the consolatory gift given to a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified in the contract. The discussion centers on the value and type of garment to be given. The author presents multiple Hanafi views: Al-Karkhi and Al-Quduri consider only the wife's status; Al-Sarakhsi considers only the husband's status based on Quran 2:236; Al-Khassaf considers both parties' status, which is preferred by Al-Walwalji and is the mufta bihi. The text also establishes two fixed limits: mut'ah cannot be less than five dirhams (the least compensation in marriage) and cannot exceed half of the woman's mahr al-mithl. The commentary further explains that even within each view, the garment should be of middle quality (not cheap, not extravagant), and it reconciles the different opinions by showing that 'middle' actually fits all views depending on the circumstances. The passage also includes a note about regional customs regarding additional garments like the izaar and mak'ab.

Key Terms
متعة (mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a woman divorced before consummation when no mahr was specified in the contract.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dower for a woman of similar status, used as a benchmark when no mahr is specified.
كرباس (karbās): A coarse cotton fabric, considered low quality for clothing.
قز (qazz): A type of silk blend, considered middle quality.
إبريسم (ibrīsam): Pure silk, considered high quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only the wife's status matters

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position on mut'ah is to consider both spouses' status, with a minimum of 5 dirhams and a maximum of half the woman's mahr al-mithl, given in a middle-quality garment.

Mahr Fixed After Contract Is Not Halved by Divorce Before Consummation
Ruling that mahr fixed after the contract is not halved upon divorce before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr fixed after the contract when divorce occurs before consummation and explain the proof from the Quran and analogy.

Core Idea
Post-contract mahr is a specification of mahr al-mithl, not a contractual mahr, so it is not halved upon divorce before consummation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq addresses a nuanced issue in nikah: the effect of divorce before consummation on mahr. The Quran (2:237) commands half of 'what you fixed' (faradhtum). But does this include mahr determined after the marriage contract? The Hanafi school clarifies that the customary meaning of 'fixing' refers to the contract itself. Therefore, post-contract mahr is not halved; it is merely a specification of the obligatory mahr al-mithl. The author uses a vivid analogy from pre-emption (shuf‘ah) to reinforce this distinction.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify the general ruling: mahr fixed after the contract is not halved by divorce before consummation. Note that this applies whether the fixing is by mutual agreement or by a judge's decree.
This is the core legal position being established.
2
Identify the Quranic text
Locate the verse cited: 'then half of what you fixed' (Al-Baqarah 2:237). Understand that the word 'faradhtum' is the key term.
The verse is the primary textual evidence (dalil naqli).
3
Understand the customary meaning of 'faradhtum'
Analyze why the Hanafi school restricts 'fixing' to the contract. The author argues that 'customary fixing' is the fixing that occurs at the time of the contract, not any later specification.
This is a usul al-fiqh move: restricting the general ('amm) based on custom.
4
Apply the analogy to pre-emption (shuf‘ah)
Examine the analogy: if a husband gives a house as mahr after the contract, the pre-emptor has no right of pre-emption because it is not a sale. But if the house is given as a substitute for mahr specified in the contract, it is a sale and pre-emption applies. Similarly, post-contract mahr is not a sale and thus not halved.
This analogy reinforces that post-contract mahr is merely a specification, not a contractual term.
5
Note the extension to judge's fixing
Recognize that the same ruling applies when a judge fixes mahr al-mithl for the woman. The judge's fixing is also considered a specification, not a contractual term, so it is not halved.
The author clarifies this to prevent confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وما فرض بعد العقد أو زيد لا يتنصف أي بالطلاق قبل الدخول أما ما فرض بعد العقد فلأن هذا الفرض تعيين للواجب بالعقد وهو مهر المثل بدليل أنه لا شفعة للشفيع لو فرض لها داراً بعد العقد بخلاف ما لو دفع لها الدار بدلاً . عن المسمى في العقد فإن له الشفعة لأنه بيع بدليل أنها لو طلقت قبل الدخول ترد نصف المسمى لا نصف الدار وذلك لا يتنصف، فكذا ما نزل منزلته والمراد بقوله تعالى فنصف ما فرضتم [البقرة: ٢٣٧] المفروض في العقد إذ هو الفرض المتعارف. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الفرض بعد العقد بتراضيهما أو بفرض القاضي فإن لها أن ترفعه إلى القاضي ليفرض لها إذا لم يكن فرض لها في العقد. كذا في فتح القدير. وقد يقال : إن فرض القاضي المذكور إذا لم يكن برضاه فهو مجيئه بذلك الكلام على صورة الاعتراض يوهم أنه غير ما أنه تقرير وتوضيح له لأن حاصله أن ما فرضه القاضي مهر المثل فهو لا يتنصف كما فرض بتراضيهما وكلام الفتح في ذلك كما لا يخفى. قال في النهر : والمراد بفرض القاضي مهر المثل لما في قبله
His statement: 'And whatever is fixed after the contract or increased is not halved' i.e., by divorce before consummation. As for what is fixed after the contract, this fixing is a specification of what is obligatory by the contract, which is mahr al-mithl. The proof is that there is no pre-emption for the pre-emptor if he fixes a house for her after the contract, contrary to if he gives her the house as a substitute for the specified [mahr] in the contract, then he has pre-emption because it is a sale. The proof is that if she is divorced before consummation, she returns half of the specified [mahr], not half of the house, and that [the house] is not halved. Similarly, what takes its place. And the meaning of His statement 'then half of what you fixed' [2:237] is the fixing in the contract, for that is the customary fixing. He [the author] gave it absolutely, so it includes whether the fixing is after the contract by mutual agreement or by the judge's decree, because she may raise the matter to the judge to fix for her if nothing was fixed for her in the contract. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And it may be said: That fixing by the judge if it is without his [the husband's] consent... He brings this statement in the form of an objection, suggesting it is other than what it is, while it is an affirmation and clarification, because the gist is that what the judge fixes as mahr al-mithl is not halved, just as what is fixed by mutual agreement. And the statement of al-Fath in that regard is as is not hidden. He said in al-Nahr: What is meant by the judge's fixing is mahr al-mithl because of what precedes it.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on mahr fixed after the marriage contract. If a mahr is determined after the contract (by mutual agreement or by a judge) and then divorce occurs before consummation, that mahr is not halved. The reason is that such a fixing is merely a specification of the mahr al-mithl that was already obligatory from the contract. In contrast, mahr specified in the contract is halved by Quran 2:237. The author proves this by analogy to pre-emption: if a husband fixes a house as mahr after the contract, the pre-emptor has no right of pre-emption because it is not a sale of the house; but if the husband gives the house as a substitute for the mahr specified in the contract, then it is a sale and pre-emption applies. Similarly, if the house were given as mahr specified in the contract, it would be halved upon divorce before consummation, but if fixed later, it is not halved. The same applies to mahr al-mithl fixed by a judge: it is not halved. The passage also notes that the judge's fixing is considered as mahr al-mithl, not as a contractual term.

Key Terms
فرض (farḍ): The specification of mahr in the marriage contract or thereafter.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dower of a woman of similar status, which becomes obligatory by the contract itself if no mahr is specified.
شفعة (shuf'ah): Pre-emption right of a co-owner to purchase a sold share in property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on mahr fixed after the marriage contract if divorce occurs before consummation?
A) Half of that mahr is due
B) The full mahr is due
C) Only mahr al-mithl is due
D) Nothing is due

Key Takeaway
Mahr fixed after the marriage contract is not halved by divorce before consummation; it is a specification of mahr al-mithl.

Increase (Ziyada) in Mahr: Conditions and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Detailed exposition of the ruling on increase in mahr and its conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on increase in mahr, identify the conditions for its validity, and explain the dispute between Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn regarding increase after the wife's death.

Core Idea
Increase in mahr is valid without special wording, but its attachment to the original contract triggers inheritance effects, disputed after death.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the rules of ziyada in mahr. It clarifies that no specific wording of 'increase' is needed, and covers various scenarios including after divorce, manumission, and even after death—where Abu Hanifah differs from his two students. The key principle is 'iltihaq bi asl al-'aqd' which governs legal consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
Recognize that the increase in mahr is a valid (sahih) act separate from the original contract.
2
Understand the condition of specification
The increase must specify a known amount; otherwise it is invalid due to ignorance (jahalah).
No specific wording of 'increase' is required.
3
Explore the scenarios covered
The increase can occur after the wife has gifted or remitted the mahr, after her death, after revocable divorce, and after manumission of a slave-wife.
Each scenario has specific rulings.
4
Focus on the dispute after wife's death
Abu Hanifah validates the increase if the heirs accept; the Sahibayn reject it by analogy to sale.
The author supports Abu Hanifah's view.
5
Analyze the principle of iltihaq bi asl al-'aqd
This principle treats the increase as part of the original contract, affecting inheritance and priority.
It is the basis for the disputed qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبما نقلناه علم أنه لا يشترط في صحتها لفظ الزيادة. وأشار بقوله «زيد» إلى أنه معلوم فلو قال زدتك في مهرك ولم يعين لم تصح الزيادة للجهالة كما في الواقعات. وأطلق في صحة الزيادة فأفاد أنها صحيحة بلا شهود كما في القنية، وشمل الزيادة بعد هبة المهر والإبراء منه، وشمل ما إذا كانت الزيادة من جنس المهر أو من غير جنسه كما في أنفع الوسائل، وشمل ما إذا زاد بعد موتها فإنها صحيحة إذا قبلت الورثة عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما كما في التبيين من البيوع، وشمل ما إذا كان بعد الطلاق الرجعي قبل انقضاء العدة وأما بعد انقضاء العدة في الرجعي وبعد الطلاق البائن فلم أر فيه نقلاً قال في أنفع الوسائل : وقياس الزيادة بعد موتها تصح فيهما عند أبي حنيفة بل بالطريق الأولى لأن في الموت انقطع النكاح وفات محل التمليك وبعد الطلاق ،قابل وما ذكر في إكراه شيخ الإسلام من أن الزيادة في المهر بعد الفرقة باطلة هكذا روى بشر عن أبي يوسف قال : إذا طلق امرأته ثلاثاً قبل الدخول بها أو بعده ثم زاده في المهر لم تصح الزيادة محمول على أنه قول أبي يوسف وحده لا على قول أبي حنيفة لأن أبا يوسف خالفه في الزيادة بعد موت المرأة فيكون قد مشى على أصله ا هـ. الزيادة بعد عتقها فذكر في التبيين في زيادة المبيع والثمن أنه لو زوج أمته ثم أعتقها ثم زاد الزوج على مهرها بعد العتق تكون الزيادة للمولى لأنها تلتحق بأصل العقد ا هـ .
أن عقد صحیح وأما ويوافقه ما قوله : (وبما نقلنا الخ) رد على ما مر عن الظهيرية من قوله لأنها ليست بزيادة لفظاً. قلت : لكن صاحب الظهيرية لم يشترط لفظ الزيادة مطلقاً بل حاصل كلامه أنها لا تلزم إلا إذا كانت بلفظ الزيادة أو ثبتت في ضمن العقد، وما ذكره هنا عن الولوالجية إنما ثبتت فيه لكونها في ضمن بخلاف تجديد النكاح فإنه حيث لم يصح العقد الثاني لم يوجد عقد، نعم عليه مسألة الإقرار المارة عن الفقيه أبي الليث لكن في شرح الوهبانية : إذا وهبت مهرها للزوج ثم بعد ذلك أشهد عليه أن لها عليه كذا وكذا من مهرها ولم يسمه زيادة تكلموا فيه قال في التتمة: اختلف المشايخ فيه قال الفقيه أبو الليث : والأصح عندي أنه يصح ويجعل كأنه زاد في المهر بعد هبة المهر، والأشبه أن لا يصح ولا يجعل زيادة إلا إذا نوى الزيادة ا هـ . فأفاد أن نية الزيادة قائمة مقام لفظها . وفي أنفع الوسائل : ولا يشترط في الزيادة لفظ الزيادة بل يصح بلفظها وبقوله راجعتك بكذا إن قبلت ذلك منه يكون زيادة وإن لم يكن بلفظ زدتك في مهرك، وكذا تصح الزيادة بتجديد النكاح . وإن لم يكن بلفظ الزيادة على خلاف فيه، وكذا لو أقر لزوجته بمهر وكانت قد وهبته له فإنه يصح وإن لم يكن بلفظ الزيادة لكن لا بد من القبول في مجلس الإقرار ا.هـ. قوله : (قال في أنفع الوسائل وقياس الزيادة الخ) قال في النهر : الظاهر عدم جوازها بعد الموت والبينونة وإليه يرشد تقييد المحيط بحال قيام النكاح إذ قد نقلوا أن ظاهر الرواية أن الزيادة بعد هلاك المبيع لا تصح، وفي رواية النوادر تصح، ومن ثم جزم في المعراج وغيره بأن شرطها بقاء الزوجية حتى لو زادها بعد موتها لم تصح
في المحيط من آخر باب نكاح الإماء : قال الزوج للمعتقة لك خمسون درهماً على أن تختاريني لزم العقد ولا شيء لها لأنه لا يصح أخذ العوض عنه، ولو قال اختاريني ولك خمسون درهماً زيادة على صداقك صحت وتجب الزيادة للمولى لأنه وجب بدلاً عن البضع لأنه زيد على الصداق والمال يصلح عوضاً عن البضع فيلتحق بأصل العقد ا هـ. ويخالفه ما في المحيط أيضاً من باب خيار العتق والبلوغ رجل زوج أمته من رجل ثم أعتقها ثم زاد الزوج في المهر فالزيادة لها ولا أجبر الزوج على دفع الزيادة للمرأة، وكذلك إن باعها فالزيادة للمشتري ولا أجبره على دفع الزيادة إليه لأنها بمنزلة الهبة ا.هـ. وهو ضعيف لأنه رواية المنتقى ولمخالفته الأصل الممهد وهو الالتحاق بأصل العقد. وفي التلخيص وشرحه : لو قال زدتك في صداقك كذا على أن تختاريني ففعلت بطل خيارها وتكون الزيادة للمولى للالتحاق كالزيادة بعد موت البائع، إذا قبل الوارث تكون للميت حتى تقضي منها ديونه وتنفذ وصاياه بخلاف تعليق الزيادة بدخول الدار حيث لا يصح ولا يجب شيء لأنها معتبرة بأصل العقد ا هـ. وقيد بزيادة المهر لأن زيادة المنكوحة لا تجوز كما إذا زوجه أمة ثم زاده أخرى لأن الشرع ما ورد بتمليك الزيادة المتولدة في المملوكة بالنكاح تبعاً للمنكوحة بخلاف البيع كما سيأتي في بابه.
And by what we have transmitted, it is known that the word 'increase' is not a condition for its validity. And He indicated by his saying 'increase' that it is known; so if he said 'I increase your mahr' and did not specify, the increase is not valid due to ignorance as in al-Waqi'at. And he gave an absolute ruling on the validity of the increase, indicating that it is valid without witnesses as in al-Qunyah. And it includes the increase after hibah of the mahr and ibra' from it, and includes when the increase is of the same type as the mahr or not as in Anfa' al-Wasa'il. And it includes when he increases after her death: it is valid if the heirs accept, according to Abu Hanifah, contrary to them (the Sahibayn) as in al-Tabyin from the book of sales. And it includes when it is after revocable divorce before the expiration of the 'iddah; as for after the expiration of the 'iddah in revocable divorce and after irrevocable divorce, I have not found a transmission. He said in Anfa' al-Wasa'il: The analogy of the increase after her death is that it is valid according to Abu Hanifah in both cases, even by primary reasoning, because in death the marriage is severed and the locus of ownership is lost, and after divorce... And what is mentioned in Ikrah Shaykh al-Islam that the increase in mahr after separation is invalid: thus Bishr narrated from Abu Yusuf: if he divorced his wife three times before or after consummation and then increased her mahr, the increase is not valid. This is taken as the view of Abu Yusuf alone, not Abu Hanifah's, because Abu Yusuf differed from him regarding increase after the wife's death, so he proceeded on his principle. End. The increase after her manumission: It is mentioned in al-Tabyin regarding increase of the sold item and price: if he married off his slave-girl then manumitted her, then the husband increased her mahr after manumission, the increase belongs to the master because it attaches to the original contract. End. That [؟] valid contract. And [؟] agrees with it. His saying: (And by what we transmitted) is a rebuttal to what was mentioned earlier from al-Dhahiriyyah: 'because it is not an increase in wording.' I say: But the author of al-Dhahiriyyah did not stipulate the wording of increase absolutely; rather, the purport of his speech is that it is not binding unless it is with the wording of increase or established within the contract. What is mentioned here from al-Walwaljiyyah is established because it is within the contract, contrary to renewing the marriage, for if the second contract is not valid, no contract exists. Yes, there remains the issue of acknowledgment from al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, but in Sharh al-Wahbaniyyah: If she gave her mahr to her husband and then after that he made witnesses that he owes her such-and-such of her mahr, without specifying an increase, they spoke about it. In al-Tatimmah: The mashayikh differed on it. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: The most correct in my view is that it is valid and it is treated as if he increased the mahr after hibah of the mahr. The more likely opinion is that it is not valid and it is not considered an increase unless he intended increase. End. So it indicates that intention of increase stands in place of its wording. And in Anfa' al-Wasa'il: The word 'increase' is not required for the increase; rather, it is valid by its wording and by his saying 'I return to you for such-and-such' if she accepts that from him, it is an increase even if not with the wording 'I increase your mahr'. Likewise, the increase is valid by renewing the marriage even if not with the wording of increase, though there is difference. Likewise, if he acknowledged to his wife a mahr while she had given it to him, it is valid even if not with the wording of increase, but acceptance is required in the council of acknowledgment. End. His saying: (He said in Anfa' al-Wasa'il: The analogy of the increase...) He said in al-Nahr: The apparent view is its impermissibility after death and separation, and that is guided by the restriction in al-Muhit to the state of marriage subsisting, since they have transmitted that the apparent ruling in the zahir al-riwayah is that increase after the destruction of the sold item is not valid, and in the narration of al-Nawadir it is valid. Hence, it was decisively stated in al-Mi'raj and others that its condition is the continuation of marriage, so much so that if he increased after her death, it is not valid. In al-Muhit from the end of Bab Nikah al-Imai': The husband said to the manumitted woman: 'You have fifty dirhams on condition that you choose me' – the contract is binding and she gets nothing because it is not valid to take compensation for it. And if he said 'Choose me and you have fifty dirhams as an increase on your mahr', it is valid and the increase is obligatory for the master because it became due in exchange for the vulva, because it was added to the mahr, and money is suitable as compensation for the vulva, so it attaches to the original contract. End. And what is in al-Muhit from Bab Khiyar al-'Itq wa al-Bulugh contradicts it: A man married off his slave-girl to a man, then manumitted her, then the husband increased the mahr – the increase is for her, and the husband is not forced to pay the increase to the woman. Likewise, if he sold her, the increase is for the buyer and he is not forced to pay the increase to him because it is like a gift. End. It is weak because it is a narration of al-Muntaqa and because it contradicts the established principle, which is attachment to the original contract. And in al-Talkhis and its commentary: If he said 'I increase your mahr by such-and-such on condition that you choose me' and she did so, her option is void and the increase belongs to the master due to attachment, like the increase after the death of the seller; if the heir accepts, it becomes for the deceased to settle debts and execute bequests, unlike suspending the increase on entering the house, where it is not valid and nothing is due because it is considered part of the original contract. End. And it is restricted to increase of mahr because increase of the married woman is not permissible, like if he marries him a slave-girl and then adds another, because the Law has not permitted ownership of the increase generated in the slave by marriage as a follow-up to the married woman, unlike sale as will come in its chapter.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the ruling of increasing the mahr. The author clarifies that no specific wording of 'increase' is required; any expression indicating an addition suffices, provided the amount is specified. The increase is valid without witnesses, contrary to the initial marriage contract. The passage covers various scenarios: increase after the wife has gifted or remitted the mahr, increase after her death (a point where Abu Hanifah differs from the Sahibayn—the former validates it if heirs accept, the latter reject), increase after revocable and irrevocable divorce, and increase after the wife's manumission. The intra-Hanafi dispute is highlighted: Abu Hanifah's view that increase after death is valid by qiyas and primary reasoning, while Abu Yusuf's narration from Bishr indicates invalidity but is confined to Abu Yusuf's own view. The author also discusses the principle of 'iltihaq bi asl al-'aqd' (attachment to the original contract), which governs whether the increase belongs to the wife or her master/mawla in the case of a former slave-girl. A contradiction in al-Muhit is noted and resolved by deeming the opposing narration weak as it is from al-Muntaqa and contradicts the established principle. The passage concludes by distinguishing increase in mahr from increase in the married woman herself, which is prohibited.

Key Terms
زيادة (ziyada): Increase in the mahr after the original contract, whether by adding a sum or item, and can be effected by any expression indicating addition.
التحاق بأصل العقد (iltihaq bi asl al-'aqd): The principle that an increase in mahr is treated as part of the original marriage contract, thus its rulings (e.g., priority for debts) apply retrospectively.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad in the six core books, which carry more weight than nawadir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true regarding increase in mahr according to the Hanafi school?
A) It requires the word 'ziyada' exactly.
B) It is valid only during the marriage.
C) It is valid after the wife's death if heirs accept (Abu Hanifah).
D) It must be witnessed.

Key Takeaway
Increase in mahr is valid by any expression indicating addition and attaches to the original contract; after death, Abu Hanifah validates it with heirs' acceptance, which is the operative view.
