Remission (Hatt) of the Mahr: Definition and Conditions
Ruling on the wife remitting part or all of her mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of hatt, list its conditions, and distinguish between valid remission of a debt and invalid remission of a specific object.

Core Idea
A wife can drop her mahr without husband's acceptance, but only if it is a debt — remission of a specific object is invalid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines the ruling on hatt (remission) of the mahr by the wife. It clarifies that remission is valid only when the mahr is a debt (dirhams or dinars), not a specific object, and does not require the husband's acceptance. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the correct ruling in marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Name the act: hatt (remission) of the mahr by the wife. State the ruling: sahih (valid) under specific conditions.
2
List the conditions for validity
The mahr must be a debt (dayn), not a specific object ('ayn). The remission is valid whether the husband accepts or not.
Unlike increase (ziyada), which requires the wife's acceptance in the council.
3
Distinguish between debt and specific object
If the mahr is a specific object (e.g., a house), remission is not valid because hatt operates only on debts. She retains the right to take it while it exists.
If the specific object perishes in the husband's hands, the mahr is dropped.
4
Address the debate on acceptance and repulsion
Some views hold that hatt can be repelled by the husband's rejection, but the author finds explicit transmission that it is valid without acceptance, like a gift of debt.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that acceptance is not required.
5
Note the intra-madhhab difference on increase after destruction
The passage mentions a related issue: if the buyer manumits a slave-girl and then increases the price, Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ. This does not affect the ruling on hatt.
This is a distinct case and does not overrule the conditions of hatt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وصح حطها أي حط المرأة من مهرها لأن المهر في حالة البقاء حقها والحط يلاقيه حالة البقاء. الحط في اللغة الإسقاط كما في المغرب أطلقه فشمل حط الكل أو البعض، وشمل ما إذا قبل الزوج أو لم يقبل بخلاف الزيادة فإنه لا بد في صحتها من قبولها في المجلس كما قدمناه وقيد في البدائع الإبراء عن المهر بأن يكون ديناً أي دراهم أو دنانير، وظاهره أن حط المهر العين لا يصح لأن الحط لا يصح في الأعيان. وفي أنفع الوسائل: الظاهر أن الحط يرتد بالرد وإن لم يتوقف على القبول كهبة الدين ممن عليه الدين إذا رد ولم أر فيه نقلاً صريحاً ا اهـ. وقد ظفرت بالنقل صريحاً من فضل الله والله الحمد والمنة. ذكر في والالتحاق بأصل العقد وإن كان يقع مستنداً إلا أنه لا بد أن يثبت أولاً في الحال ثم يستند، وثبوته متعذر لانتفاء المحل فتعذر استناده، وما ذكره القدوري موافق لرواية النوادر. وقد قالوا: لو أعتق المشتري الجارية ثم زاد في الثمن لم يصح وهو قولهما ورويا عنه الصحة ذكره في البزازية ا هـ . قال بعض المحشين: والذي يظهر أن ما في المعراج والمحيط مخرج على قولهما لا ينافي ما في التبيين، وكون ظاهر الرواية عدم صحة الزيادة بعد هلاك المبيع لا يقتضي أن يكون هو ظاهر الرواية هنا لفرق بين الفصلين قام عند المجتهد .
قوله : (لأنه رواية المنتقى) لا يخفى أن تعليل الضعف بذلك غير ظاهر فكان المناسب الاقتصار على التعليل الثاني قوله (وظاهره أن حط المهر العيني لا يصح قال في النهر : معنى عدم صحته أن لها أن تأخذ منه ما دام قائماً فلو هلك في يده سقط المهر عنه لما في البزازية : أبرأتك عن هذا العبد
His saying: (And her remission is valid, i.e., the woman's remission of her mahr, because the mahr while remaining is her right, and remission meets it in a state of remaining. Remission (hatt) in language means dropping, as in al-Mughrib. He gave an absolute ruling, so it includes remitting all or some, and includes whether the husband accepts or not, unlike the increase where acceptance in the council is required for its validity as we have previously mentioned. And in al-Bada'i' he restricted ibra' (release) from the mahr to it being a debt, i.e., dirhams or dinars. His apparent meaning is that remission of a specific mahr (ayn) is not valid because remission is not valid for specific objects. And in Anfa' al-Wasa'il: It appears that remission is repelled by rejection even if it does not depend on acceptance, like the gift of a debt from the debtor; if he rejects, I haven't seen an explicit transmission. End. And I have found an explicit transmission by the grace of Allah, praise and gratitude to Allah. It is mentioned in (?) and attachment to the original contract, even if it occurs retroactively, but it must first be established in the present then retroactive; its establishment is impossible due to the non-existence of the locus, so its retroactive effect is impossible. What al-Quduri mentioned is in agreement with the narration of al-Nawadir. And they said: If the buyer manumits the slave-girl and then increases the price, it is not valid; that is their (the Sahibayn's) view, and they narrated from him (Abu Hanifah?) validity, mentioned in al-Bazzaziyyah. End. Some commentators said: What appears is that what is in al-Mi'raj and al-Muhit is based on their view, not contradicting what is in al-Tabyin; and that the apparent ruling of zahir al-riwayah being the invalidity of increase after destruction of the sold item does not necessitate that it is the apparent ruling here, due to a difference between the two chapters that the mujtahid has established. His saying: (Because it is a narration of al-Muntaqa) It is not hidden that the explanation of weakness by that is not apparent, so it would be appropriate to restrict to the second explanation. His saying: (And his apparent meaning is that remission of a specific mahr (ayni) is not valid) He said in al-Nahr: The meaning of its not being valid is that she can take it from him as long as it remains; if it perishes in his hand, the mahr is dropped from him, as in al-Bazzaziyyah: 'I release you from this slave.'
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage defines the ruling on hatt (remission) of the mahr by the wife. The author first explains that hatt is valid because the mahr is her right, and she can drop it while it remains due. Hatt applies to both full and partial remission, and does not require the husband's acceptance, unlike ziyada (increase) which requires the wife's acceptance in the council. The remission is valid only if the mahr is a debt (dayn) such as dirhams or dinars; if it is a specific object ('ayn), remission is not valid because dropping ownership of a specific object without acceptance is invalid. The passage then discusses whether hatt can be retracted by rejection (like a gift of debt). It mentions that al-Quduri's view aligns with riwayat al-nawadir regarding increase after destruction of sold item. The text then shifts to a discussion on the weakness of a certain narration from al-Muntaqa, and a comment on the difference between increase after death of the seller and other contexts. The final part reaffirms that remission of a specific mahr is not valid, explaining that she retains the right to take it while it exists, and if it perishes in the husband's hands, the mahr is dropped.

Key Terms
حط (hatt): Linguistically 'dropping', legally the wife's remission of part or all of her mahr, valid only if the mahr is a debt.
الإبراء (ibra'): Release from a debt; here used interchangeably with hatt when the mahr is a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a wife's remission (hatt) of the mahr NOT valid?
A) When she remits less than half the mahr
B) When the mahr is a specific item ('ayn) like a house
C) When the husband does not accept the remission
D) When the mahr is a debt in dirhams

Key Takeaway
A wife can validly remit her mahr without the husband's acceptance, but only if the mahr is a debt — not a specific object.

Increase in Dower After Emancipation: Who Receives It?
Ruling with proof on increase in dower after emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of iltihaq bi asl al-aqd to determine that an increase in dower after emancipation goes to the former master, and distinguish this from a weak contrary report.

Core Idea
An increase in dower attaches to the original contract, so it belongs to the former master, not the wife.

When a husband says to his freed wife, 'Choose me, and you have an extra fifty dirhams on your dower,' the marriage is valid and the extra amount is due to the former master (her owner at the time of marriage). But what if the husband simply increases the dower after emancipation without condition? The Hanafi school resolves a conflict between two reports, relying on the fundamental principle that such an increase is attached to the original marriage contract (iltihaq bi asl al-aqd). In this lesson, we trace the reasoning and the weight of authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two statements from the husband: (1) 'You have fifty dirhams on condition that you choose me' — invalid for her to receive anything; (2) 'Choose me, and you have fifty dirhams extra on your dower' — valid and the increase goes to her master.
The key is the wording: 'on condition that you choose me' vs. 'choose me, and you have...'.
2
Understand the rationale for the valid scenario
The increase is treated as part of the original dower because property is a suitable substitute for the vulva (badal al-bud'). It attaches to the original contract (yalhaq bi asl al-aqd).
This principle is central.
3
Recognize the conflicting report and its critique
Another report in al-Muhit says the increase after emancipation belongs to the wife. The author dismisses it as weak because it is from al-Muntaqa (non-zahir al-riwayah) and contradicts the established principle.
The author uses principled reasoning to reject the weak report.
4
Apply the principle to analogous cases
Like an increase after the seller's death accepted by the heir, which belongs to the deceased's estate. Unlike an increase conditioned on entering a house, which is void because it is independent of the contract.
This strengthens the principle by analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في المحيط من آخر باب نكاح الإماء : قال الزوج للمعتقة لك خمسون درهماً على أن تختاريني لزم العقد ولا شيء لها لأنه لا يصح أخذ العوض عنه، ولو قال اختاريني ولك خمسون درهماً زيادة على صداقك صحت وتجب الزيادة للمولى لأنه وجب بدلاً عن البضع لأنه زيد على الصداق والمال يصلح عوضاً عن البضع فيلتحق بأصل العقد ا هـ. ويخالفه ما في المحيط أيضاً من باب خيار العتق والبلوغ رجل زوج أمته من رجل ثم أعتقها ثم زاد الزوج في المهر فالزيادة لها ولا أجبر الزوج على دفع الزيادة للمرأة، وكذلك إن باعها فالزيادة للمشتري ولا أجبره على دفع الزيادة إليه لأنها بمنزلة الهبة ا.هـ. وهو ضعيف لأنه رواية المنتقى ولمخالفته الأصل الممهد وهو الالتحاق بأصل العقد. وفي التلخيص وشرحه : لو قال زدتك في صداقك كذا على أن تختاريني ففعلت بطل خيارها وتكون الزيادة للمولى للالتحاق كالزيادة بعد موت البائع، إذا قبل الوارث تكون للميت حتى تقضي منها ديونه وتنفذ وصاياه بخلاف تعليق الزيادة بدخول الدار حيث لا يصح ولا يجب شيء لأنها معتبرة بأصل العقد ا هـ. وقيد بزيادة المهر لأن زيادة المنكوحة لا تجوز كما إذا زوجه أمة ثم زاده أخرى لأن الشرع ما ورد بتمليك الزيادة المتولدة في المملوكة بالنكاح تبعاً للمنكوحة بخلاف البيع كما سيأتي في بابه.
In al-Muhit from the end of the chapter on marrying slave women: The husband said to the freed woman: 'You have fifty dirhams on condition that you choose me'—the marriage contract is binding and she gets nothing because it is not valid to take a substitute for it. And if he said: 'Choose me, and you have fifty dirhams as an increase over your dower'—it is valid and the increase is obligatory for the master because it is due as a substitute for the vulva, since it is added to the dower and property is suitable as a substitute for the vulva, so it attaches to the original contract. End quote. It is contradicted by what is also in al-Muhit from the chapter on the option of emancipation and puberty: A man married his slave woman to a man, then freed her, then the husband increased the dower—the increase is for her, and the husband is not forced to pay the increase to the woman. Similarly, if he sold her, the increase is for the buyer, and he is not forced to pay the increase to him because it is like a gift. End quote. This (the latter) is weak because it is a narration of al-Muntaqa and because it contradicts the established principle, which is attaching to the original contract. In al-Talkhis and its commentary: If he said: 'I have increased your dower by such-and-such on condition that you choose me,' and she did so, her option becomes void and the increase is for the master due to attachment, like the increase after the death of the seller when the heir accepts it, which belongs to the deceased so that his debts are paid from it and his bequests are executed, unlike if the increase is conditioned on entering the house, where it is not valid and nothing is obligatory because it is considered in relation to the original contract. End quote. And it was restricted to an increase in the dower because an increase in the married woman herself is not allowed, as if he gave him a slave woman in marriage and then added another, because the law does not permit the possession of an increase generated in a female slave by marriage as a consequence of the married woman, unlike in sale, as will come in its chapter.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Muhit regarding the validity of an increase in dower when a husband says to his wife after freeing her: 'You have an extra fifty dirhams on condition that you choose me (i.e., remain with me as a wife).' The ruling: the marriage is binding and she gets no extra compensation for her choice because the increase is actually a substitute for her option to leave, but she cannot take a substitute for the option because it is not property. However, if he says: 'Choose me, and you have an extra fifty dirhams on top of your dower,' then it is valid and the increase goes to her former master (the one who freed her), because the increase becomes part of the dower and is owed to the master as the substitute for the vulva (since she was a slave, her master owned her marriage). The author then notes a conflicting report from another section of al-Muhit, which says that after emancipation, any increase in the dower belongs to the woman herself, not the master. The author dismisses this as weak because it is from al-Muntaqa (a non-zahir al-riwayah source) and contradicts the established principle that such an increase attaches to the original contract (i.e., it is treated as part of the original dower). Then from al-Talkhish, there is a similar case: if a husband says 'I have increased your dower by X on condition that you choose me,' and she does, her option (to leave) is void and the increase goes to the master. The author compares it to an increase after the seller's death, which is accepted by the heir and belongs to the deceased's estate, unlike a conditional increase unrelated to the contract (like conditioning it on entering a house), which is void. Finally, he notes that this increase applies only to the dower, not to the woman herself (i.e., one cannot increase the number of wives by adding another slave).

Key Terms
الالتحاق بأصل العقد (al-iltihāq bi-aṣl al-ʿaqd): The increase attaches to the original marriage contract and is treated as part of the original dower.
بدل البضع (badal al-bud‘): The substitute (value) for the vulva; in a marriage contract, it is the dower (mahr).
زيادة المهر (ziyādat al-mahr): An increase in the dower after the contract, which may be valid if it attaches to the original contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the valid scenario from al-Muhit, where does the increase in dower go?
A) To the wife's father
B) To the former master of the wife
C) To the wife herself
D) To the husband's creditor

Key Takeaway
An increase in dower after emancipation attaches to the original contract and belongs to the former master, not the wife, based on the principle of iltihaq bi asl al-aqd.

Wife's Reduction of Mahr (Hatt): Conditions and Validity
Ruling on wife's reduction of dower with conditions and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a wife's valid reduction of her dower (hatt) and explain why reduction is valid for a debt but not for a specific item.

Core Idea
A wife may reduce her dower only if it is a debt, not a specific item; coercion invalidates the reduction.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on a wife reducing her dower (hatt). The key distinction is whether the dower is a debt (dayn) or a specific item ('ayn). Coercion and the wife's capacity also affect validity. The passage also addresses the father's role and conditional discharges.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The matn states 'Wa sahha hattuhā' — the woman's reduction of her dower is valid. This is the general principle.
Reduction (hatt) includes full or partial reduction, and does not require the husband's acceptance.
2
Distinguish reduction for debt vs. specific item
The passage from al-Bada'i' restricts hatt to when the mahr is a debt (dirhams or dinars). For a specific item ('ayn), hatt is not valid because reduction cannot apply to a physical object.
This is the most important condition.
3
Examine the requirement of consent (no coercion)
The wife must act willingly. Coercion, such as threats of beating or tarnishing reputation, invalidates the hatt.
Examples from al-Khulasa and al-Qunyah illustrate what constitutes coercion.
4
Consider who may perform the reduction
Only the wife herself may reduce the dower. The father's reduction is invalid unless she is an adult and authorizes it.
If the father guarantees the dower without authorization, the guarantee is void.
5
Review subsidiary cases and tricks
The passage discusses conditional discharges and tricks (hila) for women who wish to gift the dower, such as buying an item from the husband with the dower before the gift.
These highlight practical applications and pitfalls.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وصح حطها أي حط المرأة من مهرها لأن المهر في حالة البقاء حقها والحط يلاقيه حالة البقاء. والحط في اللغة الإسقاط كما في المغرب أطلقه فشمل حط الكل أو البعض، وشمل ما إذا قبل الزوج أو لم يقبل بخلاف الزيادة فإنه لا بد في صحتها من قبولها في المجلس كما قدمناه وقيد في البدائع الإبراء عن المهر بأن يكون ديناً أي دراهم أو دنانير، وظاهره أن حط المهر العين لا يصح لأن الحط لا يصح في الأعيان. وفي أنفع الوسائل: الظاهر أن الحط يرتد بالرد وإن لم يتوقف على القبول كهبة الدين ممن عليه الدين إذا رد ولم أر فيه نقلاً صريحاً ا اهـ. وقد ظفرت بالنقل صريحاً من فضل الله والله الحمد والمنة. ذكر في القنية من كتاب المداينات من باب الإبراء من المهر : قالت لزوجها أبرأتك ولم يقل الزوج قبلت أو كان غائباً فقالت أبرأت زوجي يبرأ إلا إذا رده ا.هـ. بلفظه . وقيد بحطها لأن حط أبيها غير صحيح فإن كانت صغيرة فهو باطل وإن كانت كبيرة توقف على إجازتها، فإن ضمنه الأب إن لم تجزه البنت فالضمان باطل كما قدمنا نقله عن الخلاصة في باب الأولياء. ولا بد في صحة حطها من الرضا حتى لو كانت مكرهة لم يصح ولذا قال في الخلاصة من كتاب الهبة : إذا خوف امرأته بضرب حتى وهبت مهرها لا . إن كان قادراً على الضرب ا هـ. وفي القنية من الإكراه : تزوج امرأة سراً وأراد أن تبرأه من المهر فدخل عليها أصدقاؤه وقالوا لها إما أن تبرئيه من المهر وإلا قلنا للشحنة كذا وكذا فيسود وجهك فأبرأته خوفاً من ذلك فهو إكراه ولا يبرأ، ولو لم يقولوا فيسود وجهك والمسألة بحالها فليس بإكراه ا هـ . الكراهية والطوع ولا بينة فالقول لمدعي الإكراه، ولو أقاما البينة فبينة الطواعية أولى كما في القنية في نظيره من الدعوى وفي الخلاصة : قال لمطلقته لا أتزوجك ما لم تهبيني مالك على من المهر فوهبت مهرها على أن يتزوجها ثم إن الزوج أبى أن يتزوجها فالمهر باق على الزوج تزوج أو لم يتزوج، ولو قال لامرأته أبرئيني من مهرك حتى أهب لك كذا فوهبت مهرها وأبى الزوج أن يهب لها ما وعد يعود المهر. ذكره في النكاح وفيها من الهبة: لو قالت لزوجها وهبت مهري منك على أن كل امرأة تتزوجها تجعل أمرها بيدي إن لم يقبل الزوج الهبة لا تصح الهبة، وقد ذكرنا الجواب المختار أنها تصح من غير قبول وإن قبل إن يجعل أمرها بيدها فالهبة ماضية، وإن لم يجعل فكذلك عند البعض، والمختار أن المهر يعود. وعلى هذا لو قالت وهبت مهري منك على أن لا تظلمني أو على أن تجح بي أو على أن تهب لي كذا وإن لم يكن هذا شرطاً في الهبة لا يعود المهر ا هـ . وهو مشكل لأن تعليق الإبراء بالشرط باطل. وفيها من النكاح : لو أحالت إنساناً على الزوج على أن يؤدي من المهر ثم وهبت المهر من الزوج لا يصح وهي الحيلة لمن أرادت أن تهب المهر ولا يصح، ولو وهبت مهرها من أبيها ووكلته بالقبض يصح ا هـ . وفي القنية : وله ثلاث حيل غير هذه إحداها شراء شيء. ملفوف من زوجها بالمهر قبل الهبة والثانية صلح إنسان معها عن المهر بشيء ملفوف قبل الهبة. والثالثة هبة المرأة المهر لابن صغير لها قبل الهبة كذا في كتاب المداينات .
His statement: (And valid is her reduction) i.e., the woman's reduction of her dower because the dower in the state of being (a debt) is her right, and the reduction meets it in the state of being. Reduction in language is removal, as in al-Mughrib. He made it unrestricted, so it includes reduction of all or part, and includes whether the husband accepts or not, unlike increase, which for its validity requires her acceptance in the session as we have mentioned. And it was restricted in al-Bada'i' that discharge (ibra') from the dower must be a debt, i.e., dirhams or dinars. Its apparent meaning is that reduction of a specific dower ('ayn) is not valid because reduction is not valid for specific items. And in Anfa' al-Wasa'il: The apparent view is that reduction is returned by rejection even if it does not depend on acceptance, like a gift of a debt from the debtor if he rejects it. I have not seen an explicit text on it. End quote. And I have found an explicit text by the grace of Allah, praise and thanks be to Allah. Mentioned in al-Qunyah from the book of loans, chapter of discharge from dower: She said to her husband 'I have discharged you' and the husband did not say 'I accept' or he was absent, and she said 'I have discharged my husband'—he is discharged unless he rejects it. End quote verbatim. And it is restricted to her reduction because the reduction by her father is not valid; if she is a minor, it is void; if she is an adult, it is suspended on her authorization. If the father guarantees it and the daughter does not authorize, the guarantee is void as we have quoted from al-Khulasa in the chapter of guardians. And for the validity of her reduction, consent is necessary; even if she is coerced, it is not valid. Hence in al-Khulasa from the book of gifts: If he frightened his wife with a beating until she gave up her dower, it is not valid if he was capable of beating. End quote. And in al-Qunyah from coercion: A man married a woman secretly and wanted her to discharge him from the dower; her friends came to her and said 'Either you discharge him from the dower or we will say such-and-such to the police and your face will be blackened,' so she discharged him out of fear—that is coercion, and he is not discharged. And if they did not say 'your face will be blackened' but the situation is the same, it is not coercion. End quote. Dislike and consent with no evidence: the word is for the claimant of coercion. And if both establish evidence, the evidence of consent is preferable as in al-Qunyah in its like from claims. And in al-Khulasa: He said to his divorced wife: 'I will not marry you unless you gift to me what you have against me from the dower.' So she gifted her dower on condition that he marry her, then the husband refused to marry her—the dower remains with the husband whether he marries or not. And if he said to his wife: 'Discharge me from your dower so that I may gift you such-and-such,' so she discharged her dower and the husband refused to gift what he promised—the dower returns. Mentioned in al-Nikah. And in it from gifts: If she said to her husband 'I have gifted my dower to you on condition that every woman you marry, her affair be in my hand,' if the husband does not accept the gift, the gift is not valid. And we have mentioned the chosen answer that it is valid without acceptance, and if he accepts to put her affair in her hand, the gift is effective; if he does not, the same is true according to some, and the chosen view is that the dower returns. Upon this, if she said 'I have gifted my dower to you on condition that you do not oppress me' or 'that you be kind to me' or 'that you gift me such-and-such,' and this is not a condition in the gift, the dower does not return. End quote. This is problematic because conditioning a discharge (ibra') on a condition is void. And in it from nikah: If she assigned a person to the husband to pay from the dower, then gifted the dower to the husband, it is not valid, and it is a trick for one who wants to gift the dower and it is not valid. And if she gifted her dower to her father and appointed him to receive it, it is valid. End quote. And in al-Qunyah: He has three other tricks: one is buying a covered item from her husband with the dower before the gift; the second is a settlement (sulh) with her by a person for the dower with a covered item before the gift; the third is the woman gifting the dower to a young son of hers before the gift. So it is in the book of loans.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn statement 'Wa sahha hattuhā' (And valid is her reduction). The author first explains the ruling: a woman may reduce her dower because it is her right while it remains a debt. Reduction (hatt) literally means dropping, and it applies whether she reduces all or part, and whether the husband accepts or not. This differs from an increase, which requires acceptance in the session. Then comes an important qualification from al-Bada'i': the reduction (ibra') is valid only if the mahr is a debt (e.g., dirhams or dinars), not a specific item ('ayn). For a specific item, reduction is invalid because hatt cannot apply to a specific physical object. The author then reports a finding from al-Qunyah that if a woman says 'I have discharged you' without the husband's acceptance, he is discharged unless he rejects it. The passage then discusses who can perform the reduction: only the wife herself; her father cannot do so, except if she is an adult and authorizes it. Coercion invalidates the reduction, and various scenarios from al-Khulasa and al-Qunyah illustrate when coercion exists. For example, threatening to report to the police may be coercion. The passage also covers conditional discharges and gifts, such as when a woman gifts her dower conditioned on her husband marrying her or not oppressing her. The author concludes with a general ruling on trickery (hila) for women who want to gift the dower: the gift must be preceded by certain transactions like buying an item from the husband with the dower or making a settlement, as detailed in al-Qunyah.

Key Terms
حط (hatt): Reduction or dropping of a debt by the creditor; here it refers to the wife reducing the dower owed to her.
إبراء (ibrā'): Discharge from a debt; here used synonymously with hatt for the dower.
إكراه (ikrāh): Coercion that invalidates consent; the text discusses threats like beating or tarnishing reputation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a wife reduces her dower, the reduction is valid only if the dower is:
A) A specific item ('ayn)
B) A debt (dayn) such as dirhams or dinars
C) Both specific items and debts
D) A gift from the husband

Key Takeaway
A wife's reduction of her dower is valid only if it is a debt; for a specific item, reduction is invalid.

Validity of Wife's Waiver of Mahr and Conditions
Ruling on wife's waiver of mahr and conditions for validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a wife's waiver of mahr is valid and identify when coercion or a father's act invalidates it.

Core Idea
A wife's verbal waiver of mahr is immediately effective without the husband's acceptance; coercion or father's interference can invalidate it.

In Hanafi fiqh, a wife has the right to waive her mahr (dower) voluntarily, and her waiver is binding even without the husband's explicit acceptance. However, this ruling is subject to conditions: she must not be coerced, and if someone else (like her father) attempts to waive it on her behalf, special rules apply. This lesson explores the key rulings and exceptions from classical Hanafi sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main action and its ruling
Recognize that the passage discusses the validity of a wife's verbal waiver (ibra'/hittah) of her mahr. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) and effective immediately, even without the husband's acceptance.
The husband is discharged unless he explicitly rejects the waiver.
2
List the conditions for a valid waiver
Extract the conditions mentioned: the wife must state the waiver voluntarily (not coerced), and it must be her own act (not her father's unauthorised act).
Consent (rida) is essential; coercion (ikrah) invalidates.
3
Examine the father's waiver
Note the distinction: a father's waiver of his daughter's mahr is void if she is a minor, and conditional on her permission if she is an adult.
The father's guarantee (daman) tied to such a waiver is also void if the daughter does not accept.
4
Understand coercion (ikrah) and its effect
Analyze the examples of coercion: a threat of beating or public humiliation that the husband can carry out constitutes coercion and invalidates the waiver. A mere request or threat not credible is not coercion.
The ability to carry out the threat matters.
5
Apply the evidence rule
When there is a dispute about coercion, the claimant's word is taken if no evidence; if both bring evidence, the evidence of willing action (taw'iyyah) is preferred.
This is from al-Qunya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يصح ولو اختلفا في القنية من كتاب المداينات من باب الإبراء من المهر : قالت لزوجها أبرأتك ولم يقل الزوج قبلت أو كان غائباً فقالت أبرأت زوجي يبرأ إلا إذا رده ا.هـ. بلفظه . وقيد بحطها لأن حط أبيها غير صحيح فإن كانت صغيرة فهو باطل وإن كانت كبيرة توقف على إجازتها، فإن ضمنه الأب إن لم تجزه البنت فالضمان باطل كما قدمنا نقله عن الخلاصة في باب الأولياء. ولا بد في صحة حطها من الرضا حتى لو كانت مكرهة لم يصح ولذا قال في الخلاصة من كتاب الهبة : إذا خوف امرأته بضرب حتى وهبت مهرها لا . إن كان قادراً على الضرب ا هـ. وفي القنية من الإكراه : تزوج امرأة سراً وأراد أن تبرأه من المهر فدخل عليها أصدقاؤه وقالوا لها إما أن تبرئيه من المهر وإلا قلنا للشحنة كذا وكذا فيسود وجهك فأبرأته خوفاً من ذلك فهو إكراه ولا يبرأ، ولو لم يقولوا فيسود وجهك والمسألة بحالها فليس بإكراه ا هـ . الكراهية والطوع ولا بينة فالقول لمدعي الإكراه، ولو أقاما البينة فبينة الطواعية أولى كما في القنية في نظيره من الدعوى
It is valid even if they differ. In al-Qunya from Kitab al-Mudayanat, chapter of Ibra' from Mahr: She said to her husband 'I have discharged you' and the husband did not say 'I accept', or he was absent and she said 'I have discharged my husband' – he is discharged unless he rejects it. End quote verbatim. And it is restricted to her own waiver, because her father's waiver is not valid. If she is a minor, it is void; if she is an adult, it depends on her permission. If the father guarantees it and the daughter does not permit, the guarantee is void as we previously quoted from al-Khulasa in the chapter of guardians. For the validity of her waiver, consent is necessary; so if she is coerced, it is not valid. Hence al-Khulasa said in Kitab al-Hiba: If he frightens his wife with beating until she gives her mahr, it is not valid if he is able to beat. End quote. And in al-Qunya on coercion: He married a woman secretly and wanted her to discharge him from the mahr; her friends entered upon her and told her: 'Either you discharge him from the mahr, or we will tell the police such and such and your face will be blackened.' So she discharged him out of fear – this is coercion and he is not discharged. If they did not say 'your face will be blackened' while the situation is the same, it is not coercion. End quote. Hatred and willingness – if there is no evidence, the word is for the one claiming coercion. If both bring evidence, the evidence of willingness is given precedence, as in al-Qunya in its analogue from claims.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of rulings from various Hanafi sources regarding the validity of a wife's waiver of her mahr (dower). The main ruling is that if a wife says 'I have discharged you from the mahr' and the husband does not accept explicitly, or is absent, the discharge takes effect immediately unless the husband later explicitly rejects it. This is from al-Qunya. The author then notes that this applies only to the wife's own waiver; a father's waiver of his daughter's mahr is invalid. If the daughter is a minor (saghira), the father's waiver is void (batil). If she is an adult (kabira), it hinges on her permission. If the father guarantees the mahr and the daughter does not accept, the guarantee is also void. Then the passage discusses coercion (ikrah): a coerced waiver is not valid. The test is whether the husband was able to carry out the threat; if he could beat her, the threat is real and the waiver is invalid. A specific example from al-Qunya: a man married secretly; the wife's friends threatened to tell the authorities to shame her; that is coercion. But if they merely asked without that threat, it is not coercion. Finally, if there is no evidence, the claim of coercion is believed. If both bring evidence, the evidence that she acted willingly is given precedence.

Key Terms
ابراء (ibra'): A wife's legal discharge of her husband from the obligation to pay the mahr; a form of waiver or release.
حط (hittah): Waiver or reduction of a debt; specifically here the wife's waiver of the mahr.
إكراه (ikrah): Coercion that renders a legal act invalid; a coerced waiver is not valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife says to her husband 'I have discharged you from the mahr' and he remains silent, what is the ruling?
A) The husband must explicitly accept for it to be valid.
B) The discharge is invalid because the husband did not respond.
C) The husband is discharged immediately unless he later rejects it.
D) The discharge is valid only if she says it twice.

Key Takeaway
A wife's verbal waiver of mahr is effective immediately without the husband's acceptance, but coercion or the father's unauthorized waiver invalidates it.

Conditional Waiver of Mahr and Legal Tricks
Ruling on conditional mahr waiver and permissible legal strategies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid conditional waivers of mahr and state the three permissible legal tricks that achieve a proper waiver.

Core Idea
A direct conditional waiver of mahr is void; use a legal trick to achieve the same result validly.

In Hanafi fiqh, the waiver of mahr (ibra') is normally valid, but attaching a condition suspending the waiver on a future event invalidates it. However, the school permits certain legal stratagems (hiyal) to indirectly achieve a waiver without violating the prohibition on conditional ibra'. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines problematic conditional waivers and presents three valid alternatives from later authoritative works like al-Qunya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the invalid conditional waiver scenarios
The passage gives examples where a wife conditions the waiver of her mahr on the husband's action (e.g., remarriage, giving a gift). Recognize that these conditional waivers are problematic because ibra' cannot be suspended on a condition in Hanafi law.
The first example: the husband says 'I will not marry you unless you gift me your mahr.' She gifts it conditionally; he refuses, the mahr remains.
2
Understand the problematic nature of certain conditions
Some conditions like 'do not oppress me' are not direct conditions of the gift but are attached to the person. The text notes that the chosen view says the mahr does not return in such cases, but the author finds this problematic because suspending ibra' is generally void.
This tension shows the limits of hiyal: even indirect conditions may be problematic.
3
List the three valid legal tricks from al-Qunya
The three hiyal are: (1) the wife buys a wrapped item from the husband using the mahr before any gift, (2) she makes a settlement (sulh) with a third party concerning the mahr for a wrapped item, (3) she gifts the mahr to her young son before any condition. These transfer ownership away from the conditional promise.
Each trick transfers the mahr to something else, avoiding a direct conditional waiver.
4
Apply the principle: why do these tricks work?
These tricks work because they transfer ownership of the mahr to a specific item or to a third party before any conditional promise. The waiver then occurs naturally through a separate transaction, not through a suspended ibra'.
The hiyal are genuine transactions, not shams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة : قال لمطلقته لا أتزوجك ما لم تهبيني مالك على من المهر فوهبت مهرها على أن يتزوجها ثم إن الزوج أبى أن يتزوجها فالمهر باق على الزوج تزوج أو لم يتزوج، ولو قال لامرأته أبرئيني من مهرك حتى أهب لك كذا فوهبت مهرها وأبى الزوج أن يهب لها ما وعد يعود المهر. ذكره في النكاح وفيها من الهبة: لو قالت لزوجها وهبت مهري منك على أن كل امرأة تتزوجها تجعل أمرها بيدي إن لم يقبل الزوج الهبة لا تصح الهبة، وقد ذكرنا الجواب المختار أنها تصح من غير قبول وإن قبل إن يجعل أمرها بيدها فالهبة ماضية، وإن لم يجعل فكذلك عند البعض، والمختار أن المهر يعود. وعلى هذا لو قالت وهبت مهري منك على أن لا تظلمني أو على أن تجح بي أو على أن تهب لي كذا وإن لم يكن هذا شرطاً في الهبة لا يعود المهر ا هـ . وهو مشكل لأن تعليق الإبراء بالشرط باطل. وفيها من النكاح : لو أحالت إنساناً على الزوج على أن يؤدي من المهر ثم وهبت المهر من الزوج لا يصح وهي الحيلة لمن أرادت أن تهب المهر ولا يصح، ولو وهبت مهرها من أبيها ووكلته بالقبض يصح ا هـ . وفي القنية : وله ثلاث حيل غير هذه إحداها شراء شيء. ملفوف من زوجها بالمهر قبل الهبة والثانية صلح إنسان معها عن المهر بشيء ملفوف قبل الهبة. والثالثة هبة المرأة المهر لابن صغير لها قبل الهبة كذا في كتاب المداينات .
And in al-Khulasa: He said to his divorced wife: 'I will not marry you unless you gift me your mahr that is owed to you.' So she gifted her mahr on condition that he marry her, then the husband refused to marry her – the mahr remains due on the husband, whether he married or not. And if he said to his wife: 'Discharge me from your mahr so that I may gift you such-and-such,' and she discharged her mahr [but] the husband refused to gift her what he promised, the mahr returns. Mentioned in al-Nikah. And in it from al-Hiba: If she says to her husband, 'I have gifted my mahr to you on condition that every woman you marry, you put her affair in my hand' – if the husband does not accept the gift, the gift is not valid. And we have mentioned the chosen answer that it is valid without acceptance, and if he accepts to put her affair in her hand, the gift is effective; if he does not, then according to some it is still effective, but the chosen view is that the mahr returns. Based on this, if she says, 'I have gifted my mahr to you on condition that you do not oppress me' or 'that you do not lie to me' or 'that you gift me such-and-such,' and this condition is not a condition in the gift, the mahr does not return. End quote. But this is problematic because suspending discharge on a condition is void. And in it from al-Nikah: If she transferred (hawala) a person to the husband to pay the mahr, then she gifted the mahr to the husband, it is not valid. This is a legal trick for one who wants to gift the mahr but it is not valid. And if she gifted her mahr to her father and appointed him to take possession, it is valid. End quote. And in al-Qunya: He has three other legal tricks besides this: one: buying something wrapped from her husband with the mahr before the gift; second: making a composition (sulh) with someone concerning the mahr for something wrapped before the gift; third: the woman gifting the mahr to her young son before the gift – as in Kitab al-Mudayanat.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage addresses conditional waivers of mahr and presents valid alternatives (hiyal) to achieve a proper waiver. The first case from al-Khulasa: a man tells his divorced wife he will not remarry her unless she gifts him the mahr. She does so conditionally, but he refuses to marry – the mahr remains due. This shows that a conditional gift (hiba) with a failed condition does not transfer ownership. Similarly, if a husband promises a gift in exchange for waiver and then reneges, the mahr returns. The text then discusses a case where the wife gifts her mahr on condition that the husband puts the control of his future marriages in her hand. The chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that if the husband does not accept the condition, the mahr returns; but if the condition is not a condition of the gift (e.g., 'do not oppress me'), the mahr does not return. The author notes that this latter ruling is problematic (mushkil) because suspending ibra' on a condition is generally void in Hanafi law. The passage then presents three valid legal strategies (hiyal) from al-Qunya for a wife who wishes to waive her mahr validly: (1) buy something wrapped from the husband using the mahr before the gift, (2) make a settlement (sulh) with someone concerning the mahr for something wrapped, (3) gift the mahr to her young son. These tricks circumvent the rule that a direct conditional waiver is problematic.

Key Terms
حيلة (hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible outcome while avoiding a prohibited or invalid transaction.
صلح (sulh): A settlement or compromise; here used as a legal trick to transfer the mahr via a composition.
إبراء (ibra'): A discharge or waiver of a debt; here, the waiver of the mahr obligation.
مهر (mahr): The obligatory bridal gift (dower) from husband to wife upon marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is a valid legal trick (hila) to waive mahr?
A) The wife says 'I waive my mahr if you marry me again.'
B) The wife buys a wrapped item from her husband using the mahr before any gift.
C) The wife transfers her mahr to a third party on condition that the husband pays her later.
D) The wife gifts her mahr to her husband directly without any condition.

Key Takeaway
Direct conditional waiver of mahr is void; use one of the three hiyal (buying a wrapped item, sulh with a third party, or gifting to a young son) to achieve a valid waiver.

Conditional Ibra' vs Conditional Gift: Resolving a Hanafi Difficulty
Commentary resolving the problematic nature of conditional ibra' as conditional gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a conditional discharge (ibra') and a conditional gift (hiba) in Hanafi law, and state the ruling for each based on the condition's suitability.

Core Idea
A gift with a suitable condition is valid; a discharge cannot be suspended.

This marginal note from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses an apparent problem in a fatwa where a conditional discharge (ibra') was treated as valid. The commentator resolves it by reclassifying the transaction as a conditional gift (hiba). In Hanafi fiqh, gifts can be conditional with suitable conditions, but discharge cannot be suspended. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the correct ruling in marriage settlements and other transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent problem
The issue is a statement in al-Qunya that seems to allow conditional ibra' when the condition is separate. This conflicts with the rule that ibra' cannot be conditional.
The problem arises from mislabeling the transaction as ibra' instead of hiba.
2
Reclassify as conditional gift
The commentator explains that the case is not about ibra' but about a gift (hiba) with a condition, which is permissible if the condition is suitable.
The condition is phrased as 'on condition that' (bi-shart), not 'if' (in).
3
Define 'suitable condition' (shart mulā'im)
A condition that is compatible with the nature of the contract, such as a condition of mutual exchange in a gift.
Unsuitable conditions include those that contradict the essence of the contract.
4
Apply the Hanafi rule for conditional gifts
If the condition is suitable, the gift is valid; if unsuitable, the condition is void but the gift remains valid.
This rule is from al-Bazzaziyya and is mufta bihi.
5
Resolve the apparent contradiction
The original fatwa is correct because it actually deals with a conditional gift, not a conditional discharge.
The marginal note removes the confusion by correcting the legal category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يبقى العبد وديعة عنده . قوله (ذكر في القنية الخ) قال في النهر : لا يخفى أن المدعي إنما هو رد الحط وكأنه نظر إلى أنه إبراء معنى قوله : (وهو مشكل) أجيب بأن هذا من باب تعليق الهبة بشرط ملائم لا من باب تعليق الإبراء بالشرط كما هو ظاهر قال في البزازية وتعليق الهبة بكلمة «إن» باطل وبـ على إن ملائماً كهبة على أن يعوضه يجوز وإن مخالفاً بطل الشرط وصحت الهبة ا هـ. كذا في حواشي مسكين .
The slave remains a trust with him. His statement (mentioned in al-Qunya etc.) – al-Nahr said: It is not hidden that the claimant here is only the rejection of the waiver, and it seems he considered it a discharge meaning his statement: (and it is problematic) – the answer is that this is from the chapter of suspending a gift on a suitable condition, not from the chapter of suspending discharge on a condition, as is apparent. He said in al-Bazzaziyya: Suspending a gift with the word 'if' is void, but with 'on condition that' it is valid if the condition is suitable, like a gift on condition that he gives something in return; but if it is unsuitable, the condition is void and the gift is valid. End quote. Thus in Hawashi Miskin.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This marginal note (hāshiya) addresses the earlier problematic statement that conditional ibra' is valid when the condition is not part of the gift. The commentator from al-Nahr clarifies that the issue is not about ibra' but about a conditional gift (hiba). The statement 'it is problematic' (mushkil) is resolved by reclassifying the transaction as a gift suspended on a suitable condition (shart mulā'im). According to al-Bazzaziyya, a gift suspended with the word 'if' is void, but if it is with 'on condition that' (bi-shart), it is valid if the condition is suitable (like a gift in exchange for compensation). If the condition is unsuitable, the condition fails but the gift remains valid. This distinction shows that the earlier ruling is not actually problematic when properly understood.

Key Terms
شرط ملائم (shart mulā'im): A condition that is suitable or compatible with the nature of the contract; here, for a gift, a condition of mutual exchange is suitable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the marginal note, what is the pivotal distinction that resolves the problematic ruling?
A) The difference between ibra' and hiba.
B) The difference between a suitable and unsuitable condition.
C) The difference between discharging a debt and transferring it.
D) The difference between a minor and an adult woman.

Key Takeaway
The proper classification of a conditional transaction as a gift rather than a discharge resolves the apparent problem, making the earlier fatwa sound.

The Effect of Terminal Illness on Waiver of Mahr
Ruling on waiver during death-illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a terminally ill woman's waiver of mahr and explain why it is invalid.

Core Idea
A dying woman's waiver of mahr is invalid — it would harm her heirs' rights.

The rights of heirs are protected in Hanafi fiqh. Even a wife cannot freely dispose of her mahr when terminally ill, because it becomes part of the estate. We examine the rule and its rationale from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The wife's waiver (ibrā') of the mahr while terminally ill (marad al-mawt).
Marad al-mawt is defined as an illness from which death is expected.
2
State the ruling
The waiver is invalid (lā yasiḥḥ).
3
Identify the reason
Because it affects the heirs' rights, similar to the rule for an heir's release of a debt.
The text says: 'as is known in the waiver of the heir'.
4
Note the scope
This only applies to death-illness, not minor illness.
If she recovers, the waiver may become valid? The text does not address that directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي كتاب وفي التجنيس : وهبت المهر لابنها الصغير وقبل الأب فالمختار أنها لا تصح لأنها هبة غير مقبوضة ا.هـ. وفيها قالت لزوجها إن كان يهمك المهر فقد أبرأتك يبرأ في الحال وليس بتعليق، ولو طلق امرأته ثلاثاً ولم تعلم به ثم قال لها إن لم تبرئيني من المهر فأنت طالق ثلاثاً فأبرأته وقبل يبرأ . وقال أبو حامد يبرأ قبل أو لم يقبل. ولو قالت الصداق الذي لي على زوجي ملك فلان بن فلان لا حق لي فيه وصدقها المقر له ثم أبرأت زوجها عنه يبرأ ولو قالت المهر الذي لي على زوجي لوالدي لا يصح إقرارها به ا هـ . النكاح منها : اختلفا في هبة المهر فقالت وهبته لك بشرط أن لا تطلقني وقال بغير شرط فالقول قولها اهـ. وذكر في الدعوى: لو أقاما البينة فبينة المرأة أولى، وقيل بيئة الزوج أولى، ولا بد في صحة حطها من أن لا تكون مريضة مرض الموت لما عرف في إبراء الوارث. وفي الخلاصة من المهر وهبت مهرها من الزوج وماتت ثم اختلفت ورثتها مع ازوج قالت الورثة كانت الهبة في مرض الموت وقال الزوج كانت في الصحة فالقول قول الزوج لأنه ينكر المهر ا هـ. وفي القنية من كتاب الهبة وهبت مهرها من زوجها في مرض موتها ومات زوجها قبلها فلا دعوى لها لصحة الإبراء ما لم تمت فإذا ماتت منه فلورثتها دعوى مهرها ا.هـ. وفيها أيضاً من باب البينتين المتضادتين : أقام الزوج بينة أنها أبرأته من الصداق حال صحتها وأقام الورثة بينة أنها أبرأته في مرض موتها فبينة الصحة أولى، وقيل بينة الوارث أولى اهـ. والراجح الأول وفيها أيضاً من الهبة أبرأه عن الدين ليصلح مهمه عند السلطان لا يبرأ وهو رشوة، ولو أبى الاضطجاع عند امرأته فقال لها أبرئيني من المهر فأضطجع معك فأبرأته قيل يبرأ لأن الإبراء للتودد الداعي في الجماع وقال عليه السلام تهادوا تحابوا بخلاف الإبراء في الأول لأنه مقصور على إصلاح المهم وإصلاح المهم مستحق عليه ديانة وبذل المال فيما هو مستحق عليه حد الرشوة ا هـ. وفيها من كتاب الدعوى امرأة ماتت فطلب زوجها من ورثتها براءته من المهر فأبوا فأعطى المهر ثم ظهر له بينة أن امرأته أبرأته في حال الصحة ولم يعلم الزوج بذلك فله أن بما أعطى من يرجع المهر ديانة فهذا يشير إلى أنه لا يرجع عليهم قضاء ا.هـ. وفيها من باب البينتين المتضادتين : أقامت المرأة بينة على المهر على أن زوجها كان مقراً بذلك إلى يومنا هذا وأقام الزوج البينة أنها أبرأته من هذا المهر الذي تدعي فبينة البراءة أولى، وكذا في الدين ا هـ . ويشترط في صحة إبرائها عن المهر علمها بمعناها لما في التجنيس : لو قال لها قولي وهبت مهري منك فقالت المرأة ذلك وهي لا تحسن العربية لا يصح، فرق بين وبين العتق والطلاق حيث يقعان والفرق أن الرضا شرط جواز الهبة وليس بشرط لجواز العتق والطلاق ا هـ . قوله : ( وفيها قالت لزوجها أي في القنية من كتاب المداينات أيضاً . وأشار
And in Kitab and al-Tajnis: She gifted the mahr to her young son and the father accepted – the chosen view is that it is not valid because it is a gift not taken into possession. End quote. And in it: She said to her husband: 'If the mahr matters to you, I have discharged you' – he is discharged immediately and it is not a suspension. And if he divorced his wife thrice and she did not know, then he said to her: 'If you do not discharge me from the mahr, you are thrice divorced' – she discharged him and he accepted – he is discharged. Abu Hamid said: He is discharged whether he accepted or not. And if she said: 'The dower that I have on my husband is the property of so-and-so, I have no right in it' and the assignee confirms her, then she discharges her husband from it, he is discharged. And if she said: 'The mahr that I have on my husband is for my father' – her acknowledgment is not valid. End quote. From al-Nikah: They differed regarding the gift of mahr; she said: 'I gifted it to you on condition that you do not divorce me' and he said: 'without condition' – the word is hers. End quote. And it is mentioned in al-Da'wa: If both bring evidence, the woman's evidence is given precedence; some said the husband's evidence is precedence. And for the validity of her waiver, she must not be terminally ill, as is known in the waiver of the heir. And in al-Khulasa on mahr: She gifted her mahr to her husband and then she died, then her heirs and the husband differed: the heirs said the gift was during death-illness, the husband said it was during health – the word is that of the husband because he denies the mahr. End quote. And in al-Qunya from Kitab al-Hiba: She gifted her mahr to her husband during her death-illness and her husband died before her – she has no claim because the discharge is valid as long as she does not die; if she died after him, her heirs have the claim for her mahr. End quote. And in it also from the chapter of contradictory evidence: The husband brought evidence that she discharged him from the dower during her health, and the heirs brought evidence that she discharged him during her death-illness – the evidence of health is given precedence; some said the heir's evidence is precedence. End quote. And the preponderant is the first. And in it also from al-Hiba: He discharged him from a debt to fix his affair with the sultan – he is not discharged, and it is bribery. And if he refused to lie with his wife and said to her: 'Discharge me from the mahr so that I may lie with you' – she discharged him; it is said he is discharged because the discharge is for affection that calls for intercourse, and the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Give gifts to one another, you will love one another' – unlike the first discharge because it is solely for fixing a matter, and fixing a matter is a religious duty on him, and spending wealth on what is a duty is bribery. End quote. And in it from Kitab al-Da'wa: A woman died; her husband asked her heirs for his discharge from the mahr, they refused, so he paid the mahr; then he found evidence that his wife had discharged him during her health and he did not know – he may take back what he gave (the mahr) as a matter of religion; this suggests he cannot claim it back judicially. End quote. And in it from the chapter of contradictory evidence: The woman brought evidence for the mahr that her husband had acknowledged it until today, and the husband brought evidence that she had discharged him from this mahr she claims – the evidence of discharge is given precedence; similarly with debt. End quote. And it is required for the validity of her discharge from the mahr that she knows its meaning, because in al-Tajnis: If he said to her 'Say: I have gifted my mahr to you' and she said that while not knowing Arabic, it is not valid. There is a distinction between this and manumission and divorce – they take effect because for them, knowledge is not a condition; the difference is that consent is a condition for the validity of gift (hiba) but not for manumission and divorce. End quote. His statement: 'And in it she said to her husband' – meaning in al-Qunya from Kitab al-Mudayanat also. And he indicated.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This lengthy passage from page 265 presents numerous specific rulings on waiver of mahr. It begins with a case from al-Tajnis: a woman gifting her mahr to her young son – it is invalid because the son (a minor) cannot take possession through his father's acceptance; the gift is not effectively delivered (ghayr maqbuda). Next, a woman says 'if the mahr matters to you, I have discharged you' – this is not a conditional suspension; it is an immediate discharge. Then a scenario where a husband threatens triple divorce if she does not discharge him; she does so and he accepts – he is discharged. Abu Hamid adds that he is discharged whether he accepts or not. Then cases of conflicting acknowledgments: if she says her mahr belongs to someone else and that person confirms, then she discharges her husband, it is valid; but if she says it belongs to her father, her acknowledgment is not valid (because it is a claim against herself without benefit). Then a dispute (ikhtilaf) over the gift of mahr: she claims it was conditional on no divorce, he says unconditional – her word is taken. Then the rule that for a valid waiver, she must not be terminally ill (marid marad al-mawt) because that would affect the rights of her heirs. If she dies and there is a dispute between heirs and husband over whether the gift was during health or death-illness, the husband's word is taken (as he denies owing the mahr). Similarly, if both bring evidence, the husband's evidence is given precedence if it shows discharge during health. But there is a difference of opinion; the preponderant (al-rajih) is the first (health evidence preferred). Also, a discharge given to effect a bribe (to fix a matter with the sultan) is invalid because it is bribery. In contrast, a discharge given so that the husband will lie with her is valid, because it is for mutual affection and supported by the hadith 'give gifts to one another'. Finally, it is a condition that the woman understands the meaning of what she says; if she does not know Arabic and utters the words without understanding, the discharge is invalid, unlike divorce and manumission which do not require understanding because they are effective by utterance alone. The passage ends with a marginal note referring back to earlier content.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): Terminal illness; a woman in death-illness cannot validly waive her mahr because it would prejudice her heirs' rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman waives her mahr while terminally ill, the waiver is:
A) Valid
B) Invalid because it harms heirs
C) Valid if husband accepts
D) Suspended until recovery

Key Takeaway
A woman's waiver of mahr is invalid if she is in death-illness, as it affects inheritance rights.

5 min
Knowledge of Meaning Required for Valid Discharge
Condition of knowing the meaning for valid waiver

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition that a woman must understand the meaning of her discharge statement for it to be valid.

Core Idea
A wife's discharge of mahr is invalid if she utters the words without understanding their meaning.

Unlike divorce and manumission, which take effect by utterance alone, a discharge (ibrā') requires the wife's consent and understanding. We explore why knowledge of the language is a condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
A woman says 'I have gifted my mahr to you' without knowing Arabic.
The husband instructed her to say it.
2
State the ruling
The gift (waiver) is not valid (la yasihh).
3
Identify the reason
Consent (riḍā) is a condition for the validity of hiba (gift), and true consent requires understanding.
In contrast, talaq and itq do not require understanding because they are effective by utterance alone.
4
Note the distinction
The difference is that hiba requires consent (riḍā), while talaq and itq do not; they are effective even if the person does not understand.
This is a key Hanafi usul point.

Source Text

Valid and Invalid Motives for Discharge of Mahr
Rulings on discharge: bribery vs affection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a valid discharge given for affection and an invalid discharge given for bribery.

Core Idea
A discharge given to bribe an official is invalid; a discharge to encourage marital intimacy is valid.

The motive behind a waiver matters. The Hanafi school examines the intent: a discharge for a noble purpose like marital love is valid, while one intended to achieve an improper end like bribery is void. We explore two contrasting cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Case 1: discharge to fix a matter with the sultan (bribery). Case 2: discharge so that husband will lie with his wife (affection).
2
State rulings
Case 1: the discharge is invalid (la yabra'u) and constitutes bribery (rashwa). Case 2: the discharge is valid (yabra'u) because it is for affection.
3
Identify the rationale
Bribery is haram; a contract based on it is void. In the second case, the Prophet ﷺ encouraged gift-giving to foster love.
Hadith: 'Tahadū taḥābbū'
4
Distinguish
The first is for an obligatory matter (fixing one's affair), which is already a duty; paying for a duty is bribery. The second is for a recommended act (intercourse) and the discharge is a gift to foster love.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ورثتها مع ازوج قالت الورثة كانت الهبة في مرض الموت وقال الزوج كانت في الصحة فالقول قول الزوج لأنه ينكر المهر ا هـ. وفي القنية من كتاب الهبة وهبت مهرها من زوجها في مرض موتها ومات زوجها قبلها فلا دعوى لها لصحة الإبراء ما لم تمت فإذا ماتت منه فلورثتها دعوى مهرها ا.هـ. وفيها أيضاً من باب البينتين المتضادتين : أقام الزوج بينة أنها أبرأته من الصداق حال صحتها وأقام الورثة بينة أنها أبرأته في مرض موتها فبينة الصحة أولى، وقيل بينة الوارث أولى اهـ. والراجح الأول وفيها أيضاً من الهبة أبرأه عن الدين ليصلح مهمه عند السلطان لا يبرأ وهو رشوة، ولو أبى الاضطجاع عند امرأته فقال لها أبرئيني من المهر فأضطجع معك فأبرأته قيل يبرأ لأن الإبراء للتودد الداعي في الجماع وقال عليه السلام تهادوا تحابوا بخلاف الإبراء في الأول لأنه مقصور على إصلاح المهم وإصلاح المهم مستحق عليه ديانة وبذل المال فيما هو مستحق عليه حد الرشوة ا هـ. وفيها من كتاب الدعوى امرأة ماتت فطلب زوجها من ورثتها براءته من المهر فأبوا فأعطى المهر ثم ظهر له بينة أن امرأته أبرأته في حال الصحة ولم يعلم الزوج بذلك فله أن بما أعطى من يرجع المهر ديانة فهذا يشير إلى أنه لا يرجع عليهم قضاء ا.هـ. وفيها من باب البينتين المتضادتين : أقامت المرأة بينة على المهر على أن زوجها كان مقراً بذلك إلى يومنا هذا وأقام الزوج البينة أنها أبرأته من هذا المهر الذي تدعي فبينة البراءة أولى، وكذا في الدين ا هـ . ويشترط في صحة إبرائها عن المهر علمها بمعناها لما في التجنيس : لو قال لها قولي وهبت مهري منك فقالت المرأة ذلك وهي لا تحسن العربية لا يصح، فرق بين وبين العتق والطلاق حيث يقعان والفرق أن الرضا شرط جواز الهبة وليس بشرط لجواز العتق والطلاق ا هـ . قوله : ( وفيها قالت لزوجها أي في القنية من كتاب المداينات أيضاً . وأشار
And in Kitab and al-Tajnis: She gifted the mahr to her young son and the father accepted – the chosen view is that it is not valid because it is a gift not taken into possession. End quote. And in it: She said to her husband: 'If the mahr matters to you, I have discharged you' – he is discharged immediately and it is not a suspension. And if he divorced his wife thrice and she did not know, then he said to her: 'If you do not discharge me from the mahr, you are thrice divorced' – she discharged him and he accepted – he is discharged. Abu Hamid said: He is discharged whether he accepted or not. And if she said: 'The dower that I have on my husband is the property of so-and-so, I have no right in it' and the assignee confirms her, then she discharges her husband from it, he is discharged. And if she said: 'The mahr that I have on my husband is for my father' – her acknowledgment is not valid. End quote. From al-Nikah: They differed regarding the gift of mahr; she said: 'I gifted it to you on condition that you do not divorce me' and he said: 'without condition' – the word is hers. End quote. And it is mentioned in al-Da'wa: If both bring evidence, the woman's evidence is given precedence; some said the husband's evidence is precedence. And for the validity of her waiver, she must not be terminally ill, as is known in the waiver of the heir. And in al-Khulasa on mahr: She gifted her mahr to her husband and then she died, then her heirs and the husband differed: the heirs said the gift was during death-illness, the husband said it was during health – the word is that of the husband because he denies the mahr. End quote. And in al-Qunya from Kitab al-Hiba: She gifted her mahr to her husband during her death-illness and her husband died before her – she has no claim because the discharge is valid as long as she does not die; if she died after him, her heirs have the claim for her mahr. End quote. And in it also from the chapter of contradictory evidence: The husband brought evidence that she discharged him from the dower during her health, and the heirs brought evidence that she discharged him during her death-illness – the evidence of health is given precedence; some said the heir's evidence is precedence. End quote. And the preponderant is the first. And in it also from al-Hiba: He discharged him from a debt to fix his affair with the sultan – he is not discharged, and it is bribery. And if he refused to lie with his wife and said to her: 'Discharge me from the mahr so that I may lie with you' – she discharged him; it is said he is discharged because the discharge is for affection that calls for intercourse, and the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Give gifts to one another, you will love one another' – unlike the first discharge because it is solely for fixing a matter, and fixing a matter is a religious duty on him, and spending wealth on what is a duty is bribery. End quote. And in it from Kitab al-Da'wa: A woman died; her husband asked her heirs for his discharge from the mahr, they refused, so he paid the mahr; then he found evidence that his wife had discharged him during her health and he did not know – he may take back what he gave (the mahr) as a matter of religion; this suggests he cannot claim it back judicially. End quote. And in it from the chapter of contradictory evidence: The woman brought evidence for the mahr that her husband had acknowledged it until today, and the husband brought evidence that she had discharged him from this mahr she claims – the evidence of discharge is given precedence; similarly with debt. End quote. And it is required for the validity of her discharge from the mahr that she knows its meaning, because in al-Tajnis: If he said to her 'Say: I have gifted my mahr to you' and she said that while not knowing Arabic, it is not valid. There is a distinction between this and manumission and divorce – they take effect because for them, knowledge is not a condition; the difference is that consent is a condition for the validity of gift (hiba) but not for manumission and divorce. End quote. His statement: 'And in it she said to her husband' – meaning in al-Qunya from Kitab al-Mudayanat also. And he indicated.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This lengthy passage from page 265 presents numerous specific rulings on waiver of mahr. It begins with a case from al-Tajnis: a woman gifting her mahr to her young son – it is invalid because the son (a minor) cannot take possession through his father's acceptance; the gift is not effectively delivered (ghayr maqbuda). Next, a woman says 'if the mahr matters to you, I have discharged you' – this is not a conditional suspension; it is an immediate discharge. Then a scenario where a husband threatens triple divorce if she does not discharge him; she does so and he accepts – he is discharged. Abu Hamid adds that he is discharged whether he accepts or not. Then cases of conflicting acknowledgments: if she says her mahr belongs to someone else and that person confirms, then she discharges her husband, it is valid; but if she says it belongs to her father, her acknowledgment is not valid (because it is a claim against herself without benefit). Then a dispute (ikhtilaf) over the gift of mahr: she claims it was conditional on no divorce, he says unconditional – her word is taken. Then the rule that for a valid waiver, she must not be terminally ill (marid marad al-mawt) because that would affect the rights of her heirs. If she dies and there is a dispute between heirs and husband over whether the gift was during health or death-illness, the husband's word is taken (as he denies owing the mahr). Similarly, if both bring evidence, the husband's evidence is given precedence if it shows discharge during health. But there is a difference of opinion; the preponderant (al-rajih) is the first (health evidence preferred). Also, a discharge given to effect a bribe (to fix a matter with the sultan) is invalid because it is bribery. In contrast, a discharge given so that the husband will lie with her is valid, because it is for mutual affection and supported by the hadith 'give gifts to one another'. Finally, it is a condition that the woman understands the meaning of what she says; if she does not know Arabic and utters the words without understanding, the discharge is invalid, unlike divorce and manumission which do not require understanding because they are effective by utterance alone. The passage ends with a marginal note referring back to earlier content.

Key Terms
رشوة (rashwa): Bribery; a discharge given to achieve an improper purpose (like influencing a sultan) is invalid and constitutes bribery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wife discharges her husband from the mahr so that he will not divorce her. Based on the lesson, what is the ruling?
A) Invalid, because it is a conditional discharge.
B) Invalid, because it is bribery.
C) Valid, because it is for affection and marital harmony.
D) Valid, but only if witnessed.

Key Takeaway
A discharge given for a haram or obligatory purpose is bribery and invalid; a discharge given for affection and love is valid.
